---
title: LargeFileBridge — Warnings (the yellow banner, the arrow button, and the educate-and-fix popup)
description: The cross-cutting source of truth for how LFBridge surfaces problems to a non-expert. Defines the yellow "Improvable" / red "Broken" banner that sits at the top of a page (headline + one plain-English sentence), the NEW blue-filled white right-arrow button on the right of that banner that opens a modal popup, and the popup's exact anatomy — an educational header and body (what it means, why it matters), zero-or-more apply/fix checkboxes, and a footer with a Cancel hyperlink on the left and a blue "Apply/Fix" button (white text + right chevron) on the bottom-right. Locks the reusable components (WarningBanner, WarningArrowButton, WarningPopup, and the warning registry) and the data model each warning is declared with (id, severity, where-shown, detection, popup content, fix action). Then catalogs EVERY warnable condition in the product — one section per warning — each with three mandated parts: (1) how to detect it and all conditions, (2) what the popup should do, (3) what the fix should do — with the exact source file, class, and method that implements each. This is the file the code follows for every warning surface.
---

# LargeFileBridge — Warnings

Every screen in LFBridge has to answer one question for a non-expert: **"Am I OK — and if not, what
is wrong and how do I fix it?"** ([use_cases.mdx](./use_cases.mdx) §0–§1). When the answer is *not*
"everything is fine," the screen shows a **warning**: a colored banner at the very top of the page
with a plain-English headline, one sentence of "what this means for you," and — new in this spec — a
**blue arrow button** that opens a **popup** which *educates* the user about the problem and gives
them the **button to fix it**.

This file owns the warning surface end to end so no per-page spec restates it:

1. The **warning model** and how it maps to the locked health model (§1).
2. The **banner** anatomy — the yellow/red rounded rectangle at the top of the page (§2).
3. The **blue arrow button** on the banner that opens the popup (§3).
4. The **popup** anatomy — educate + options + the fix button (§4).
5. The **lifecycle** — open → (choose options) → apply → progress → success/error → dismiss (§5).
6. **Accessibility & keyboard** (§6).
7. The **reusable components** to build and where they live (§7).
8. The **warning registry** — the data model each warning is declared with (§8).
9. **Multiple warnings on one page** — rollup, ordering, and the "N issues" affordance (§9).
10. The **catalog** — one section per warnable condition, each with the three mandated parts:
    **(A) how to detect it and all conditions**, **(B) what the popup should do**, **(C) what the fix
    should do** — with the exact code that implements each (§10+).

It builds on and does not repeat: [Use cases & health model](./use_cases.mdx),
[Tables](./tables.mdx), [Page actions](./page_actions.mdx), [Menus](./menus.mdx),
[One repo](./one_repo.mdx), [IPFS](./ipfs.mdx), [IPFS UI](./ipfs_ui.mdx), [Sync](./sync_process.mdx),
[Sync resilience](./sync_resilience.mdx), [Compression](./compression.mdx), [Scan](./scan.mdx),
[Security](./security.mdx), [Settings](./settings.mdx), [Devices](./devices.mdx),
[File system](./file_system.mdx).

---

## 1. The warning model (built on the LOCKED health model)

The app speaks in three states ([use_cases.mdx](./use_cases.mdx) §1, LOCKED). A **warning** is any
state that is **not Fixed**:

| Health state | The banner is… | Color token | Icon | Tone |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Fixed** (`ok`) | *no warning banner* (or a quiet green "all good" line) | `--lfb-ok` `#16a34a` / bg `--lfb-ok-bg` `#f0fdf4` | `CheckCircle2` | reassurance |
| **Improvable** (`warn`) | a **yellow** warning — an **offer, never an alarm** | `--lfb-warn` `#d97706` / bg `--lfb-warn-bg` `#fffbeb` | `AlertTriangle` | "this could be safer/smaller/cleaner" |
| **Broken** (`bad`) | a **red** error — files at risk or not moving | `--lfb-bad` `#dc2626` / bg `--lfb-bad-bg` `#fef2f2` | `AlertCircle` | "act now" |
| *(Neutral)* | slate, informational / nothing set up yet | `rgba(0,0,0,0.45)` / bg `#fff` | `Circle` | neutral |

The single source of these colors/icons is
`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/health.ts` — functions
`healthColor()`, `healthBg()`, `healthIcon()`, and the `worst()` rollup. **Warnings never invent their
own colors** — they read them from `health.ts`.

**The example that drives this spec.** On the One-Repo page today, when files exist that the user has
not decided to Sync or Ignore, a yellow banner reads:

> **6 files need a decision**
> Choose Sync or Ignore for them in the table below so LFBridge knows what to move.

That banner is produced in
`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` —
component `RepoStatusVerdict`, the `undecided > 0` branch. This spec generalizes that banner into a
**reusable warning surface with an arrow button and an educate-and-fix popup**, and then requires the
**same** surface for every other warnable condition (§10+).

> **Rule — every warning is a first-class, specified thing.** No warning ships as an ad-hoc string in
> a page. Every warning is declared in the **warning registry** (§8), rendered by the shared
> **WarningBanner** (§2), and (unless it is purely informational) opens a **WarningPopup** (§4) via the
> **arrow button** (§3). If a page needs a new warning, it adds a registry entry and a §10 catalog
> section here first.

---

## 2. The warning banner (the yellow/red rounded rectangle)

The banner is the first thing on the page body, directly under the `PageHeader` and the page action
row. It is the generalization of today's `StatusBanner`
(`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/StatusBanner.tsx`).

**Anatomy (left → right):**

```
┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  ⚠  6 files need a decision                                              [→]   │
│     Choose Sync or Ignore for them in the table below so LFBridge knows        │
│     what to move.                                                              │
└───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
   ▲   ▲                                                                     ▲
   │   │                                                                     │
 icon  headline (bold) + one-sentence sub (muted)                    blue arrow button (§3)
```

**Container.** `rounded-lg border px-4 py-3`, `mb-4`. Background = `healthBg(state)`; border color =
`healthColor(state)` for `warn`/`bad`, `--lfb-border` for `neutral`. A flex row: `flex items-start
gap-3`.

**Leading icon.** `healthIcon(state)` at `h-5 w-5`, colored `healthColor(state)`, `mt-0.5 shrink-0`.
Amber `AlertTriangle` for a warning, red `AlertCircle` for an error.

**Text column (`min-w-0 flex-1`).**
* **Headline** — `text-sm font-semibold text-black`. One line, plain English, includes the count where
  relevant ("6 files need a decision", singular/plural correct). No jargon.
* **Sub** — `mt-0.5 text-sm text-black/60`. Exactly one sentence: *what this means for you* and where
  to look / what to do. Never a paragraph — the paragraph lives in the popup.

**Trailing action area (`shrink-0`).** Right-aligned. Historically this held an optional `FixButton`
(e.g. "Sync now", "Open IPFS"). Under this spec the **default** trailing affordance is the **blue
arrow button** (§3) that opens the popup. A page MAY still show an inline `FixButton` *in addition* for
a one-click primary action that needs no explanation (e.g. "Sync now") — but the arrow-to-popup is the
standard, because the popup is where we **educate and offer the fix with its options**.

> **When there is no popup (informational only).** A purely neutral/informational banner (e.g.
> "Nothing set to sync in this repo yet") has **no arrow button** — there is nothing to open. Arrow
> button ⇔ there is a popup to educate and/or a fix to apply.

**Reference implementation to evolve:** `StatusBanner` + `FixButton` in
`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/StatusBanner.tsx`. This spec
extends `StatusBanner` with an optional `warning` prop (a registry entry, §8) that renders the arrow
button and wires the popup.

---

## 3. The blue arrow button (opens the popup)

New control. It lives on the **right** of the banner and is the affordance that says "there's more —
open it to understand and fix this."

**Look:**
* A **solid blue circle**, fill `--lfb-primary` `#2563eb`.
* A **white right-pointing arrow** centered inside (Lucide `ArrowRight`, `h-4 w-4`, `text-white`,
  `strokeWidth 2.5`).
* Size: `h-8 w-8` circle (`rounded-full`), `grid place-items-center`, `shrink-0`.
* Hover: darken ~8% (`hover:brightness-95`) + a subtle ring `ring-2 ring-[var(--lfb-primary-tint)]`.
* Focus-visible: `outline-2 outline-[var(--lfb-primary)] outline-offset-2`.
* Disabled (rare — e.g. the fix is mid-apply from elsewhere): `opacity-50 cursor-not-allowed`.

**Semantics:**
* `role="button"`, `aria-haspopup="dialog"`, `aria-label="Open details and fix: {warning headline}"`.
* Click / Enter / Space → open the WarningPopup (§4) for this warning.
* The arrow **always points right** regardless of state — it means "go forward into the fix."

**Why blue and not amber/red?** The banner already carries the severity color. The arrow is the
**action** affordance and uses the **brand action color** (blue) so "the thing you press to move
forward" is visually consistent everywhere in the app (same blue as `FixButton`'s non-broken state and
the page action links). Severity lives in the banner tint + icon; **action lives in blue**.

**Component:** `WarningArrowButton` (new), in
`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/WarningArrowButton.tsx`.

---

## 4. The warning popup (educate + options + the subjects list + fix)

Pressing the arrow opens a **modal** that follows the app's hand-rolled modal pattern (fixed overlay,
backdrop-click to cancel, inner `stopPropagation`, `Esc` to cancel), exactly like
`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/ConfirmDialog.tsx`. It is
NOT `window.confirm` and NOT a browser dialog.

### 4.0 Size & layout — one pane or two (LOCKED)

The popup has **two layouts**, chosen automatically by whether the warning names **specific subjects**
(files or directories — see §8 `targets`):

* **Single-pane** — for a warning with no specific subject list (e.g. "Start IPFS", "Serve only my
  content", "Install background sync"). The dialog is a **narrow column** (`w-[34rem]`, `max-w-full`):
  header → educate body → options → footer. This is the shape shipped today.
* **Two-pane** — for a warning that is **about a specific set of files or directories** (e.g. "6 files
  need a decision", "12 videos can be compressed", "9 big files aren't git-ignored"). The dialog grows
  **wide** and splits into a **left column** (educate + options) and a **right column: the subjects
  list** (§4.5) — the actual files/directories the warning is talking about, each with a **checkbox**.

**Width.** The two-pane popup may be **wide — up to 80% of the viewport width** (`width: 80vw`), capped
at a sane maximum (`max-w-[80rem]`), and **min `44rem`** so the two columns never crush. It is a fixed
overlay centered over the **whole screen**, so it **overlays the left nav bar** — it is not constrained
to the content area. Height is capped at `85vh`; the header and footer are pinned and only the two
column bodies scroll. On a **narrow viewport** (`< 44rem`, e.g. a phone) the two panes **stack**
vertically (educate on top, subjects list below) instead of sitting side by side.

**Anatomy — two-pane (the common, file-specific case):**

```
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  ⚠  6 files need a decision                                                          (×)  │  ← header
├──────────────────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  What this is                            │  Files this applies to        4 of 6 selected │  ← §4.5
│  LFBridge found 6 large files in this    │  [Select all]  [Clear]                        │     subjects
│  repo you haven't told it what to do     │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐  │     pane
│  with yet…                               │  │ ☑  renders/final_v3.mp4         1.4 GB   │  │     (right)
│                                          │  │ ☑  b-roll/city_night.mov        820 MB   │  │
│  Why it matters                          │  │ ☐  scratch/test_export.mp4      610 MB   │  │  ← unchecked
│  • Undecided files aren't backed up…     │  │ ☑  photos/hero_raw.tiff         240 MB   │  │     → excluded
│  • …and git may try to commit them.      │  │ ☐  scratch/old_take.mov         190 MB   │  │
│                                          │  │ ☑  photos/cover_master.png       96 MB   │  │
│  What do you want to do                  │  └─────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│  ◉ Sync  ○ Ignore                        │  Uncheck any file to leave it out.            │
├──────────────────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  Cancel                                                          Apply & sync — 4 files [→]│  ← footer
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

**Anatomy — single-pane (no specific subjects):**

```
┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  ⚠  The IPFS engine isn't running                     (×)  │  ← header
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  What this is / Why it matters …                           │  ← educate
│  ☐ Also keep IPFS on after I reboot                        │  ← options
├────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│  Cancel                                  Start IPFS   [→]   │  ← footer
└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4.1 Header
* Left: the state icon (`healthIcon(state)`, colored `healthColor(state)`) + the **title** (the same
  headline as the banner, `text-lg font-semibold`).
* Right: a small **close (×)** icon button (`aria-label="Close"`), which behaves exactly like Cancel.
* `role="dialog"`, `aria-modal="true"`, `aria-labelledby` the title.

### 4.2 Body — educate (mandatory)
Two short labeled blocks (`text-sm`, `text-black/70`), each a heading in `font-medium text-black` +
prose:
* **"What this is"** — one short paragraph explaining, in plain language, exactly what LFBridge found
  and what it means. No jargon; if a term is unavoidable (CID, peer, git-ignore) explain it in half a
  clause.
* **"Why it matters"** — 1–3 bullets on the consequence to *the user's files* (lost / not backed up /
  wasting space / at risk of being committed). This is the "so what."

Optionally a third block, **"Details"**, behind a `Disclosure` chevron
(`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/Disclosure.tsx`) for the
technical specifics (the exact file list, CIDs, sizes, the command we'd run). Hidden by default —
progressive disclosure ([use_cases.mdx](./use_cases.mdx) §2).

### 4.3 Options — the apply/fix choices (zero or more)
Between education and the footer, the popup renders the warning's **options** (from its registry entry,
§8):
* **Radios** for a mutually-exclusive decision (Sync all / Ignore all).
* **Checkboxes** for independent toggles ("Also remember this choice", "Compress in place vs. keep
  original", "Convert PNG → JPEG (loses transparency)").
* Each option has a **label** and an optional **one-line helper** (`text-xs text-black/50`).
* Options may show a **count** and be **scoped** (all N / just the selected rows).
* If a warning has **no options** (a pure one-click fix, e.g. "Start IPFS"), this region is empty and
  the footer button is the single action.
* If an option is **destructive or lossy** (PNG→JPEG drops alpha; "delete original after compress"),
  it is marked with a small amber/red note and, if checked, upgrades the footer button styling to the
  danger treatment and requires an explicit confirm (§5.4).

### 4.4 Footer — Cancel link (left) + blue Fix/Apply button (right)
`mt-5 flex items-center justify-between`.

* **Left: a Cancel hyperlink.** NOT a button — a text hyperlink styled like the page action links
  (`--lfb-primary`, no underline, underline on hover), reading **"Cancel"**. Clicking it (or `Esc`, or
  backdrop, or ×) closes the popup with no change.
* **Right: the primary action button.** `bg` = `--lfb-primary` `#2563eb` (or `--lfb-bad` when the
  chosen options are destructive/lossy — §5.4). White text (`text-white font-medium`),
  `rounded-md px-4 py-2 text-sm`. The label is **whatever is appropriate** to the warning and the
  chosen options — "Apply & sync", "Ignore these files", "Compress", "Start IPFS", "Fix gateway",
  "Install background sync", "Fix & apply". A **right chevron** (Lucide `ChevronRight`, `h-4 w-4`)
  sits at the **right side** of the button, after the label (`inline-flex items-center gap-1`).
  Disabled while no valid option is chosen or while applying (§5.2).

> **Locked footer grammar (every warning popup):** Cancel is a **hyperlink on the left**; the action is
> a **blue (or red-if-destructive) button on the right** with **white text + a right chevron**. The
> label changes per warning; the shape never does.

**Component:** `WarningPopup` (new), in
`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/WarningPopup.tsx`.

---

## 5. Lifecycle & states

### 5.1 Open
Arrow (§3) or a page action link opens the popup for a given warning `id`. The popup reads the
warning's registry entry (§8) for its education copy, options, and fix action, plus any **live payload**
(the actual file list / counts / CIDs) fetched or passed in.

### 5.2 Choose → Apply
* The action button is **disabled** until the chosen options form a valid, applyable request (e.g. a
  radio must be picked when the warning requires a choice).
* On click, it enters a **pending** state: button shows a spinner + present-tense label ("Applying…",
  "Starting IPFS…", "Compressing…"), is disabled, and the popup blocks further edits. Cancel stays
  available and, if pressed mid-apply, requests cancellation where the backend supports it (compression,
  scans) or is disabled where it cannot (a git-ignore write).

### 5.3 Success
* On success the popup either **closes** and the underlying page + banner **re-derive** their state
  (the warning disappears or downgrades because its detection condition is now false), OR, for
  long-running work (compress, big sync), it **hands off to the Progress dock**
  (`~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ProgressDock.tsx`) and closes.
* A brief success confirmation is acceptable inline before close ("Done — 6 files set to sync"). The
  banner must reflect the new truth on the next data refresh — **no stale warnings**.

### 5.4 Destructive / lossy confirm
If any chosen option is destructive or lossy (drops alpha, deletes an original, rewrites a file in
place, changes many files), the action button uses the **red** `--lfb-bad` treatment and the
click first shows a compact inline confirm inside the popup (or reuses `ConfirmDialog`) — never a
silent destructive apply. This mirrors the charter rule: **never compress or alter a file unless the
user explicitly asks**, and warn before losing data (alpha channel, etc.).

### 5.5 Error
If the fix fails, the popup **stays open**, keeps the chosen options, and shows a red inline error line
(`text-sm text-[var(--lfb-bad)]`) with the plain-English reason + a "Try again" affordance (the action
button re-enables). The durable fault is written to the app error log
(`~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err`).

### 5.6 Dismiss / snooze
* **Cancel / Esc / backdrop / ×** — closes, no change; the warning remains (it's still true).
* Some warnings support **"Don't offer this again for this file/repo"** (an *offer* dismissal, only for
  Improvable offers, never for Broken alarms). When present it is a checkbox in the options region, and
  it persists per-user, per-scope in `users/<email>/config.yaml`
  ([tables.mdx](./tables.mdx) §4 persistence pattern). A Broken (`bad`) warning can **never** be
  permanently dismissed — only fixed.

---

## 6. Accessibility & keyboard

* The arrow button is reachable by keyboard (`Tab`), activates on `Enter`/`Space`, has an `aria-label`
  naming the warning.
* On open, focus moves into the dialog; **initial focus is the first interactive option** (or the
  action button if there are none) — but for a **destructive default**, focus the **Cancel** link
  (mirrors `ConfirmDialog` focusing Cancel so a stray Enter never fires a destructive action).
* `Esc` closes (= Cancel). Focus is **trapped** within the dialog while open and **restored** to the
  arrow button on close.
* The overlay uses `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`; the title is the accessible name.
* Color is never the only signal — every state also carries an icon and text. Contrast meets AA on the
  amber/red tints (dark ink on light tint).

---

## 7. Reusable components (what to build, where)

All under `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/`:

| Component | File | Role |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `health.ts` *(exists)* | `ui/health.ts` | color/icon/rollup source of truth — unchanged |
| `StatusBanner` *(extend)* | `ui/StatusBanner.tsx` | add an optional `warning` prop → renders `WarningArrowButton` + wires `WarningPopup` |
| `WarningArrowButton` *(new)* | `ui/WarningArrowButton.tsx` | the blue circle + white right-arrow (§3) |
| `WarningPopup` *(new)* | `ui/WarningPopup.tsx` | the modal: header + educate body + options + footer (§4) |
| `warningRegistry` *(new)* | `ui/warnings/registry.ts` | the typed registry + `useWarnings(scope)` hook (§8) |
| per-warning defs *(new)* | `ui/warnings/defs/*.ts` | one file per warning: detection selector, copy, options, fix thunk |

**Backend fix endpoints** live in their existing owning modules (repos, ipfs, compress, git, fs, …) —
the popup's "fix" calls the module that owns the action; §10 names each. No new backend "warnings"
module is required for the actions; a small read-model that rolls up "what warnings are live for this
scope" MAY live in `backend/src/modules/health` if we want a single endpoint (§9).

---

## 8. The warning registry (data model)

Every warning is one typed record. Adding a warning = adding a record + a §10 catalog section.

```ts
type WarningDef = {
  id: string;                    // stable kebab id, e.g. "files-need-decision"
  severity: (ctx) => Health;     // "warn" | "bad" | "neutral" — from live data, uses health.ts
  scope: "file" | "directory" | "repo" | "ipfs" | "device" | "storage" | "computer" | "global";
  // BANNER (§2)
  headline: (ctx) => string;     // count-correct, plural-correct, plain English
  sub: (ctx) => string;          // one sentence
  // POPUP (§4)
  popup?: {
    whatThisIs: (ctx) => ReactNode;   // "What this is" education
    whyItMatters: (ctx) => ReactNode; // "Why it matters" bullets
    details?: (ctx) => ReactNode;     // optional Disclosure content
    options?: OptionSpec[];           // radios/checkboxes (§4.3); [] = one-click fix
    actionLabel: (ctx, opts) => string; // footer button label, e.g. "Apply & sync"
    destructive?: (opts) => boolean;    // true → red button + confirm (§5.4)
    dismissible?: boolean;              // Improvable offers only; false for bad
    apply: (ctx, opts) => Promise<void>;// THE FIX — calls the owning backend module
  };
};
```

* **`ctx`** is the live payload for the scope (the repo detail, the ipfs status, the file list, the
  counts) — the same data the page already loads.
* A warning **without** a `popup` is informational — banner only, **no arrow button**.
* `severity`, `headline`, `sub` are derived from `ctx` so the banner and popup can never disagree with
  the data.

**Rollup.** A page collects the live warnings for its scope, sorts by `worst()` severity then a fixed
priority, and shows the **top** one in the banner (§9). `health.ts::worst()` is the rollup rule.

---

## 9. Multiple warnings on one page

A page/scope can have several live warnings at once (a repo can be *both* IPFS-down *and* have
undecided files). Rules:

* The banner shows the **single most severe** warning (`bad` > `warn` > neutral; ties broken by a fixed
  per-scope priority order listed in each §10 section). Broken always wins the banner.
* When **more than one** warning is live, the banner appends a quiet **"+N more"** affordance next to
  the arrow (a small `text-xs` pill). Its arrow opens a **popup list**: each live warning as a row
  (icon + headline + its own arrow), and selecting one opens that warning's popup. This keeps the
  top-of-page to a single banner while still exposing everything.
* At the **directory / repo / computer rollup** level, the charter's **category rollup table** (charter
  "Category rollup table"; [scan.mdx](./scan.mdx), [file_system.mdx](./file_system.mdx)) is the *table*
  form of the same warnings: each row is a warning category with a count and a per-row action that
  opens the **same** WarningPopup. The banner is the "worst thing here"; the rollup table is "all the
  things here." They share the registry (§8) so a fix from either surface clears both.

---

## 10. The catalog — every warnable condition

Each subsection below is one warning. Every one documents the three mandated parts:

* **(A) Detection & conditions** — the exact fields, thresholds, and boolean logic that make it fire,
  with the source file + class/function + line range that computes it (frontend and backend).
* **(B) Popup** — what the educate body says, the options/checkboxes, and the action-button label.
* **(C) Fix** — what pressing the button concretely does (the backend action/endpoint and its side
  effects), or, if there is no safe auto-fix, the manual next step it routes the user to.

> The sections below are populated from a full code scan. They are ordered by scope (repo → IPFS →
> devices/sync → files/directories → file-system rollup → compression → storages → scanner/jobs →
> git/resilience → settings/security) and, within a scope, Broken before Improvable.

<!-- CATALOG-START -->

## 10.1 IPFS engine, install, config-health & only-our-content compliance

IPFS (Kubo) is the local peer-to-peer engine that actually moves large git-ignored files between the user's own computers — nothing here is a cloud service and, per the charter, nothing is ever a public gateway or relay. This category owns every condition of that engine: whether it is installed, running, correctly configured, up to date, and staying inside the **only-our-content** security policy. It also owns the **canonical "IPFS is down / unreachable" verdict** (§10.1.2); the repo page ([one_repo.mdx](./one_repo.mdx) `repo-ipfs-down`), the Scans page (`sync-on-but-ipfs-down` / `ipfs-down-while-sync-on`), the Settings row, and the MediaViewer button all read the same `ipfs.health()` signal and cross-reference this section rather than re-documenting it. Detection splits cleanly: a cheap **liveness** endpoint drives the app-wide banner ladder (installed → running → configBlocker), while the fuller `/api/ipfs` and `/api/ipfs/node` payloads drive the on-page verdicts, compliance posture, and upgrade cards. Within this category, Broken (engine down / files at risk / security violation) is ordered before Improvable (offers) before neutral.

#### 10.1.1 IPFS isn't installed on this computer — `bad` (id: ipfs-not-installed)

*Where shown:* App-wide `IpfsStatusBanner` (mounted in AppShell) on every page **except** `/ipfs*` — amber strip, "Install IPFS" link → `/ipfs/off`. The full surface is the `/ipfs/off` **InstallCard**. Also rendered as the `ipfs` row on the **Tools** page (`required-tool-ipfs-missing`, "✗ missing", plus an "Install all required" bar).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `liveness.installed === false`, where `installed = hasBinary("ipfs")` (`ipfs` resolvable on PATH via `command -v`/`where`) **OR** the daemon answers an RPC `id`. So false means **no CLI binary AND no running daemon**. This is the first rung of the app-wide A/B/C scenario ladder (first-true wins; label becomes "Install IPFS"); liveness polls every 20 s. A sub-fork governs whether an auto-fix is even possible: `packageManagerPresent === false` (or `installPlan(platform).bin === null` on Linux/other, where we never run `sudo`/`snap` non-interactively) means **no auto-install** — the InstallCard shows a red "(not found)" and only a copyable command. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` — `liveness()` (lines 216–234, `installed` at 219 via `hasBinary()` lines 42–50) and `installPlan()` (lines 59–88, `bin=null` on linux/other); frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/IpfsStatusBanner.tsx` — `IpfsStatusBanner()` query lines 34–38 + scenario-A branch lines 63–82, and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/ipfs/IpfsOffPage.tsx` — `InstallCard` (lines 217–251, `auto = installMethod && packageManagerPresent` at 218).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* IPFS is the **local** engine LFBridge uses to move big files between your own computers — it is not a cloud service and it makes nothing public; until it is installed, no large file can sync or back up. *Why it matters:* every large git-ignored file is stranded on this one machine — none of it is backed up to your other computers, so if this machine is lost the files are gone. *Options:* none — a one-click install where a package manager exists; where none exists, no options, just a copyable command. *Action button:* "Install IPFS" (only when a package manager is present); otherwise the card shows the copyable `node.installCommand` with the note "Automatic install isn't available here — run this in a terminal."

**(C) The fix.** "Install IPFS" POSTs `/api/ipfs/install`, a single-flight re-attachable job: detect platform → run `brew install ipfs` / `winget install --id IPFS.Kubo -e` → `ipfs init` → spawn the detached daemon → `enforceCompliance()`. Progress polls `GET /api/ipfs/install/status`; on success the page auto-redirects to the running dashboard. When `packageManagerPresent === false` there is **no safe auto-fix** — the manual next step is the copyable `installCommand` run in a terminal, then reopen the page. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /install` (lines 39–41) → `ipfs-node.service.ts` `startInstall()` (lines 428–478); frontend `IpfsOffPage.tsx` `InstallCard` `onInstall` (line 235) and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` `startInstall()` (lines 64–68).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-not-installed-appwide`, `ipfs-not-installed`, `ipfs-not-installed-offpage-no-pkgmgr`, the `required-tool-ipfs-missing` Tools-row surface, and the `ipfs-autoinstall-unavailable` no-package-manager fork (all the same real-world condition + fix endpoint). The app-wide banner is a `Link`, not a popup — a deliberate cheap-liveness nudge that never reads the pinset; it is suppressed on `/ipfs*` paths. The code uses **amber** (warn tint) here even though this is semantically Broken — one amber "can't sync" banner covers scenarios A and B; on-page verdicts (§10.1.2) render the same family **red**, a known color disagreement between surfaces.

#### 10.1.2 IPFS is installed but not running / the engine is unreachable — `bad` (id: ipfs-not-running)

*Where shown:* **This is the canonical "IPFS is down" verdict for the whole app.** App-wide `IpfsStatusBanner` (amber "Start IPFS" → `/ipfs/off`); the `/ipfs/pins` **NodeVerdict** red `StatusBanner`; the `/ipfs` dashboard worst-first verdict; the **Settings** IPFS row ("Unreachable"); and the **MediaViewer** (Add/Remove-IPFS button disabled). Other categories cross-reference here: [one_repo.mdx](./one_repo.mdx) `repo-ipfs-down`, the Scans banner `sync-on-but-ipfs-down` / `ipfs-down-while-sync-on`, and the entity/MediaViewer `ipfs-node-unreachable`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Two equivalent framings of the same fact — the daemon isn't answering its RPC. **Liveness:** `installed === true` AND `running === false` AND `configBlocker === false` (label "Start IPFS"); `running = ipfs.health() === "ok"` (an RPC `id` succeeds). If `configBlocker` is also true a different message fires → §10.1.3. **Full payload:** `node.health === "unreachable"` (RPC `id` fails) forces `running=false`, `compliant=false`, and drops all metrics/posture to app-config intent. `nodeDown` disables Rescan / Import / pin-toggles and swaps the pinset table for a red DiagnosticCard. A distinct sub-cause: the daemon may actually be up but bound to a non-default port — then `ipfs.api_addr` (which drives `apiBase()`) is wrong. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` — `liveness()` (lines 216–234, `running` 217, `configBlocker` 232) and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.service.ts` — `health()` (lines 39–48), `apiBase()` (lines 12–18); frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/ipfs/IpfsPage.tsx` — `nodeDown` (line 86), `NodeVerdict()` (lines 388–397), and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/IpfsStatusBanner.tsx` (lines 63–82).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the daemon is installed but stopped (or crashed, or reachable only on a wrong API address), so pins can't be read, added, or fetched and transfers between your computers are paused — but your Sync/Ignore decisions and metadata are still saved to config. *Why it matters:* no bytes move in either direction; a file that lives only on another machine can't arrive here, and a file only here can't reach the others. Nothing is lost — this is a paused pipe, not a broken file. *Options:* a checkbox "Also keep IPFS on after I reboot" (installs the auto-start LaunchAgent alongside starting — see §10.1.11). *Action button:* "Start IPFS".

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/daemon {action:"start"}` → `controlDaemon("start")`: a watchable job that runs `ensureInit` → `startDaemon` (detached `ipfs daemon --enable-gc`, waits up to 30 s for health) → `enforceCompliance`. Passing `{autostart:true}` also installs the reboot LaunchAgent; `{migrate:true}` covers a repo-migration failure (§10.1.5). If start fails, `diagnoseStartFailure()` names the real cause (deprecated config / migrate / port / lock) instead of a fake timeout, routing to §10.1.3–§10.1.7. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /daemon` (lines 51–69) → `ipfs-node.service.ts` `controlDaemon()` (lines 485–558), `startDaemon()` (lines 369–425); frontend `IpfsOffPage.tsx` `StoppedCard` (lines 128–214).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-not-running-appwide`, `ipfs-not-running`, `ipfs-node-unreachable-verdict`, `ipfs-node-unreachable-page`, and the Settings/entity `ipfs-node-unreachable` renderings. **Gap:** the `/ipfs/pins` NodeVerdict red banner has **no wired Fix button** (lines 388–397 pass no `action` prop) — it relies on the DiagnosticCard below (copyable `ipfs daemon` / `brew install ipfs`) and on the app-wide banner routing to `/ipfs/off`; the compliance verdict on the *same* component (§10.1.8) does have a Fix, so this is an inconsistency worth closing. **Gap:** the MediaViewer only greys the IPFS button with a tooltip — no page-level banner. Note two different endpoints/types back this (`api.ipfs` → `IpfsNodeCard` on `/ipfs/pins` vs `api.ipfsNode` → `IpfsNodeStatus` on the dashboard); `api_addr` misconfiguration is a distinct sub-cause the popup should distinguish from a plain "off."

#### 10.1.3 IPFS can't start — its configuration needs a fix (Kubo 0.42 Reprovider crash) — `bad` (id: ipfs-config-blocker-reprovider)

*Where shown:* App-wide `IpfsStatusBanner` (button becomes **"Fix IPFS"** → `/ipfs/off`); the `/ipfs/off` **ConfigHealthCard** rendered as a **full-page blocker takeover**; and the `/ipfs` dashboard ConfigHealthCard.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `configBlocker === true`: the node is NOT running AND `configHealth.hasBlocker` is true with a blocker-severity issue whose `class !== "missing"`. The headline case is `deprecated-reprovider`: the parsed `~/.ipfs/config` has a top-level `Reprovider` key **AND** (`cliVersion() >= 0.42.0` OR the version is unreadable). Kubo 0.42 removed the `Reprovider` block, so the daemon **FATAL-s on startup** ("Deprecated configuration detected. Manually migrate Reprovider…") — which previously looked like a start *timeout*. The same key on Kubo < 0.42 is only `info` severity (works now, breaks after upgrade), **not** a blocker. `class === "missing"` is deliberately excluded (turning IPFS on runs `ipfs init`, so it flows through the normal start — see §10.1.16). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `configHealth()` (lines 141–173, `REPROVIDER_REMOVED_IN='0.42.0'` line 27, `versionGte`), `hasBlocker` (line 194), `diagnoseStartFailure()` cause `deprecated_config` (lines 216–224); frontend `IpfsOffPage.tsx` `configBlocker()` (lines 24–26, excludes class "missing") and `IpfsStatusBanner.tsx` (lines 64–69).

**(B) The popup.** The ConfigHealthCard **is** the educational surface. *What this is:* Kubo 0.42 removed the old `Reprovider` config block, so the daemon exits immediately on start until it is migrated to `Provide`; LFBridge will migrate the key for you. *Why it matters:* IPFS literally cannot start — no file can sync — until this one config key is fixed. *Options:* a "What we'll change" bullet list of each plain-language migration step, shown **before** you commit, plus an "Or do it yourself" disclosure with copyable manual commands. It states a timestamped backup (`config.bak.<unixtime>`) is written first and that your node identity/PeerID does **not** change. *Action button:* "Review & Fix Configuration".

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/config-repair {issueIds:['deprecated-reprovider']}` → `repairConfig()`: an in-process JSON edit (no daemon needed) — back up config → set `Provide.Strategy` from `Reprovider.Strategy` (default `pinned`) → move `Reprovider.Interval` → `Provide.DHT.Interval` → **delete** the `Reprovider` block → write. If the blocker then clears, the off-page auto-starts the daemon (`repair.onSuccess`). **Critical (charter/MEMORY):** the fix writes the modern `Provide.Strategy` and must **never re-add `Reprovider`** — doing so re-arms the crash. Non-fixable issues fall back to the `manualSteps` escape hatch. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /config-repair` (lines 84–108) → `ipfs-config-health.service.ts` `repairConfig()` (lines 283–376, Reprovider→Provide migration lines 340–362); frontend `IpfsOffPage.tsx` `repair.onSuccess` (lines 62–72) and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/ipfs/ipfsShared.tsx` `ConfigHealthCard` `onFix` (line 323).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-config-blocker-appwide`, `ipfs-config-blocker-offpage-takeover`, and `ipfs-config-blocker-reprovider`. This is the exact incident from MEMORY (IPFS Reprovider crash): `enforceCompliance` (§10.1.8) is also coded to write `Provide.Strategy` and only fall back to `Reprovider.Strategy` on builds lacking `Provide`, so neither path ever re-creates the crash. Only issues with `fixable === true` get an auto-fix button; the app-wide banner is the alarm, the ConfigHealthCard is the guided-repair takeover.

#### 10.1.4 IPFS config file is unreadable (corrupt) — `bad` (id: ipfs-config-unreadable)

*Where shown:* `/ipfs/off` and `/ipfs` dashboard **ConfigHealthCard** (blocker, with a Fix button).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The config file at `$IPFS_PATH/config` (default `~/.ipfs/config`) **exists** but `JSON.parse` throws → issue `id:'unreadable'`, `class:'unreadable'`, `severity:'blocker'`, `hasBlocker=true`. IPFS can't read its own config, so it won't start; because `class !== 'missing'`, `IpfsOffPage.configBlocker()` is true and the Fix card shows. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `configHealth()` JSON.parse catch branch (lines 114–137).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* your IPFS config exists but is no longer valid JSON, so the engine can't start; the fix backs up the broken file to `config.bak.<timestamp>` and recreates a fresh configuration. *Why it matters:* **the one destructive config-repair path** — recreating the config gives this computer a **new node identity (PeerID)**, so your other computers will see this machine as a brand-new peer. *Options:* the "What we'll change" list plus manual steps; because of the PeerID side effect this should carry a prominent amber/red note. *Action button:* "Review & Fix Configuration" — treat as **destructive** (red + explicit confirm per §5.4) since it changes identity.

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/config-repair {issueIds:['unreadable']}` → `repairConfig()`: back up → remove the corrupt config → return `needsInit=true`; the UI then starts the daemon, which runs `ipfs init`, generating a new repo/PeerID. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `repairConfig()` unreadable branch (lines 315–335).

**Notes / gaps.** The new-PeerID consequence must be surfaced prominently — it is the only config-repair that changes identity, unlike the Reprovider migration (§10.1.3) which explicitly preserves it.

#### 10.1.5 IPFS repository needs a one-time migration — `bad` (id: ipfs-repo-needs-migration)

*Where shown:* `/ipfs/off` start-failure state — the start job's diagnosis surfaces in the progress log with a copyable command.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `startDaemon` fails to become healthy within 30 s; `diagnoseStartFailure()` reads the daemon's own log tail and matches `/ipfs daemon --migrate/`, `/run migrations/`, or `/Please run.*migrat/` → cause `needs_migrate`, `isConfigBlocker=true`. The on-disk repo format is older than the installed Kubo binary. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `diagnoseStartFailure()` (lines 225–233), invoked from `ipfs-node.service.ts` `startDaemon()` (line 419).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* IPFS was upgraded and the on-disk repository is an older format than the new binary; a safe one-time migration updates it. *Why it matters:* until the migration runs, the daemon won't start and nothing syncs — but there is **no data loss**, it just needs to run once. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Start & migrate IPFS".

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/daemon {action:'start', migrate:true}` → `controlDaemon('start',{migrate:true})` → `startDaemon({migrate:true})`, which spawns `ipfs daemon --enable-gc --migrate`. This is the wired auto-fix. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` — `startDaemon()` args (line 398), `controlDaemon()` migrate option (lines 487/524); router `POST /daemon` migrate (lines 51–63).

**Notes / gaps.** The repo page's `repo-ipfs-down` fix passes `migrate:true`, so starting from there also clears this. Distinct from the Reprovider crash (§10.1.3): a `--migrate` alone won't fix a bad config key.

#### 10.1.6 IPFS won't start — a port is already in use — `bad` (id: ipfs-port-busy)

*Where shown:* `/ipfs/off` start-failure state; the job progress log.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Daemon didn't answer in 30 s; `diagnoseStartFailure()` matches `/address already in use/`, `/bind: address/`, or `/could not bind/` → cause `port_busy`, `isConfigBlocker=false`. Usually another `ipfs daemon` is already running (API `:5001` / swarm `:4001`). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `diagnoseStartFailure()` (lines 234–243).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* something already holds the port IPFS needs — most likely an IPFS daemon that was started outside the app, in which case the node may already be usable and a refresh will pick it up. *Why it matters:* this instance can't bind, so the app thinks IPFS is down even though a working daemon may be running. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Re-check IPFS" (re-probes `GET /api/ipfs/liveness`).

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix** — we must never kill an unknown process holding the port. Manual next step: stop the other `ipfs daemon`, or change the API/swarm ports in `~/.ipfs/config`, then retry Start; the app should re-probe health in case a node is already up. *Fix in:* no auto-fix — the copyable `manualCommand` (`ipfs daemon --enable-gc`) is the only surfaced remedy; detection at `ipfs-config-health.service.ts` `diagnoseStartFailure()` (lines 234–243).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** no dedicated banner — only surfaces as a failed start job. A distinct "already running elsewhere?" hint that re-checks health would be a better UX than the raw manual command.

#### 10.1.7 IPFS won't start — the repo lock is held — `bad` (id: ipfs-repo-lock-held)

*Where shown:* `/ipfs/off` start-failure state; the job progress log.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Start failed; `diagnoseStartFailure()` matches `/someone else has the lock/`, `/repo\.lock/`, or `/lock.*held/` → cause `lock_held`, `isConfigBlocker=false`. Either a live daemon holds `~/.ipfs/repo.lock` or a stale lock remains from a crash. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `diagnoseStartFailure()` (lines 244–252).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* IPFS keeps a lock file so only one daemon runs at a time; if IPFS is already running you can just use it, but if it crashed a **stale** lock is left behind and blocks restart. *Why it matters:* deleting `repo.lock` is safe **only** when no daemon is actually running — removing it while one runs risks repo corruption. *Options:* none by default; a guarded "remove stale lock and retry" is only offered after a health re-check confirms the node is unreachable. *Action button:* "Re-check IPFS" (then, if unreachable, "Remove stale lock & start" — destructive-guarded).

**(C) The fix.** **No unconditional auto-fix.** Safe path: re-check health; if unreachable, offer a guarded action that deletes `~/.ipfs/repo.lock` then POSTs `/daemon start`. Today only the manual command is provided. *Fix in:* no wired endpoint — the guarded stale-lock removal is a gap; only the `manualCommand` string (`rm -f ~/.ipfs/repo.lock && ipfs daemon --enable-gc`) exists; detection at `ipfs-config-health.service.ts` (lines 244–252).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** the guarded stale-lock removal is not implemented as an endpoint. Never delete the lock without first proving no daemon is live.

#### 10.1.8 This computer is set to serve other people's content — `bad` (id: ipfs-noncompliant-serving-others-content)

*Where shown:* `/ipfs/pins` **NodeVerdict** red `StatusBanner` (with a Fix button); the `/ipfs` dashboard **SecurityCard** (red footer + per-key posture pills) and **Gateway panel** ("public ✗"); the Settings IPFS row ("Needs a fix", rendered as self-healing warn there).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `node.compliant === false` **AND** `node.publicGateway === false` (drift, **not** a deliberate opt-out). `compliant = running && reprovideStrategy ∈ {pinned, roots} && gatewayLocalOnly`. So this fires on either of two legs, without the user having flipped the public-gateway setting: **(1) reprovide leg** — `reprovideStrategy` is neither `pinned` nor `roots` (i.e. `all`, or empty which defaults to `all`); strategy is read from the live config, modern `Provide.Strategy` first, falling back to deprecated `Reprovider.Strategy`. **(2) gateway leg** — `Addresses.Gateway` has ≥1 non-loopback multiaddr (not matching `/ip4/127.0.0.1/` or `/ip6/::1/`); no gateway at all counts as local-only (safest), a loopback-only gateway is fine. GC-off folds into posture but isn't itself a compliance failure. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.service.ts` — `nodePosture()` `gatewayLocalOnly` (lines 329–333), `gatewaySummary()`/`LOOPBACK` regex (lines 287–318), `readReprovideStrategy` (lines 374–378), `isCompliant` (lines 381–391); assembled `compliant` in `ipfs-node.service.ts` `nodeStatus()` (lines 148–152) and `ipfs-page.service.ts` `computeIpfsPage` (lines 163–165); frontend `IpfsPage.tsx` `NodeVerdict` (lines 398–425) and `ipfsShared.tsx` `SecurityCard` (lines 219–252).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the charter's headline security rule — this machine must announce, pin, and serve **only your own files** and never become a public IPFS gateway or relay that bounces or caches other people's content. There are three levers: reprovide strategy must not be `all`, the HTTP gateway must bind loopback-only, and GC keeps any incidental third-party cache transient. *Why it matters:* a wrong setting lets strangers route requests through your machine and makes it cache/serve content that isn't yours — a bandwidth, privacy, and abuse-exposure risk. *Options:* none — a single one-click restore. *Action button:* "Serve only my content" (ShieldCheck).

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/enforce` → `enforceCompliance()`: sets `Provide.Strategy` to the configured `reprovide_strategy` (default `pinned`) via RPC `config set`, and if any `Addresses.Gateway` is non-loopback rebinds it to the configured loopback default (only rewriting when a public bind is actually present, so a custom loopback PORT is preserved), and ensures GC is on. **Critical (charter/MEMORY):** it writes the modern `Provide.Strategy` and **never** re-adds the deprecated `Reprovider` key (Kubo 0.42 FATAL). Config `set` is live — no daemon restart needed. Toast: "Restored only-our-content defaults." *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /enforce` (lines 193–202) → `ipfs.service.ts` `enforceCompliance()` (lines 394–451, reprovide set, gateway rebind lines 432–447).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-noncompliant-serving-others-content`, `ipfs-noncompliant-reprovide-all`, `ipfs-noncompliant-public-gateway`, and `ipfs-gateway-public-dashboard-panel` (all the same `node.compliant=false` rollup, two legs, one fix). The Gateway panel itself is a read-only status; the actionable Fix lives on the SecurityCard/NodeVerdict. Two renderings driven by the same booleans across two endpoints (`IpfsNodeCard.compliant` on `/ipfs/pins` vs `IpfsNodeStatus.compliant` on the dashboard). `enforceCompliance` early-returns (warn-log only) when the machine opted out via `ipfs.public_gateway=true` → that acknowledged state is §10.1.12. This is the charter's "always look for cases where we are out of compliance and flag/fix them."

#### 10.1.9 An IPFS job failed (install / start / stop / upgrade) — `bad` (id: ipfs-job-failed)

*Where shown:* the `/ipfs/off` **ErrorPanel** and the `/ipfs` install/start/stop/upgrade **progress view** (`job.status === 'error'`), polled via `GET /api/ipfs/install/status`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The single-flight job (`install | start | stop | upgrade`) ended with `status='error'`; `fail()` sets `job.error` + a copyable `job.manualCommand` and logs a warn. Covers: no auto-installer on the platform, package manager missing, install finished but `ipfs` not on PATH, `ipfs init` failed, a diagnosed daemon-start failure, a stop that didn't complete, or an upgrade exit code ≠ 0. A **config-crash diagnosis is deliberately re-routed** to the ConfigHealthCard (§10.1.3) — that takeover wins over the ErrorPanel — so this panel is the fallback for **non-config** failures. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` — `fail()` (lines 278–286) with failure sites `startInstall` (435–474), `controlDaemon` (495–555), `startUpgrade` (573–614); exposed `GET /install/status` (`ipfs.router.ts` lines 44–46); frontend `IpfsOffPage.tsx` `jobErrored` (line 44), ErrorPanel branch (lines 107–112), `ipfsShared.tsx` `ErrorPanel` (lines 149–170).

**(B) The popup.** The ErrorPanel **is** the surface. *What this is:* which step failed (install vs start vs stop vs upgrade), shown via `job.error`, with the terminal log tail and a copyable manual command to finish by hand. *Why it matters:* whatever the failed step was blocking (installing the engine, starting it, upgrading it) isn't done, so syncing is still stalled. *Options:* none — Retry / Dismiss. *Action button:* "Retry" (re-POSTs the original action); "Dismiss" sets the job `idle` client-side.

**(C) The fix.** Depends on `job.kind`: retry the same POST (`/install`, `/daemon`, `/upgrade`) after addressing the named cause, or run the provided `manualCommand`. Start-failure sub-causes route to their specific fixes (config-repair §10.1.3, start+migrate §10.1.5). No blind auto-retry — the manual command is the guaranteed fallback. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` — `fail()` `manualCommand` (lines 278–286); frontend `IpfsOffPage.tsx` `ErrorPanel` `onRetry` (lines 109–111).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-job-failed` and the frontend `ipfs-install-start-job-errored`. Because config-crash diagnoses are re-routed, a persistent ErrorPanel means a genuinely non-config failure (missing package manager, permissions, PATH).

#### 10.1.10 A tracked file has zero peers — it isn't backed up — `bad` (id: ipfs-pin-zero-peers-not-backed-up)

*Where shown:* the `/ipfs/pins` pinset table — the **Peers** column cell renders the count `0` in **red text**. No banner, no rollup, no popup, no Fix today.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** For a pin row: `p.tracked !== 'import'` **AND** `p.peers === 0` → the peer count renders red. Meaning: LFBridge is tracking this file but **no other of the user's computers** is pinning it — a single copy, at risk. Untracked/import pins are excluded (not managed yet). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/ipfs/IpfsPage.tsx` — peers column cell (lines 217–226, red when `tracked!=='import' && peers===0`); the type doc in `shared/src/types.ts` notes "peers: 0 on a tracked file = not backed up."

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* this tracked file currently exists on **only this computer** — no other machine has pinned its CID. *Why it matters:* this is the charter's whole point ("if you lose a laptop, your files are safely on your other computers") — if this machine is lost, the file is **gone**. *Options:* none — the real remedy is another machine coming online. *Action button:* "Publish IPFS list" (so a peer can pin these CIDs) — informational, not a true auto-fix.

**(C) The fix.** **No single safe auto-fix** — the actual fix is another computer running LFBridge and pinning the CID. The app can `publishIpfsList` so peers know what to fetch. Manual next step: open LFBridge on a second computer and let it sync. *Fix in:* not wired as a banner — related publish action `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/menu/domainActions.ts` `publishIpfsList()` (used in `IpfsPage` `ipfsActions` line 91).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap — high priority:** this is arguably the single most important "files at risk" (Broken) signal in the whole app, yet it is only per-cell red text with no aggregate verdict. It **should** roll up to a top-of-page banner ("N tracked files have no backup copy") — a real gap to close.

#### 10.1.11 IPFS won't restart after you reboot (auto-start off) — `warn` (id: ipfs-autostart-off)

*Where shown:* App-wide `IpfsStatusBanner` **scenario C** — a gentle, dismissible, one-time **slate** strip (never the amber alarm), only when the node is healthy; and the `/ipfs` dashboard **AutostartRow** (a filled-blue CTA when off, a muted green "on ✓" when on).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `liveness.running === true` AND `autostartSupported === true` (macOS) AND `autostartEnabled === false` AND (for the banner) the one-time dismissal `localStorage['lfb.ipfs.autostartNudgeDismissed'] !== '1'`. `autostartEnabled` = the LaunchAgent plist exists **AND** `launchctl print` shows it loaded. A related sub-condition, **installed-but-not-loaded**: `autostartStatus().installed === true` (plist present at `~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.largefilebridge.ipfs.plist`) but `enabled === false` (booted out / never bootstrapped) — the reboot promise is silently broken; liveness only exposes `autostartEnabled`, so today the banner treats this identically to "off." *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-autostart.service.ts` — `autostartStatus()` (lines 109–119, `installed` via `fs.existsSync` 113, `enabled` via `isLoaded` 99–106); frontend `IpfsStatusBanner.tsx` scenario-C branch (lines 86–113, `nudgeDismissed` 23–29) and `ipfsShared.tsx` `AutostartRow` (lines 409–457).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* after a reboot or logout, the IPFS daemon won't come back on its own unless a per-user launchd LaunchAgent (`com.largefilebridge.ipfs`, running `ipfs daemon --enable-gc`) is installed and loaded; without it, background sync silently pauses until you next open the app. Framed as an **offer**, not an alarm. *Why it matters:* your 15-minute background sync stops moving files after any reboot and you may not notice for days. *Options:* checkbox "Don't offer this again for this computer" (Improvable-only dismissal, persisted client-side). *Action button:* "Turn on auto-start" (in-place, no daemon restart, no navigation).

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/autostart {action:'install'}` → `installAutostart()`: resolve the absolute `ipfs` path → write `~/Library/LaunchAgents/com.largefilebridge.ipfs.plist` (RunAtLoad + KeepAlive=false, so your manual On/Off still wins) → `launchctl bootout/bootstrap/enable` → persist `ipfs.auto_start_daemon=true`. It is **idempotent**, so it also re-loads an installed-but-unloaded agent. `{action:'remove'}` turns it off. On success invalidates the `ipfsLiveness` + `ipfsNode` queries. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /autostart` (lines 119–131) → `ipfs-autostart.service.ts` `installAutostart()` (lines 127–158, bootout/bootstrap/enable 152–154).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-autostart-off-gentle-nudge`, `ipfs-autostart-off`, `ipfs-autostart-off-dashboard-row`, `ipfs-autostart-installed-but-not-loaded`, and `ipfs-autostart-binary-not-found`. **Binary-not-found sub-case:** `installAutostart()` calls `resolveIpfsBin()` (`command -v ipfs`, absolute path required); null → throws "Couldn't find the ipfs binary to auto-start" — during a start-with-autostart this is caught as a **non-fatal** note ("IPFS is running, but auto-start couldn't be fully enabled"), the running daemon isn't torn down; fix is to install `ipfs` to a standard path (`/opt/homebrew/bin` / `/usr/local/bin`) and retry (`ipfs-autostart.service.ts` `resolveIpfsBin()` lines 47–55). **Gap:** liveness doesn't distinguish installed-but-unloaded from not-installed — it would need an `autostartInstalled` field, or the banner should read `node.autostart` from `GET /node`. This LaunchAgent is for the **IPFS daemon**, separate from the 15-minute LFBridge sync plist. The only genuinely amber IPFS state in the app-wide banner.

#### 10.1.12 Public-gateway opt-out is on (acknowledged) — `warn` (id: ipfs-public-gateway-optout-acknowledged)

*Where shown:* the `/ipfs/pins` NodeVerdict and dashboard SecurityCard rendered **amber "acknowledged"** instead of red (no Fix button); the Settings IPFS row (self-healing warn: "Public gateway opt-out: yes").

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `node.publicGateway === true` (app config `ipfs.public_gateway`) **AND** the node is not compliant — the user **deliberately** flipped the public-gateway setting on this machine, so the red compliance error (§10.1.8) is downgraded to amber. `state = acknowledged ? 'warn' : 'bad'`; the Fix `action` is `undefined` when acknowledged. `enforceCompliance()` early-returns (warn log, no change) while the opt-out is on. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` — `publicGateway` (line 148), `ipfs.service.ts` `enforceCompliance()` early-return (lines 396–399); frontend `IpfsPage.tsx` `acknowledged` (line 399), `state` (line 402), `ipfsShared.tsx` `SecurityCard` amber footer (lines 234–241).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* you opted this machine out of the only-our-content default via global settings, so it may act as a broader gateway — this is the **one acceptable exception** the charter allows. *Why it matters:* while opted out, this machine can cache and serve content that isn't yours (bandwidth/privacy/abuse tradeoff you accepted). *Options:* checkbox "Return this computer to the secure default." *Action button:* "Keep opt-out" (Cancel) / "Restore secure default" when the option is chosen.

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix by design** — it's an acknowledged opt-out, not a defect. To return to the secure default: turn off `ipfs.public_gateway` in global settings (PATCH app config), **then** POST `/api/ipfs/enforce` to rebind loopback-only and reset the reprovide strategy. *Fix in:* no wired revert action from the banner today (a gap — `IpfsPage.tsx` renders `undefined` action when acknowledged); the enforce endpoint exists at `ipfs.router.ts` `POST /enforce` (line 193), gated behind flipping the setting.

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-noncompliant-acknowledged-optout`, `ipfs-public-gateway-optout-acknowledged`, and the Settings `ipfs-not-compliant-gateway` warn rendering (which says it "will be corrected on the next sync" — self-healing, not an alarm, and is suppressed when `publicGateway=true`). Per the charter, this amber/acknowledged state must **never** be rendered red — it is the sanctioned exception, the counterpart to the §10.1.8 flag.

#### 10.1.13 A newer, recommended IPFS (Kubo) is available — `warn` (id: ipfs-kubo-below-baseline)

*Where shown:* the `/ipfs` dashboard **UpgradeCard** — an urgent amber variant when below baseline, a non-urgent variant when merely an update is available.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Two states, one card. **Urgent (amber):** `upgrade.belowBaseline === true` — installed Kubo version `< RECOMMENDED_MIN_VERSION` (`0.30.0`), a network-free version compare, only true when the version parses. **Non-urgent (neutral offer):** `upgrade.updateAvailable === true` and NOT below baseline — macOS + package manager only, `brew outdated --quiet ipfs` reports it outdated (reads brew's local state, no forced network fetch, 6 s timeout, swallowed to `null` on error / non-mac / inconclusive). The card returns null when neither is true. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `upgradeInfo()` `belowBaseline` (line 390, `RECOMMENDED_MIN_VERSION='0.30.0'` line 24), `updateAvailable` (lines 395–407); frontend `ipfsShared.tsx` `UpgradeCard` (lines 358–402, `urgent=belowBaseline` 367).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* your installed Kubo predates LFBridge's supported floor (`0.30.0`) — old enough to risk the very start-crash this feature guards (the Kubo 0.42 Reprovider FATAL class), or, in the non-urgent case, simply behind the latest build. *Why it matters:* old builds can fail to start after a config change and may miss config keys LFBridge relies on. *Options:* none — one-click when a package manager can run it; otherwise a copyable command. *Action button:* "Upgrade IPFS" (only when `canAutoUpgrade`).

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/upgrade` → `startUpgrade()`: a single-flight watchable job — stop daemon → `brew upgrade ipfs` / `winget upgrade IPFS.Kubo` → restart (with start-failure diagnosis) → `enforceCompliance`. On unsupported platform / missing package manager it fails to a copyable manual command (dist.ipfs.tech). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /upgrade` (lines 111–114) → `ipfs-node.service.ts` `startUpgrade()` (lines 566–617); `upgradePlan()` in `ipfs-config-health.service.ts` (lines 425–438).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-version-below-baseline`, `ipfs-kubo-below-baseline`, and `ipfs-kubo-update-available`. `belowBaseline` is authoritative and network-free (a baked-in baseline); `updateAvailable` is best-effort **local** package-manager state that never phones home — `null` (unknown) must never render an alarm.

#### 10.1.14 Pinned files aren't tracked yet (import backlog) — `warn` (id: ipfs-untracked-import-backlog)

*Where shown:* the `/ipfs/pins` page — an amber DiagnosticCard, an amber "Untracked" StatTile, an "Import all untracked (N)" header button, and an "Untracked only" table filter; also a metric on the dashboard "Shared files" tile ("N to import").

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `node.untrackedCount > 0` — pins present on this computer that LFBridge isn't managing (`tracked === 'import'`). The card and warn StatTile render only when the node is up (`!nodeDown`) and `untrackedCount > 0`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/ipfs/IpfsPage.tsx` — `untrackedCount` (line 85), DiagnosticCard (lines 297–313), warn StatTile (lines 285–292), "Import all untracked" header button (lines 259–267); dashboard tile `IpfsDashboardPage.tsx` (lines 177–184).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "Tracked" means LFBridge recorded the file in a repo manifest so it can keep it synced and backed up across your computers; importing is **metadata-only** — no bytes move, nothing on disk changes. *Why it matters:* these stray pins aren't being synced or protected like the rest of your files until they're brought under management. *Options:* scope — "Import all N," "Import selected," or per-row "Import." *Action button:* "Import all" (metadata-only, safe).

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/import {all:true}` (or `{cids:[...]}` for a scoped subset) → records the CIDs into tracking; returns `{imported, skipped, data}`. Disabled when `nodeDown`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /import` (line 155); frontend `IpfsPage.tsx` `doImport` mutation (lines 55–63) + DiagnosticCard FixButton (lines 303–307).

**Notes / gaps.** The model example of the well-wired amber "offer, not alarm" pattern for this category. Per-row and bulk imports are the same action scoped.

#### 10.1.15 Proactive IPFS config improvements (GC period, StorageMax, repo behind) — `warn` (id: ipfs-config-health-warn-info-dashboard)

*Where shown:* the `/ipfs` **running** dashboard — a low-key ConfigHealthCard (amber tint for `warn`, plain white for `info`); never blocks because the node is up.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `node.configHealth.checked === true` AND `issues.length > 0` AND the most-severe issue is `warn` or `info` (no blocker, since the node is running). Instances include: **GC off** — the config has a `Datastore` block but `Datastore.GCPeriod` is empty → issue `id:'gc-off'`, `class:'suspicious'`, `severity:'info'`, `fixable:false` (also `posture.gcOn === false`); **StorageMax unset** — GC has no cap; **repo behind the binary** — could `--migrate` proactively. `class 'suspicious'` (info) is never force-fixed. The card returns null when `!checked` or no issues. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `configHealth()` `gc-off` (lines 177–192); `nodePosture()` `gcOn` in `ipfs.service.ts` (lines 334–338); frontend `IpfsDashboardPage.tsx` ConfigHealthCard mount (line 233) + `ipfsShared.tsx` ConfigHealthCard (lines 271–353, tone by severity 290–294).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* proactive, non-blocking config tune-ups while the engine is up and fine — e.g. GC reclaims incidentally-cached third-party blocks so your repo doesn't grow with other people's content; StorageMax gives GC a cap; a repo a version behind can be migrated ahead of the next upgrade. *Why it matters:* left alone, the repo can slowly bloat or hit a future start snag — none of it is urgent. *Options:* the "What we'll change" list; info-class items are advisory only. *Action button:* "Review & Fix Configuration" (only when there's a fixable issue).

**(C) The fix.** POST `/api/ipfs/config-repair {issueIds}` while the node keeps running (proactive migration); a backup is written and the toast reports its path. **GC-off has no auto-fix** (`fixable:false`) because LFBridge always launches the daemon with `--enable-gc` at runtime, so only the config-level period is at issue — manual next step `ipfs config Datastore.GCPeriod "1h"`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.router.ts` — `POST /config-repair` (line 84); frontend `IpfsDashboardPage.tsx` repair mutation (lines 69–76).

**Notes / gaps.** Merges `ipfs-config-health-warn-info-dashboard` and `ipfs-gc-off`. Same component as the §10.1.3 blocker takeover, but on the dashboard it must **never** block (node running). Keep info-class items low-key — not amber alarms.

#### 10.1.16 No IPFS repository yet — first-run setup — `warn` (id: ipfs-config-missing)

*Where shown:* effectively invisible as an alarm — routed via the app-wide "not installed/not running" banner to `/ipfs/off`, where it flows through the normal Start (not the Fix-config card).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `configHealth` reads `$IPFS_PATH/config` (default `~/.ipfs/config`); the file doesn't exist → issue `id:'missing'`, `class:'missing'`, `severity:'blocker'`, `hasBlocker=true`. The repository was never initialized. Crucially, `IpfsOffPage.configBlocker()` **excludes** `class 'missing'` (lines 24–26), so a missing config does **not** show the red Fix-config takeover — it's treated as a normal Start that will init. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-config-health.service.ts` — `configHealth()` missing branch (lines 98–112); frontend `IpfsOffPage.tsx` `configBlocker()` (lines 24–26).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* there's no IPFS repository yet; turning IPFS on will initialize one (`~/.ipfs`) and generate this computer's node identity (PeerID). Frame as one-time setup, not an error. *Why it matters:* nothing to lose — it's benign first-run. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Start IPFS" (which inits first).

**(C) The fix.** No separate fix — POST `/api/ipfs/daemon {action:'start'}` → `controlDaemon` → `ensureInit()` runs `ipfs init` (idempotent) before starting. An equivalent `config-repair {issueIds:['missing']}` returns `needsInit=true` for the caller to init. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` — `ensureInit()` (lines 339–350); `repairConfig` missing branch (lines 306–313).

**Notes / gaps.** Severity is `blocker` in the raw health model but user-facing this is **benign** — treat as warn/neutral, never a red alarm. It is the deliberate exclusion that lets §10.1.3's `configBlocker()` fire only on real, non-missing config faults.

#### 10.1.17 IPFS repo is nearly full (near StorageMax) — `warn` (id: ipfs-repo-near-storage-max)

*Where shown:* **Gap — not yet wired.** The data (`repoSizeBytes` vs `storageMaxBytes`) is displayed on the `/ipfs` dashboard node metrics, but no verdict/banner is computed from it.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `repoStat()` exposes `RepoSize` and `StorageMax`; these surface as `repoSizeBytes` / `storageMaxBytes` in the node metrics but are **never compared**. The intended condition: when `repoSizeBytes` approaches/exceeds `StorageMax` (the Kubo GC watermark), pinning your own files starts to fail and sync silently stalls. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs.service.ts` — `repoStat()` (lines 204–223); surfaced in `ipfs-node.service.ts` metrics (lines 129–140, `repoSizeBytes` 133, `storageMaxBytes` 134) but with no threshold check.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* IPFS has a `StorageMax` cap; as the repo fills, GC runs and pinning new content can fail — silently stopping the sync of your large files. *Why it matters:* new/changed files stop backing up to your other computers without any error the user notices. *Options:* "Raise StorageMax" vs "Free disk space." *Action button:* "Raise storage limit" (candidate).

**(C) The fix.** **Gap — no auto-fix wired.** Candidate: offer to raise `Datastore.StorageMax` via RPC `config set` after confirming free disk, or run GC. Manual next step: `ipfs config Datastore.StorageMax "<N>GB"` then restart, or free disk space. *Fix in:* no endpoint today — detection scaffolding at `ipfs.service.ts` `repoStat()` (lines 204–223).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** a condition that clearly *should* warn (files-at-risk / sync-not-moving) but no detection is implemented yet — flagged for future wiring.

#### 10.1.18 The IPFS liveness check itself is failing (invisible) — `warn` (id: ipfs-liveness-endpoint-error)

*Where shown:* nowhere visible by design — the app-wide banner renders nothing; the failure is logged only.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The `useQuery(['ipfsLiveness'])` returns an error (endpoint down / network fail). The banner's `if (!data) return null` guard hides it; a `useEffect` logs a WARN via `clientLog`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/IpfsStatusBanner.tsx` — query + `clientLog.warn('IpfsStatusBanner.liveness', error)` (lines 34–44), null guard (line 59).

**(B) The popup.** N/A to the user by design — a briefly-down node is an expected transient state, so no alarm is raised. *What this is / Why it matters:* only relevant to an operator: if the endpoint itself is persistently 500-ing, the user gets **zero** IPFS guidance anywhere off the `/ipfs` pages. *Options / Action button:* none.

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix** — warn-by-intent. The fault trail lands in `clientLog` under `IpfsStatusBanner.liveness`; a persistent failure means the `/api/ipfs/liveness` route or the app server is down — restart the backend. *Fix in:* logging only at `IpfsStatusBanner.tsx` (lines 42–44).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap (intentional):** invisible. Included for completeness — the endpoint-error path is a real handled condition; a persistent (not transient) failure has no user-facing surface, which is a coverage hole worth acknowledging.

#### 10.1.19 Auto-start isn't available on this operating system — `neutral` (id: ipfs-autostart-unsupported-os)

*Where shown:* the `/ipfs/off` StoppedCard note and the `/ipfs` dashboard AutostartRow ("not available on this operating system yet"); the app-wide scenario-C nudge is **suppressed** entirely.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `autostartStatus().supported === false` whenever `process.platform !== 'darwin'` (the launchd LaunchAgent is macOS-only). On such machines IPFS will not come back after a reboot and there is no in-app way to make it. The scenario-C nudge is gated on `autostartSupported`, so non-mac users never see it. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-autostart.service.ts` — `supported()` (lines 30–32), `autostartStatus()` (line 110), `installAutostart` throw on unsupported (lines 128–129); frontend `IpfsStatusBanner.tsx` scenario-C guard (line 86), `ipfsShared.tsx` `AutostartRow` `!supported` branch (lines 417–424), `IpfsOffPage.tsx` StoppedCard note (lines 203–207).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* reboot auto-start is currently macOS/launchd only; on other OSes you must restart IPFS manually after a reboot (or configure your OS's own service). Neutral, informational. *Why it matters:* after a reboot on this OS, background sync stays paused until you reopen the app and start IPFS. *Options / Action button:* none.

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix** (feature not implemented for this OS). Manual next step: after each reboot reopen LFBridge and turn IPFS on, or configure an OS-native service (a systemd user unit on Linux running `ipfs daemon --enable-gc` at login). *Fix in:* no endpoint — informational only.

**Notes / gaps.** Merges both `ipfs-autostart-unsupported-os` entries. Neutral, not warn/bad — included because it changes what the auto-start warnings (§10.1.11) *can* say and it silently suppresses the scenario-C nudge. **Gap:** Windows/Linux auto-start is unimplemented; per the charter, hosted/server-side comes later, so this is acceptable but should be acknowledged, not silent.

## 10.2 Repos & per-repo verdicts

Every repo answers "am I OK?" through one **RepoVerdict** banner on the One-Repo page, plus per-row colored cues on the Repos list. The verdict is a **worst-first state machine**: a single `RepoVerdict` component walks a fixed branch chain and shows the first condition that is true, so exactly one banner shows at a time. That chain is computed in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — component `RepoVerdict` (lines 347–406), fed by backend rollup `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `rollupStatus()` (lines 250–263) and `countDecisions()` (lines 230–241). The locked precedence is: **#1 IPFS down → #2 last-sync error (incl. missing folder) → #3 synced-but-no-peer → #4 needs-decision → #5 pending → #6 nothing-set-to-sync → ok**. Below, the fifteen conditions are ordered Broken → Improvable → neutral/ok; each names its rank in that chain where it participates.

#### 10.2.1 IPFS engine is down — `bad` (id: repo-ipfs-down)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page banner, **worst-first cause #1** (wins over every other repo condition).

**Cross-reference — owned by §10.1 (IPFS).** This is the repo-page *surface* of the global IPFS-unreachable verdict; its detection (`detail.ipfs === "unreachable"`), popup education, and the real fix (start/install the daemon) are fully documented at **§10.1 `ipfs-down`**. On the repo page specifically it is the first branch of `RepoVerdict` (`OneRepoPage.tsx` line 347 `const ipfsDown = detail.ipfs === "unreachable"`, branch lines 359–367) and it **gates the whole page**: the page-level `ipfsDown` (line 101) disables the `PinToggle` (line 151) and the header **Sync now** button (line 232). `detail.ipfs` is filled server-side by `computeRepoDetail(folder, await ipfs.health())` (`repos.router.ts` line 101; `units.service.ts` `computeRepoDetail` lines 178–197).

**Notes / gaps.** Today's inline `FixButton` reads **"Open IPFS"** and only *navigates* to `/ipfs` — it does not start the daemon. Per §10.1 the blue-arrow popup should start it inline (`POST /api/ipfs/daemon {action:"start", autostart:true, migrate:true}`).
