Beware the Kubo 0.42 Reprovider crash (MEMORY): an "unreachable" node may be crash-looping on a bad config, which plain start+migrate won't fix — that is the distinct IPFS-partition condition, not a repo condition.

#### 10.2.2 Last sync hit an error — `bad` (id: repo-last-sync-error)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page banner, **worst-first cause #2** (only reachable when IPFS is up).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `detail.status === "error"`. Backend `rollupStatus()` returns `"error"` as its **first, highest-precedence** branch when **`status.last_error` is set OR `status.repo_state === "missing"`** — i.e. the most recent sync/scan pass persisted an error message to the unit status file, *or* the working tree is gone (see 10.2.3). `last_error` is the verbatim failure string from that last pass. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — `RepoVerdict` `else if (detail.status === "error")` (lines 368–376); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `rollupStatus()` line 256 `if (status.last_error || status.repo_state === "missing") return "error"` (lines 250–263); status schema `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/shared/src/schemas.ts` lines 402–403 (`repo_state`, `last_error`).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The previous attempt to sync this repo failed and stopped partway; decisions are still saved but the last pass did not complete, so files may be stale on your other computers. *Why it matters:* files you thought were backed up may not have moved; a repeated error usually points at a specific fixable cause. *Options:* none — one-click retry; the popup should surface `detail.status`/`last_error` **verbatim** (via a "Details" disclosure) so the user can judge transient vs. structural. *Action button:* "Sync now".

**(C) The fix.** Retries the whole-repo sync: `POST /api/repos/:repoId/sync`, which runs `track('sync', …) → syncRepoFolder`; on success the pass clears `last_error` and recomputes `status`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /:repoId/sync` (lines 152–177).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** `RepoDetail` exposes only the coarse `status` enum, **not** `last_error`, so today the banner can't say *why* it errored — add `last_error` to `RepoDetail` so the popup can explain the specific failure. **Guard:** if the underlying cause is a missing folder (10.2.3), "Sync now" cannot help — the popup must distinguish that case.

#### 10.2.3 Repo folder is gone from disk — `bad` (id: repo-folder-missing)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page — **currently folded into the generic "error" banner (10.2.2)**; not yet distinguished.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `status.repo_state === "missing"` — the registered working tree no longer exists (moved, renamed, deleted, or on an unmounted drive/cloud mount). `rollupStatus()` maps this to the **same `"error"`** status as `last_error`, so the frontend currently shows the identical "hit an error on its last sync" banner and offers "Sync now" — which cannot recreate a vanished folder. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `rollupStatus()` line 256 (`|| status.repo_state === "missing"`); schema `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/shared/src/schemas.ts` line 402; frontend collapses it into `OneRepoPage.tsx` lines 368–376.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The folder LFBridge was watching can't be found — likely moved, renamed, deleted, or on a drive/cloud mount that isn't mounted right now. *Why it matters:* this machine can no longer scan or update those files; pinned copies may still be safe on IPFS/peers, but this computer has dropped out of the loop for this repo. *Options:* radios for the real choices — **(a) I'll restore/remount the folder** (then Rescan), **(b) Unregister this repo from LFBridge** (leaves files on disk untouched). *Action button:* "Rescan" for (a), or **"Unregister repo"** for (b) — the unregister variant is **destructive → red button + confirm** (it removes the repo from LFBridge, though never deletes files).

**(C) The fix.** No safe auto-fix — LFBridge must never recreate or delete folders. If the path is restored, `POST /api/repos/rescan` re-discovers it. If the folder is intentionally gone, `DELETE /api/repos/:repoId` unregisters it (never deletes files on disk). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `DELETE /:repoId` (lines 84–94) and `POST /rescan` (lines 54–57).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** not distinguished from a generic sync error — split `rollupStatus()` so `repo_state === "missing"` produces a **distinct** verdict/message with a folder-relocate-or-unregister action instead of the misleading "Sync now".

#### 10.2.4 The repo scan failed — `bad` (id: repos-scan-failed)

*Where shown:* Repos landing page — **currently a transient toast only; should be a persistent banner**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `scan.status === "error"` from `GET /api/repos/scan-status` (React Query key `['scanStatus']`). Detected when a running discovery scan transitions to error; an effect fires `toast.error(scan.error ?? 'Scan failed')`. A failed discovery scan means repo counts/candidates are **stale**, so the whole page's data may be wrong. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/ReposPage.tsx` — `scanStatus` query + error effect (lines 38–49), rescan `onError` (lines 57–60); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /rescan` + `GET /scan-status` via `getScanJob` (lines 52–63); the scanner module `scan-job.ts` owns the `error` field.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The background scan that discovers big files and refreshes counts hit an error, so the repo list may be out of date. *Why it matters:* the numbers you see (undecided/pending/peers) can't be trusted until a scan succeeds. *Options:* none — one-click retry; surface `scan.error` **verbatim** (permission denied, unmounted path, folder removed are the common causes). *Action button:* "Rescan".

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/repos/rescan` (`startScan('manual')`, single-flight/coalescing) re-runs discovery. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /rescan` + `GET /scan-status` (lines 52–63); frontend rescan mutation `ReposPage.tsx` (lines 51–61).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** only a disappearing sonner toast today — it vanishes in seconds and never explains the cause. A persistent `bad` banner (or the missing list-rollup of 10.2.13) should hold the error until the next successful scan.

#### 10.2.5 Repo not found / removed — `bad` (id: repo-not-found)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page, Repo Settings page, and every repo action — **surfaces as a query error / toast, not a banner**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Backend `folderForRepoId(repoId)` returns `null` → `404 {ok:false, error:'repo not found'}` on `GET /:repoId`, `GET/PATCH /:repoId/settings`, `PATCH /:repoId/files`, `POST /:repoId/sync`, `POST /:repoId/bookmark`, and `DELETE /:repoId`. Happens when the `repoId` in the URL no longer maps to a registered folder (unregistered on this or another computer, config drift, a stale bookmark/tab). *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — the `if (!folder) return res.status(404)` guards at lines 71, 86, 99, 112, 132, 156, 182, 194; frontend `OneRepoPage.tsx` repo query `['repo', repoId]` (lines 49–52, no explicit 404 UI — `detail` stays `undefined` so `RepoVerdict`/counts never render), `RepoSettingsPage.tsx` `if (!s) return 'Loading…'` (line 30).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The repo this page points at is no longer registered with LFBridge — it may have been removed here or on another computer. *Why it matters:* nothing on this page is actionable until you point at a live repo; note that "unregistered from LFBridge" leaves the files on disk untouched — it is **not** the same as the folder being deleted. *Options:* radios — **(a) Back to Repos list**, **(b) Re-add this folder** (only if it still exists on disk). *Action button:* "Back to Repos" (or "Add repo" for (b)).

**(C) The fix.** No auto-fix — route back to `/repos`, and if the folder still exists offer Add repo: `POST /api/repos {path}`. *Fix in:* re-add via `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /api/repos` (lines 37–50); the not-found source is the `folderForRepoId` guards above — no auto-fix, routes to the Repos list.

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** the 404 has no dedicated UI. `RepoSettingsPage`'s `if (!s) return 'Loading…'` (line 30) conflates "not loaded yet" with "does not exist," so a missing repo hangs on a **permanent, misleading "Loading…"** — replace it with an explicit not-found state.

#### 10.2.6 Synced files aren't on any other computer yet (not backed up) — `warn` (id: repo-synced-no-peer)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page banner, **worst-first cause #3** (IPFS up, no error); mirrored per-row on the Repos list as a red peer count (no banner).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `noPeerCount = detail.files.filter(f => f.decision === "sync" && f.peers.length === 0).length`; fires when `> 0`. `f.peers` comes from the manifest's `pinned_by` list — a synced file with **zero peers exists only on this machine**. On the Repos list the same risk shows as `peerCount === 0` rendered red at the repo level, with no banner. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — `RepoVerdict` `noPeerCount` (line 350) + branch (lines 377–385), per-file red peers cell (lines 200–201); list mirror `ReposPage.tsx` peers column (lines 126–127, `peerCount === 0 → text-red-600`); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `composeFileRows()` `peers = m?.pinned_by ?? []` (lines 207–221), `peerCountForFiles()` (lines 243–247).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* A file set to Sync is only truly **backed up** once at least one *other* of your computers has pinned it; these files have a CID but zero peers, so they live only here. *Why it matters:* if this machine dies, these files are **lost** — this is the app's headline promise (UC-2, "a file didn't show up on my other computer"). *Options:* none from this machine — the fix lives on the *other* computer. *Action button:* "See devices" (routes to `/devices`); optionally an inline "Re-announce" that runs a sync pass to re-provide the CID.

**(C) The fix.** **No single-click server fix from this machine can create a peer** — backup requires another machine to pin. The button routes to `/devices` to show which computers are online and nudge the user to open LFBridge there. Optionally `POST /api/repos/:repoId/sync` re-announces/provides the CID so peers find it faster. *Fix in:* re-announce via `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /:repoId/sync` (lines 152–177); peer/device visibility is served by the devices module — no auto-fix, routes to `/devices`.

**Notes / gaps.** Distinguish from **pending** (10.2.8): here the CID **exists**, only no peer has pulled it; pending may still lack a CID. **Gap:** the list-level equivalent (`peerCount === 0`) has **no banner** — the Repos list should roll this into a verdict (see 10.2.13).

#### 10.2.7 N files need a decision (Sync or Ignore) — `warn` (id: repo-files-need-decision)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page banner, **worst-first cause #4**; Repos list shows the undecided count in brand color per row. **This is the canonical example that drives §0–§4 of this spec.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `detail.counts.undecided > 0` (and no worse cause). A file is "undecided" when there is **no entry in `cfg.decisions[path]`** (`Decision` defaults to `"undecided"`); `countDecisions()` increments `undecided` for every such file, and `rollupStatus()` maps `undecided > 0` (when not error/syncing/behind) to `"needs_review"`. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — `RepoVerdict` undecided branch (lines 386–389), summary strip (line 256, undecided highlighted); list `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/ReposPage.tsx` undecided column (lines 122–123, `text-[var(--lfb-primary)]`); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `composeFileRows()` decision default undecided (line 208), `countDecisions()` (lines 230–241), `rollupStatus()` `needs_review` (line 260).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFBridge found big files it doesn't yet have instructions for — **Sync** = pin and back up across your computers via IPFS; **Ignore** = leave it alone (still git-ignored, just not bridged). *Why it matters:* nothing moves for undecided files, so your backup is **incomplete** until every big file is decided. *Options:* radios — **◉ Sync all N undecided** (helper: "back them up over IPFS") / **○ Ignore all N undecided** (helper: "git-ignore, don't sync"); plus a checkbox **☐ Also remember this choice for new files here**. There is no correct auto-decision, so the popup presents the choice rather than picking. *Action button:* "Apply & sync" (or "Ignore these files" per the chosen radio).

**(C) The fix.** Writes decisions in bulk: `PATCH /api/repos/:repoId/files {paths, decision}` (`updateRepoConfig` sets `decisions[p] = decision`, or deletes the entry to return a file to undecided). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `PATCH /:repoId/files` (lines 122–150); frontend mutation `OneRepoPage.tsx` `setDecision` (lines 54–62).

**Notes / gaps.** Ties to the charter category-rollup ("big files git-ignored but not tracked → nudge to decide"). **Gap:** today's banner has **no action button** — the fix is only the per-row Decision dropdown / bulk menu in the table; wiring the blue-arrow bulk-decision popup here is exactly what closes the pattern.

#### 10.2.8 N files are queued to transfer — `warn` (id: repo-files-pending-transfer)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page banner, **worst-first cause #5**; Repos list shows the pending count in amber per row.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `detail.counts.pending > 0` (and no worse cause). `transferFor()` returns `'pending'` for a Sync file that has **no CID yet, OR has a CID but zero peers**; `countDecisions()` counts Sync files whose `transfer !== 'synced'` as pending, and `rollupStatus()` maps `pending > 0` to `"behind"`. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — `RepoVerdict` pending branch (lines 390–398); list `ReposPage.tsx` pending column (lines 120–121, amber); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `transferFor()` (lines 224–228), `countDecisions()` (lines 235–238, `transfer !== synced → pending`), `rollupStatus()` `behind` (line 259).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* These files are marked Sync but haven't finished pinning/announcing — either not yet added to IPFS (no CID) or a CID exists but no peer has pulled it. *Why it matters:* they aren't backed up yet, but this is expected in-flight state, not a fault. *Options:* none — one-click. *Action button:* "Sync now".

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/repos/:repoId/sync` runs the pass now (adds missing files to IPFS, provides CIDs, then a background full pass over other repos); report honest counts (added/fetched/skipped/failed) via `syncSummary` rather than a blanket "complete." Otherwise the 15-minute background sync picks them up. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /:repoId/sync` (lines 152–177); frontend `syncNow` mutation `OneRepoPage.tsx` (lines 64–78), `syncSummary` (lines 31–40).

**Notes / gaps.** **Pending overlaps no-peer (10.2.6):** a pending file that has a CID but 0 peers is counted as pending, so `noPeerCount` (#3) can fire on files that are *also* pending — #3 is deliberately ranked **above** #5 so the "not backed up" message wins.

#### 10.2.9 Some files failed to sync — `warn` (id: repo-sync-partial-failures)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page — **currently a transient toast from Sync now, not a persistent banner**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `SyncNowResult.counts.failed > 0`, in two shades: **(a)** `failed > 0 AND added === 0 AND fetched === 0` → `toast.error` (total failure); **(b)** `failed > 0` with some added/fetched → `toast.success` with "N failed" appended. Either way some files did not transfer and remain not-backed-up. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — `syncNow.onSuccess` (lines 66–73, error vs. success on `r.counts.failed`), `syncSummary` (lines 31–40, `if (c.failed) parts.push('${c.failed} failed')`); backend `repos.router.ts` line 167 `track('sync', …)` returns counts from `syncRepoFolder`; counts shape `SyncCounts` in `@lfb/shared`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The last sync pass moved some files but **N failed** (network drop, peer offline, IPFS add error) and those files are **not** yet backed up. *Why it matters:* you may believe a sync "finished" when part of it silently didn't. *Options:* none — one-click retry; ideally list which files failed. *Action button:* "Try again".

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/repos/:repoId/sync` retries — because the failed-file identities aren't returned per-path today, a **whole-repo re-sync** is the safe retry. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /:repoId/sync` (lines 152–177).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** the failed count is transient (toast only). After the pass, failed files fold back into the pending/no-peer banners (#5 / #3), so the durable warning is recoverable — but a per-pass "N failed, retry" banner would close the loop, and the backend should return failed paths so the retry can be scoped.

#### 10.2.10 Repo is not being bridged (Sync is off) — `warn` (id: repo-sync-toggle-off)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page — **only as a tiny "Sync off" label inside the collapsed Repo-details disclosure** — plus a toggle on the Repo Settings page. **No verdict banner today (gap).**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `detail.synced === false` (`RepoUnitConfig.synced`). When the repo-level Sync switch is off, **no** large file in the repo is bridged regardless of per-file Sync decisions — `rollupStatus()` even returns `'never'` when there's no `last_sync_at`. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` line 320 (details disclosure `Sync {detail.synced ? on : off}`, **not** in `RepoVerdict`); settings toggle `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/RepoSettingsPage.tsx` (lines 40–43); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `rollupStatus()` line 261 (`!last_sync_at → 'never'` regardless of `synced`); config field `cfg.synced`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The repo-level Sync switch gates everything — with it off, per-file Sync decisions are saved but nothing pins or transfers, so **none** of this repo's big files are backed up. *Why it matters:* a user can have hundreds of files marked Sync and still be **completely unprotected** because the master switch is off, with no top-of-page warning. *Options:* radios — **(a) Turn Sync on** (resume bridging) / **(b) Keep it paused** (I did this on purpose). Only *warn*, never auto-enable, since a user may have deliberately paused a large repo. *Action button:* "Turn Sync on".

**(C) The fix.** `PATCH /api/repos/:repoId/settings {synced:true}`, then optionally a sync pass `POST /:repoId/sync`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `PATCH /:repoId/settings` (sets `c.synced`, lines 192–226); frontend toggle `RepoSettingsPage.tsx` (lines 41–42).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** not wired into `RepoVerdict`. The neutral "nothing set to sync" banner (10.2.14) does **not** distinguish "repo Sync off" from "no files chosen" — they must be **separate messages** because the fix differs (flip the repo switch vs. choose files).

#### 10.2.11 Repo is shared but has no participant emails — `warn` (id: repo-shared-no-participants)

*Where shown:* Repo Settings page, Sharing section — **no verdict banner today (gap)**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `s.access.shared === true` **AND** `s.access.participants` is empty. "Shared" is on but no allow-listed emails are present, so **no other person's computer is authorized** to pin/fetch this repo — sharing is a silent no-op and the user may falsely believe others are backing up their files. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/RepoSettingsPage.tsx` — `access.shared` toggle + participants `GlobField`, shown only when shared (lines 78–86); backend persists `c.access {shared, participants}` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `PATCH /:repoId/settings` (lines 214–218).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Sharing lets *other* allow-listed people's computers pin this repo (extra off-site backup / family sync), but only the emails you list are authorized — with Sharing on and the list empty, no one else can participate. *Why it matters:* you get **none** of the extra backup you think you enabled; ties to the charter allow-list / no-anonymous-access policy. *Options:* radios — **(a) Add participant emails** (focus the editor) / **(b) Turn Sharing off**. *Action button:* "Add people" (or "Turn Sharing off").

**(C) The fix.** No destructive auto-fix. Either focus the participant editor and save `PATCH /api/repos/:repoId/settings {access:{participants:[…]}}` (emails are **lowercased** on save), or turn sharing off `PATCH {access:{shared:false}}`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `PATCH /:repoId/settings` access (lines 214–218); frontend `RepoSettingsPage.tsx` participants onSave lowercases (lines 81–85).

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** `RepoSettingsPage` has **no StatusBanner at all** — a settings-level verdict row could carry this plus the Sync-off warning (10.2.10).

#### 10.2.12 Repos list has no top-of-page verdict banner — `warn` (id: repos-list-no-rollup-banner)

*Where shown:* Repos landing page — **should be a StatusBanner above the table; currently absent (this warning IS the gap)**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** **GAP:** `ReposPage` renders only a title, an action-links row, and the `DataTable` — **no StatusBanner**. Per-repo problems (`status` `behind`/`needs_review`/`error`, `peerCount === 0`, `pending > 0`, `undecided > 0`) are visible only as colored numbers inside table cells; there is **no worst-of-all-repos rollup** telling the user "am I OK?" at a glance — even though every `RepoRow` already carries `counts`, `peerCount`, and `status`. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/ReposPage.tsx` (lines 148–201, no StatusBanner) — cell cues only: pending (120–121), undecided (122–123), peers (126–127), status pill (130–131); rollup helper available at `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/health.ts` — `worst()` (lines 10–12).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* An aggregate health across all repos, naming the worst offender ("3 repos have files not backed up", "IPFS is down so no repo can sync"). *Why it matters:* green = all repos synced+backed up, amber = some repos have undecided/pending/no-peer files, red = a repo errored or IPFS is down — without it the user must scan every row to notice trouble. *Options:* none — the banner routes to the worst repo. *Action button:* label depends on the worst cause (e.g. "Fix IPFS" → `/ipfs`, or "Open repo" → the single worst repo).

**(C) The fix.** Compute `worst(...)` over all `RepoRow.status` + derived flags (any `peerCount === 0` with `synced > 0` → warn; any `status === 'error'` → bad; global IPFS unreachable → bad) and render a `StatusBanner` whose Fix routes to the single worst repo or to `/ipfs`. **No new backend needed** — `GET /api/repos` already returns everything; add the rollup client-side (or a new `GET /api/repos/health`). *Fix in:* data source `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `GET /api/repos` (rows via `computeRepoRow`, lines 26–34); client rollup would live in `ReposPage.tsx` using `health.ts::worst()` — **no auto-fix, this is a build gap**.

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap: banner not wired yet.** Note `RepoRow` does **not** carry an `ipfs` field (only `RepoDetail` does), so a global IPFS-down verdict on the list needs `GET /api/ipfs/status` or adding `ipfs` to the list payload.

#### 10.2.13 Nothing set to sync in this repo yet — `neutral` (id: repo-nothing-set-to-sync)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page banner, **cause #6 / lowest** (a slate neutral banner, not a warning).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `detail.counts.synced === 0` **and** no error, no pending, no undecided, IPFS up. Means no file has reached `transfer === 'synced'` — either no files are set to Sync, or none have completed. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — `RepoVerdict` synced-zero branch (lines 399–403); backend `counts.synced` from `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/units.service.ts` — `countDecisions()` (lines 236–237, `transfer === 'synced'`).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* This repo is registered but not actively bridging anything yet — a starting state, not a problem; it turns green once at least one file is synced and has a peer. *Why it matters:* nothing is protected until you pick files, but nothing is at risk either. *Options:* none. *Action button:* optional guidance link — "Choose files" (jump to the File System page or the undecided rows). No fix required.

**(C) The fix.** Informational — no fix needed. Decisions are set via `PATCH /:repoId/files`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `PATCH /:repoId/files` (lines 122–150) — **no auto-fix, informational**.

**Notes / gaps.** If `synced === 0` but `undecided > 0`, the undecided branch (10.2.7, warn) fires first, so this neutral state means the repo genuinely has nothing to bridge. **Does not distinguish "repo Sync off" (10.2.10)** — those should be separate messages.

#### 10.2.14 No repos yet — `neutral` (id: repos-empty-no-repos)

*Where shown:* Repos page — **an empty-state block inside the table, not a banner**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The `repos` array is empty (`GET /api/repos` returns `[]`); the `DataTable` renders its empty slot — a dashed "No repos yet. Add your first repo →" button. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/ReposPage.tsx` — `empty` prop (lines 196–200); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `GET /api/repos → listRepoFolders().map(computeRepoRow)` (lines 26–34).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFBridge needs at least one git working tree registered before it can bridge large files. *Why it matters:* onboarding step, not a fault. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Add repo".

**(C) The fix.** Opens `AddRepoDialog` → `POST /api/repos {path}`; on add the backend registers the repo and kicks a background scan (`startScan`). No auto-fix — the user must choose which folder. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/repos/repos.router.ts` — `POST /api/repos` (`registerRepo` + `startScan`, lines 37–50); frontend `AddRepoDialog` `ReposPage.tsx` (lines 232–275).

**Notes / gaps.** Informational neutral onboarding state — no defect.

#### 10.2.15 Everything here is synced and backed up — `ok` (id: repo-everything-synced-ok)

*Where shown:* One-Repo page banner, the **default / green terminal state**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** No branch taken: IPFS ok, `status !== error`, `noPeerCount === 0`, `undecided === 0`, `pending === 0`, `synced > 0`. The sub-line shows last sync time + peer count when `detail.lastSyncAt` is set. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/repos/OneRepoPage.tsx` — `RepoVerdict` initial `state = "ok"` (lines 352–357) falling through every branch to the final `StatusBanner` (line 406).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* All Sync files are pinned locally **and** present on at least one other computer, so they are backed up; shows last sync time and peer count. *Why it matters:* nothing to do — this is the healthy state. *Options:* none. *Action button:* none (no arrow button — there is nothing to fix, per §2 "informational only").

**(C) The fix.** None — this is the healthy/green terminal state. No endpoint. *Fix in:* n/a.

**Notes / gaps.** Included as the `ok` baseline so the `RepoVerdict` state set is exhaustive; per §1 a green "all good" line (or no banner) is the correct render.

## 10.3 Files & directories (per-entity warnings)

These are the warnings that fire on a **single entity** — one file (`/file`, `/image`, `/video`, `/audio`) or one directory (`/dir`) — as opposed to a whole repo (§10.1) or the file-system rollup (§10.4). Almost all are computed by one of two backend functions in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `buildEntityView()` (per-file verdict inputs: decision, transfer, peers, compress heuristic) and `buildDirRollup()` (per-directory category counts) — and rendered by the frontend verdict helpers `fileVerdict()` (`ViewOneFilePage.tsx`) and the rollup table (`ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx`). A recurring theme below is a **gap**: the verdict/state is computed correctly but the standard §2 `WarningBanner` + §3 arrow + §4 popup is **not yet wired** — today's UI is a bare `StatusBanner` with no action, a dead-end toast, or a per-file offer that never rolls up to the page. Ranked Broken first, then Improvable, then neutral.

#### 10.3.1 This file or directory is no longer at that path — `bad` (id: entity-missing-gone)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneFilePage`, `ViewOneDirectoryPage`, and `MediaViewer` all **replace the entire page** with the `EntityHeaderMissing` card when the entity doesn't exist. **Gap:** it renders as a *neutral-bordered* card, not a red/`bad` `WarningBanner`, despite being a Broken condition.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `v.exists === false`. Backend `resolveEntity()` calls `statSync` on the absolute path; if it throws (moved/deleted since last scan) it returns `{ exists: false }`, and `buildEntityView()` returns an all-null `EntityView` with `exists:false` (no decision, transfer, peers, or compress info). Every entity page guards on this first, before any verdict. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `resolveEntity()` (lines ~57–70) + `buildEntityView()` not-exists branch (lines ~117–137); frontend guards `ViewOneFilePage.tsx` (line ~40), `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` (line ~40), `MediaViewer.tsx` (line ~111), rendered by `EntityHeaderMissing` in `entityShared.tsx` (lines ~62–93).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the file (or folder) moved or was deleted since LFBridge last scanned it — the path we're viewing no longer resolves on disk. *Why it matters:* if this file was **set to sync**, the repo manifest and IPFS pin are now **stale**; other computers may still hold the last-synced copy, but this machine's copy is gone; a directory going missing means everything under it is unaccounted for. *Options:* none (no options can recreate bytes) — optionally a single checkbox-free helper "Remove stale sync entry" if the entity was tracked. *Action button:* there is **no fix that restores bytes**; the primary affordance is "Open parent in File System" (and "Copy path"). If it was tracked, a safe secondary action "Remove stale entry" clears the phantom decision so the repo verdict stops flagging it.

**(C) The fix.** No fix endpoint recreates the file. Manual next steps: (1) restore from LFBridge trash (`<stateDir>/trash`) if it was deleted locally; (2) pull the CID from another computer/peer; or (3) clear the stale sync decision. Clearing a decision is `POST /api/entity/decision {decision:'undecided'}` but a missing entity generally can't be re-fetched afterward. *Fix in:* trash restore path via `deleteEntity()` `entity.service.ts` (lines ~405–415); decision clear `entity.router.ts` `POST /decision` (lines ~52–65) — **no auto-fix for the bytes; routes to File System parent + trash.**

**Notes / gaps.** Severity mismatch to fix: the charter treats at-risk/lost bytes as **Broken (red)**, but `EntityHeaderMissing` renders as a neutral card. Promote it to a `StatusBanner state='bad'` (or the shared `WarningBanner`) so the color/icon match the health model (§1).

#### 10.3.2 Set to sync, but the copy isn't in place — `bad` (id: file-sync-transfer-failed)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneFilePage` (`/file`) per-file `StatusBanner`. **Gap:** the banner text says "try Sync now from the repo" but the `/file` page exposes **no Sync-now button**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Inside `fileVerdict()`'s `decision === 'sync'` branch, this is the **first** check, so it outranks the 0-peer warn (10.3.5): fires when `v.transfer === 'missing' || v.transfer === 'error'`. Note: `transferFor()` in the service only ever emits `'na' | 'pending' | 'synced'`, so `'missing'`/`'error'` must arrive from the **repo status/manifest merge outside the entity partition** — confirm that path to make detection complete. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/entity/ViewOneFilePage.tsx` — `fileVerdict()` (verified lines ~164–165); transfer field origin `entity.service.ts` `transferFor()` (lines ~96–100, which cannot itself produce missing/error).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* this file is marked to sync but the actual bytes aren't pinned/available — either the local file went missing or the IPFS add/pull errored. *Why it matters:* until this clears the file is **NOT protected** — it is neither reliably on this machine nor confirmed on any peer. *Options:* none — one-click retry. *Action button:* "Sync now" (blue). If the underlying local file is gone, there is no auto-fix — the popup must say "restore the file first."

**(C) The fix.** "Sync now" re-triggers the **enclosing repo's** sync so this file is re-added and re-pinned — that is a **repo-module** action (`POST` repo sync), not an entity endpoint; the entity service has no re-pin action. *Fix in:* repo sync endpoint in `backend/src/modules/units` / `repo` (not the entity partition) — **no entity auto-fix; routes to repo Sync.** **Gap:** the `/file` page renders the banner but wires no Sync-now button, so the instruction is currently a dead reference.

**Notes / gaps.** Verify which code path populates `EntityView.transfer` with `missing`/`error` (likely the manifest/status merge) so this Broken verdict is provably reachable and not dead. Related repo-level surface: see §10.1 `repo-last-sync-error` / `repo-sync-partial-failures`.

#### 10.3.3 This browser can't play or show this file — `bad` (id: media-decode-failed)

*Where shown:* `MediaViewer` (`/video`, `/image`, `/audio`) — the `DecodeFailure` overlay card inside the media surface (band 5).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** For **video**: the native `<video>` decode fails **and** the backend transcode-stream fallback (`/api/media/stream`) **also** fails → `setFailed(true)`. For **image/audio**: the single element's `onError` fires → `setFailed(true)` (no transcode fallback for those). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` — `ViewerSurface` video `onError` (lines ~761–771, native-then-stream-then-fail), image `onError` (line ~747), audio `onError` (line ~790); overlay is the `DecodeFailure` component (lines ~799–848).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the browser — and the server's on-the-fly transcode — couldn't decode this codec/profile/pixel-format. *Why it matters:* you can't preview the file here; and if it's in a codec like AV1, it also won't upload cleanly to X/TikTok/YouTube/Instagram. *Options:* for video only (when the file lacks the "Do not compress" flag), the convert offer is present; for image/audio there is no convert. *Action button:* video → "Convert to H.264 (MP4)…" (confirm first); image/audio → "Open raw / hand off to the OS" (opens the signed raw URL). Converting to H.264 · yuv420p · AAC · MP4 makes it play everywhere and upload cleanly; the **original is preserved to LFBridge trash**.

**(C) The fix.** "Convert to H.264 (MP4)…" calls `api.compressFile(path, {videoCodec:'h264'})`, **forcing H.264 regardless** of the user's default video-compression preference; on success the original moves to recoverable trash and the viewer re-points to the new path. *Fix in:* `MediaViewer.tsx` `runConvertOffer()` (lines ~873–878) → `api.compressFile` `client.ts` (line ~234); convert is offered only when `kind==='video' && !view.flags.noCompress` (`offerConvert`, line ~814). See compression §10.5 for the transcode engine and trash/transactional guarantees.

**Notes / gaps.** The convert offer is **suppressed** when the file carries the "Do not compress" sticky flag (`offerConvert=false`) — the user must clear that flag first. Distinct from 10.3.12 (compatibility mode), where playback **succeeds** via transcode.

#### 10.3.4 Not set to sync yet — `warn` (id: file-not-set-to-sync)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneFilePage` (`/file`) per-file `StatusBanner` directly under the badge strip. **Gap:** the banner has **no `action` prop** today — the only fix affordance is the separate blue "Add to IPFS" header button.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when the file is inside a registered repo **and** its decision is `undecided`: `v.repo != null && v.decision !== 'sync' && v.decision !== 'ignore'` (the `decision === 'ignore'` case returns a neutral "Set to Ignore — not synced" verdict instead, not this warn). Decision defaults to `undecided` in the backend when the repo config has no entry for the file's relative path. *Computed in:* `ViewOneFilePage.tsx` — `fileVerdict()` `decision !== 'sync'` branch (verified lines ~153–162), rendered via `StatusBanner`; backend default `entity.service.ts` `buildEntityView()` (`decision = cfg.decisions[rel] ?? 'undecided'`, line ~157).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* this file lives inside a repo LFBridge manages, but you haven't decided whether to sync it. *Why it matters:* an undecided large file is **not backed up** to your other computers and, being large, is the kind of file you usually don't want committed to git either — it sits in limbo. *Options:* radios — "Sync (pin to IPFS, keep it on all my computers)" vs "Ignore (git-ignore, don't sync)"; optional checkbox "Also remember this choice for new files here." *Action button:* "Add to IPFS" (blue) when Sync is chosen.

**(C) The fix.** "Add to IPFS" issues `POST /api/entity/decision {path, decision:'sync'}` (`api.setEntityDecision`), flipping the decision to `sync` and returning the fresh `EntityView`; the verdict then re-derives away. **Refused with 409** if the Never-IPFS flag is set for the path. *Fix in:* `entity.router.ts` `POST /decision` (lines ~52–65) → `setEntityDecision()` `entity.service.ts` (lines ~353–367); frontend `api.setEntityDecision` `client.ts` (line ~223).

**Notes / gaps.** Wiring the existing "Add to IPFS" click into `StatusBanner.action` (or the shared `WarningArrowButton`) would complete the §3 pattern. The Decision `<select>` on the page disables the `sync` option when `v.flags.neverIpfs` is on.

#### 10.3.5 Set to sync, but on 0 other computers — not backed up yet — `warn` (id: file-synced-not-backed-up)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneFilePage` (`/file`) per-file `StatusBanner`; the same 0-peer condition also renders the **Peers count in red** in the Sync card and in the `MediaViewer` property grid.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Inside the `decision === 'sync'` branch, **after** the missing/error check (10.3.2): fires when `v.peers.length === 0`. `peers` is derived from the repo manifest entry's `pinned_by[]`. Because `transferFor()` returns `'pending'` whenever `peers` is empty even with a CID, a 0-peer sync file is never reported as `'synced'`. *Computed in:* `ViewOneFilePage.tsx` — `fileVerdict()` 0-peer branch (verified lines ~167–173) + red Peers count (line ~100); `MediaViewer.tsx` PropertyGrid Peers cell (line ~639); backend peers derivation `entity.service.ts` (`m?.pinned_by ?? []`, lines ~158–160), transfer floor `transferFor()` (lines ~96–100).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "synced" locally only means the file is pinned on **this** machine — it is **not a backup** until a second computer pins it too. *Why it matters:* if this machine dies, the file is gone even though it's marked synced; you have zero redundancy. Reassure: the file **is announced** to the IPFS network, so a peer just needs to come online and pull it. *Options:* none actionable on this machine. *Action button:* no safe single-click fix (a real fix requires another peer); a useful secondary "Re-announce to the IPFS DHT" would help peers find it faster — that is an **IPFS-module** action, not an entity endpoint.

**(C) The fix.** No entity endpoint fixes this — the fix is another computer pulling and pinning the CID. Manual next step: open LFBridge on a second allow-listed machine (or wait for its 15-minute launchd sync). *Fix in:* reprovide/announce lives in `backend/src/modules/ipfs/*` (not `entity.router.ts`) — **no entity auto-fix; manual per charter.**

**Notes / gaps.** This is the charter's core value (files safe across your computers), so it must read as an **offer, not an alarm** despite pointing at a real redundancy gap. Related computer-level: see §10.6 `only-this-computer-not-backed-up` and IPFS §10.2 `ipfs-pin-zero-peers-not-backed-up`.

#### 10.3.6 Transfer in progress — `warn` (id: file-transfer-in-progress)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneFilePage` (`/file`) per-file `StatusBanner`; the header button shows a "Syncing" pill.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The lowest-urgency sync verdict: `decision === 'sync'` **and** `v.peers.length > 0` **and** `v.transfer` is set **and** `v.transfer !== 'synced'` (i.e. `'fetching' | 'pushing' | 'pending'`). It sits below the missing/error and 0-peer checks in `fileVerdict()`. *Computed in:* `ViewOneFilePage.tsx` — `fileVerdict()` transfer-in-progress branch (verified lines ~174–175); "Syncing" header pill via `pickPrimary` (lines ~210–216).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the file is actively moving to or from another of your computers and will settle to green (Fixed) when done; "fetching" means it's coming in, "pushing" means it's going out. *Why it matters:* nothing is wrong — this is transient; no action is needed. *Options:* none. *Action button:* none — informational; a "Refresh" that re-invalidates the `['entity', path]` query is the only useful control. This is a purely informational banner (§2), so per the spec it may carry **no arrow button** unless we want the education popup.

**(C) The fix.** No backend action — the state clears itself when the transfer completes. *Fix in:* none; transient state derived from the `transfer` field. **No auto-fix — waits out the transfer.**

**Notes / gaps.** Must **not** render as an alarm; it is the gentlest of the sync verdicts. Consider treating it as informational-only (no popup) per §2's "when there is no popup" rule.

#### 10.3.7 Big files here aren't git-ignored — `warn` (id: dir-big-not-git-ignored)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage` (`/dir`) — the "What's inside" rollup TanStack table row. **Gap:** there is **no top-of-page `WarningBanner`** rolling the categories up, and the row's action is a **dead-end toast**, not a real git-ignore write.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `v.rollup.bigNotIgnored > 0`. Backend, during a bounded walk (≤20k stats, depth ≤8), increments `bigNotIgnored` when a file's `size >= big_file.threshold_bytes` **and** the file is **NOT** among the enclosing repo's discovered git-ignore candidates (`candidateRel`). This row is **never hidden** by a sticky flag. *Computed in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` — row build (line ~47, `hidden:false`); backend `entity.service.ts` `buildDirRollup()` counter `bigNotIgnored` (verified init line ~215, increment line ~289), threshold from `getAppConfig().big_file.threshold_bytes` (line ~193).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* large files bloat a git repo; they should usually be **git-ignored** and synced via IPFS instead. Explain the big-file threshold. *Why it matters:* committing big binaries makes every clone huge and slow, and git is the wrong backup for them. Stress the charter rule: **LFBridge NEVER edits `.gitignore` automatically** — it only surfaces and offers a one-click ignore. *Options:* none / a scoped "all N matching" one-click. *Action button:* "Git-ignore…" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** The button **should** append the matching path(s) to the repo's `.gitignore` (the charter's "easy one-click option to git-ignore"). Today there is **NO such endpoint wired** from this row — the `RowAction` `onClick` only fires `toast.message('Git-ignore is offered per file — open in File System to review.')`. Manual next step: open the folder in File System and git-ignore per file. *Fix in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` `RowAction` onClick (toast only, lines ~145–146; kebab lines ~101–103) — **no auto-fix; routes to File System (`/fs`) for per-file ignore. Gap: needs a real `.gitignore`-write endpoint.**

**Notes / gaps.** Charter "Big-file / git-ignore nudging" explicitly wants the one-click ignore; the current behavior is a dead-end toast. This is the entity-scoped twin of file-system §10.4 `fs-big-not-ignored`.

#### 10.3.8 Big git-ignored files aren't tracked or synced — `warn` (id: dir-big-ignored-not-tracked)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage` (`/dir`) rollup table row. **Gap:** no top-of-page banner; the row navigates away rather than doing a bulk sync.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `v.rollup.bigIgnoredNotTracked > 0` **and** `!v.flags.neverIpfs` (row hidden when the folder's Never-IPFS flag is on — a deliberate opt-out). Backend increments the counter when a file **is** a git-ignore candidate (in `candidateRel`), its decision is **not** `sync` (not in `candidateDecided`), **and** Never-IPFS is off. *Computed in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` — row (line ~48, `hidden` when `flags.neverIpfs`); backend `entity.service.ts` `buildDirRollup()` — candidate/decision gathering (lines ~205–210) + counter `bigIgnoredNotTracked` (verified init line ~216, increment line ~287).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* these big files are **correctly git-ignored**, but **nothing is backing them up** — LFBridge isn't syncing them, so a lost laptop loses them. *Why it matters:* this is the worst-of-both-worlds state — out of git and out of IPFS; zero copies elsewhere. *Options:* radios/checkbox — "Track & sync all N (pin to IPFS)"; mention the Never-IPFS opt-out for anyone who deliberately doesn't want it synced. *Action button:* "Track / Sync" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** Intended one-click: set each matching file's decision to `sync` via `POST /api/entity/decision` per file. Today the row only **navigates to `/fs`** (File System) at this dir for manual per-file decisions — the bulk "sync all matching" is **not wired**. *Fix in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` "track" action navigates to `/fs` (`showMatching`, lines ~92, ~105, ~147); the per-file sync endpoint exists — `entity.router.ts` `POST /decision` (lines ~52–65) — but **no bulk track endpoint is wired from the rollup row. Gap.**

**Notes / gaps.** This is exactly the charter's category-rollup **row 4** ("not tracked by us and not synced"). Hidden entirely when Never-IPFS is on for the folder (deliberate opt-out — do not nag). Twin of file-system §10.4 `fs-big-ignored-not-tracked`.

#### 10.3.9 Videos inside this folder can be compressed — `warn` (id: dir-videos-to-compress)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage` (`/dir`) rollup table row. **Gap:** no top-of-page `WarningBanner` summarizing the categories into a page verdict.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `v.rollup.videosToCompress > 0` **and** `!v.flags.noCompress` (the whole row is hidden when the folder's "Do not compress" sticky flag is on). Backend counts a file when `compressInfo(name).compressState === 'should'` **and** `compressible === 'video'` **and** `!flags.noCompress` **and** `size >= COMPRESS_FLOOR_BYTES (1 MiB)`, over the bounded ≤20k-stat / depth-≤8 walk. *Computed in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` — row (line ~45, hidden when `flags.noCompress`) + Action cell (lines ~143–144); backend `entity.service.ts` `buildDirRollup()` (`videosToCompress++`, verified lines ~274–275), floor `COMPRESS_FLOOR_BYTES` (line ~189).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* N videos under this directory look uncompressed (from the learned duration×resolution size baseline) and could be shrunk with **resolution preserved**. Explain the bulk "Compress inside" flow. *Why it matters:* uncompressed video wastes disk and IPFS bandwidth on every sync. *Options:* checkboxes — which kinds (videos / images), recursive on/off, and whether originals **hard-delete** or go to **recoverable trash** (default: trash). Nothing runs until confirmed. *Action button:* "Compress…" (blue; danger treatment + confirm if hard-delete-originals is chosen).

**(C) The fix.** The confirm-gated "Compress all…" page action calls `api.compressEntity(dir)` → `POST /api/entity/compress`, which **only ACKs and queues** — it does **not** transcode. The **real** per-directory transcode is `POST /api/compress/inside` (`api.compressInside`) with `{root, images, videos, recursive, deleteOriginal}`. *Fix in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` `compressDirConfirmed` (lines ~60–64) + `dirPageActions 'compress-all'` (lines ~65–80); `api.compressEntity` `client.ts` (line ~225) → `entity.router.ts` `POST /compress` (lines ~69–74, queue-only); real engine `api.compressInside` `client.ts` (line ~240) → `/compress/inside`. See compression **§10.5** for the transcode engine, baselines, and trash semantics.

**Notes / gaps.** Two gaps: (1) the dir page has no `WarningBanner` rolling these categories into a top-of-page verdict; (2) `entity/compress` only ACKs+queues — the actual work is `/compress/inside`, so the row and the engine must be wired together or the "Compress…" click appears to do nothing.

#### 10.3.10 Images inside this folder can be compressed — `warn` (id: dir-images-to-compress)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage` (`/dir`) rollup table row. **Gap:** no top-of-page banner.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `v.rollup.imagesToCompress > 0` **and** `!v.flags.noCompress`. Backend counts a file when `compressInfo(name).compressState === 'should'` **and** `compressible === 'image'` **and** `size >= 1 MiB` **and** `!flags.noCompress`. *Computed in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` — row (line ~46); backend `entity.service.ts` `buildDirRollup()` (`imagesToCompress++`, verified lines ~274, ~276).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* N images under this folder look uncompressed. *Why it matters:* image compression is the **secondary** priority (video first, image second per charter) but still reclaims disk and sync bandwidth. Explain the PNG→JPEG/WebP conversion path and its **alpha-channel safety check** before any lossy convert. *Options:* checkboxes as in 10.3.9 (kind, recursive, delete-vs-trash). A PNG with real transparency will be **blocked, not silently flattened**. *Action button:* "Compress…" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** Same path as 10.3.9: `api.compressEntity(dir)` queue, then the real `POST /api/compress/inside` with `images:true`. The per-file alpha check runs **inside the engine** and blocks a PNG with genuine transparency. *Fix in:* `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` (lines ~52–80); `entity.router.ts` `POST /compress` (lines ~69–74); real engine `api.compressInside` `client.ts` (line ~240). See compression **§10.5** and the alpha-block warnings cross-referenced in 10.3.14.

**Notes / gaps.** The **image-interest floor for the folder tint** is 3 MB (`IMAGE_INTEREST_FLOOR_BYTES`, `entity.service.ts` line ~282) — **higher** than the 1 MiB compress-count floor — so the "this folder has interesting images" tint and the compressible-image **count can legitimately differ**; don't treat that as a bug.

#### 10.3.11 This file looks uncompressed — you can compress it — `warn` (id: file-uncompressed-can-compress)

*Where shown:* `MediaViewer` (`/image`, `/video`) action bar as an amber "Compress…" button. **Gap:** `ViewOneFilePage` (`/file`) prints the compress text in its Compression card but shows **no offer button and no verdict banner** — the `/file` page never surfaces the compress offer as a verdict even though the detection would be true there.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `canOfferCompress` is true when `v.compressState === 'should'` **and** `!v.flags.noCompress` **and** `v.compressible` is `'video'` or `'image'`. `compressState`/`compressible` come from `compressInfo(name)` (the learned duration×resolution size baseline) in `badges.ts`. *Computed in:* `MediaViewer.tsx` — `canOfferCompress()` (lines ~851–854), button built (lines ~303–309); `ViewOneFilePage.tsx` — Compression card text only, no banner (lines ~116–128); backend heuristic `entity.service.ts` (`comp = compressInfo(name)`, line ~164).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the file appears uncompressed relative to the learned size baseline for its duration and resolution. *Why it matters:* compressing saves disk and IPFS bandwidth; **resolution is preserved**, quality is medium, and the **original is moved to recoverable LFBridge trash**. *Options:* for a PNG, the alpha/format-change safety check runs first; optional "convert format" choice. *Action button:* "Compress…" (blue; confirm first).

**(C) The fix.** Single file: `api.compressFile(path)` runs the real engine and, on a format change (PNG→JPG), re-points the viewer to the new path. For a directory it's `api.compressEntity(path)` → `POST /api/entity/compress` (queue only). *Fix in:* `api.compressFile` `client.ts` (line ~234) → backend compress module; dir queue `entity.router.ts` `POST /compress` (lines ~69–74); `MediaViewer.tsx` `onCompress` (lines ~253–256) + compress mutation (lines ~238–252). **The full transcode engine, baselines, trash, and safety checks are owned by compression §10.5 — see it for the fix internals.**

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: `ViewOneFilePage` has no compress action/banner at all even though `canOfferCompress` would be true there — the offer exists only in the media viewer. Wiring a `warn` `WarningBanner` + Fix on `/file` closes it. Today's `MediaViewer` still uses a bare `window.confirm` before compressing rather than the §4 popup.

#### 10.3.12 Compatibility mode — streaming a converted copy — `warn` (id: video-compatibility-mode)

*Where shown:* `MediaViewer` (`/video`) — a small translucent overlay **chip** on the media surface while the transcode stream is playing.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `videoFallback === true`: the native `<video>` decode failed **once**, so the element was remounted against `/api/media/stream` (server transcode), which is now playing successfully. *Computed in:* `MediaViewer.tsx` — `videoFallback` state (line ~697), set on first native error (lines ~762–766), `streamSrc` build (line ~706), overlay chip (lines ~774–778).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the file's real codec isn't natively playable, so LFBridge is **transcoding on the fly** just for this preview; seeking and quality may be limited, and it **re-transcodes on every view**. *Why it matters:* it's a recurring CPU cost and a degraded preview — the file is fine, but it will keep needing conversion; it also won't upload natively to social platforms. *Options:* video convert offer. *Action button:* "Convert to H.264 (MP4)…" — but **this is a gap: no convert affordance surfaces while `videoFallback` is active** (only the informational chip); convert is currently offered only after a **full** failure (10.3.3).

**(C) The fix.** "Convert to H.264 (MP4)…" reuses `api.compressFile(path, {videoCodec:'h264'})`, making the on-disk file natively playable and **stopping the repeated transcode**. *Fix in:* `MediaViewer.tsx` `runConvertOffer()` (lines ~873–878) / `api.compressFile` `client.ts` (line ~234). **Gap: not wired into compat mode — only the chip shows; add the convert button here.**

**Notes / gaps.** Distinct from 10.3.3 (`media-decode-failed`): here playback **succeeds** via transcode, so the warn is about the **ongoing cost**, not a broken state — hence `warn`, not `bad`.

#### 10.3.13 Not tracked — this file isn't inside a managed repo — `neutral` (id: entity-not-tracked)

*Where shown:* `ViewOneFilePage` (`/file`) per-file `StatusBanner` + the Sync card's `NotTracked` block. Deliberately **neutral** (not a warning) — included for completeness as a distinct per-file verdict state.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `v.repo === null`: `enclosingRepo(abs)` found no registered repo whose path encloses the file, so `fileVerdict()` returns `state:'neutral'`. This is the very first branch of `fileVerdict()`. *Computed in:* `ViewOneFilePage.tsx` — `fileVerdict()` no-repo branch (verified lines ~146–152) + `NotTracked` component (lines ~220–230); backend `enclosingRepo()` `entity.service.ts` (lines ~81–94; `repo` stays `null` on no match).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFBridge only syncs files **inside repos it manages**; this file is outside all registered repos, so it can't be pinned or synced. *Why it matters:* nothing is at risk from LFBridge's view — it's simply not something we back up until you register its folder. *Options:* none. *Action button:* none inline today; a "Register this folder as a repo" deep-link (pre-filled with the parent path) is the intended affordance. Being neutral/informational, this banner carries **no arrow button** unless we add the education popup.

**(C) The fix.** No per-file auto-fix. Manual next step: register the enclosing folder as a managed repo (repos module), then set the file's decision to `sync`. *Fix in:* repo registration lives in `backend/src/modules/units` / `repo` (not entity); the `NotTracked` link only navigates to `/fs` at the parent (`ViewOneFilePage.tsx` lines ~225–227). Note `setEntityDecision` **explicitly rejects** a non-repo file (`entity.service.ts` line ~359). **No entity auto-fix; routes to File System / Add-repo.**

**Notes / gaps.** Deliberately neutral, not a warning — do not color it amber. Its natural fix ("register a repo") is owned by the repos/units category.

#### 10.3.14 Cross-references — per-entity transcribe / AI-credentials / compress-blocked banners

Several per-entity banners **appear on** the file and media pages but are **owned by other §10 categories** — they are documented in full there, and only cross-referenced here so this category's inventory is complete:

* **`transcribe-tools-missing`** (`warn`) — shown in the `MediaViewer` Transcription column (band 6) for a video/audio file with no transcript when `api.transcribeTools()` reports `!tools.whisper`. Owned by the **transcription/AI category** — see that section for the setup fix (install Whisper).
* **`describe-needs-setup`** (`warn`) and **`ai-credentials-missing-for-description`** (`warn`) — shown from the per-entity "Generate description" action (`MediaViewer` / `/file`). `describe-needs-setup` fires when `resolveDescriptionPath().needsSetup` is true (no ancestor `storage.yaml`/`.lfbridge`/`.git` and no Personal storage) and opens the storage-setup wizard; `ai-credentials-missing-for-description` fires when `api.describeFile` returns `status:'no_provider'` (no `GEMINI_API_KEY`/`XAI_API_KEY`/`OPENAI_API_KEY` resolves; video specifically needs Gemini) and opens `CredentialsMissingDialog`. Both owned by the **AI-descriptions category** — see it for the wizard and provider-key fix.
* **`compress-blocked-alpha-video`** (`bad`), **`compress-resolution-changed-blocked`** (`warn`), and **`compress-blocked-or-skipped-result`** (`warn`) — surfaced as **result toasts** after a Compress/Convert attempt on `/image` or `/video` (alpha would be dropped from a video; the encode changed WxH so the temp was discarded per the charter's never-downscale invariant; or the size-gain guard skipped a not-smaller output). The transactional rule means the **original is never touched on a block**. All owned by **compression §10.5** — see it for the pre-flight `CompressCheck` (`alphaUsed`/`alphaSafe`/`warning`) and why these are today toast-only with **no pre-flight banner (gap)**.

**Notes / gaps.** Each of these fires on a single entity but belongs to its home category's registry entry (§8); a fix from either surface clears both (§9). The common gap across all three groups is the same as this whole section's theme: the condition is detected but surfaced as a toast or ad-hoc dialog rather than the standard §2 banner + §3 arrow + §4 educate-and-fix popup.

## 10.4 File System pages & big-file category rollup

The two File System surfaces — the **Miller-column browser** (`FileSystemPage`) and the flat recursive **Full Paths** large-file table (`FullPathsPage`) — plus the **View-one-directory category rollup table** (`ViewOneDirectoryPage`) are where a user browses real folders and meets big/uncompressed files. Today these pages carry only scattered inline amber/red strips and per-row badges; **none of them mounts the health-model `StatusBanner`** (§2) or its blue-arrow popup (§3–§4). This category catalogs every warnable condition on these pages, folds duplicate scanner verdicts into one canonical warning each, and ties rows 3 & 4 of the rollup to the charter's **Category Rollup Table** (§9). Several entries are flagged **gap: not wired** — they are conditions the backend already computes but the pages never surface.

Broken conditions first (a folder that can't be read or is off-limits), then the Improvable offers (truncation, uncompressed media, big-not-ignored, ignored-not-tracked, partial pin), then the structural gap that no fs page has a verdict banner at all.

#### 10.4.1 This folder can't be read — `bad` (id: fs-column-read-error)

*Where shown:* File System page (Miller-column browser) — small red text **inside the affected column body**, per-column, not a top-of-page banner. No icon, no headline, no Fix button; not rolled into any page verdict.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** A column's `GET /api/fs?path=<abs>` rejects. Backend `listDirectory` calls `fs.readdirSync(dirAbs, {withFileTypes:true})` inside try/catch; on **any** throw — `EACCES` (permission denied), `ENOENT` (folder vanished), `EPERM`, `EIO` — it logs the real errno and re-throws a **genericized** `new Error("cannot read directory")`; the router's `GET '/'` catch returns HTTP 400 `{ok:false,error:"cannot read directory"}`. It therefore fires whenever the OS denies or loses the directory **after** `resolveDir` already validated it exists — a TOCTOU race (folder moved / permission changed between `stat` and `readdir`), or a directory the process can `stat` but not enumerate. Frontend: `FsColumn`'s `useQuery` enters `q.isError` and renders `(q.error).message || "Cannot read directory"`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/fs.service.ts` — `listDirectory` readdir catch (lines 35–39, genericized message ~57–64) and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/fs.router.ts` — `GET '/'` catch (lines 141–150); frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FileSystemPage.tsx` — `FsColumn` `q.isError` branch (lines 260–264).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFBridge could not list this folder. Almost always this is a macOS permission wall (the app lacks **Full Disk Access** or hasn't been granted this folder under Files & Folders), or the folder was moved/removed while the column was open. *Why it matters:* Nothing is at risk — this is only a **read** failure, no file is altered or lost; you just can't browse into this folder until access is restored. *Options:* none — a one-click **Retry** plus a deep-link. *Action button:* "Retry" (re-fetch); the popup also links to **System Settings → Privacy & Security → Full Disk Access / Files and Folders**. Not dismissible — it's a live `bad` state, only clears when the read succeeds.

**(C) The fix.** No safe silent auto-fix — the app cannot grant itself macOS TCC permissions. Retry = `queryClient.invalidateQueries(['fs','list',root,showHidden])` to re-run the column query; no backend mutation. Manual next step: grant Full Disk Access, then Retry. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FileSystemPage.tsx` — Retry invalidates the `['fs','list',…]` query; no backend endpoint. Routes the user to the macOS Privacy pane for the actual grant.

**Notes / gaps.** The backend **deliberately genericizes** the message (`fs.service.ts` ~61–63) to `"cannot read directory"`, so the popup **cannot** distinguish `EACCES` vs `ENOENT` without a code change — *gap: surface the captured errno to the client*. This one red column string is **overloaded across three distinct causes**: this read failure and both `resolveDir` rejections (see §10.4.3 fs-path-not-allowed and §10.4.4 fs-path-not-found-or-not-dir) all reach the UI as the same generic red text via the router, so a reliable per-cause popup branch needs the server to pass a discriminator.

#### 10.4.2 Couldn't scan this folder for large files — `bad` (id: fullpaths-walk-error)

*Where shown:* Full Paths page (flat recursive large-file table) — a **red banner above the table** showing the raw error string. No icon, no headline, no Fix button.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The NDJSON stream `GET /api/fs/flat/stream` emits a terminal `{t:'error'}` event, captured by `useStreamedFlatListing` into `flat.error` and rendered as `rootError`. Backend `walkFilesFlatStreaming` throws before/at **root** resolution and the router catches it (`log.error` + `write({t:'error',error})`). The realistic trigger is `resolveDir` throwing at the ROOT — `"path not allowed"` / `"directory not found"` / `"not a directory"` / `"invalid path"` — because **per-subdirectory `readdir`/`stat` failures deeper in the walk are swallowed** (skipped silently) and never error the stream. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fsindex/fsindex.service.ts` — `walkFilesFlatStreaming` root `resolveDir` (line 58) and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/fs.router.ts` — `GET '/flat/stream'` catch (lines 121–125); frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — `rootError = flat.error` (line 272), banner (lines 492–496).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The recursive large-file scan of this root **failed to start**. Likely causes: the folder is outside the app's allowed browse roots, was moved/deleted, or sits behind a permission wall. *Why it matters:* No files were touched — this is a scan that couldn't begin, not a data operation; you simply have no large-file list for this root until it's resolved. *Options:* none — Retry plus a cause-dependent link. *Action button:* "Retry" (re-opens the stream); when the cause looks like `EACCES`, links to macOS folder-permission settings; when it's a confinement rejection, routes to Settings to **add the folder as a scanner/browse root**. Not dismissible.

**(C) The fix.** No silent auto-fix. Retry re-runs `useStreamedFlatListing` (re-set root / re-open stream). Root allow-listing is configuration, not a mutation: `scanner.roots` (or the `LFB_BROWSE_ROOTS` env) consumed by `allow-root.ts` `rawRoots`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/table/useStreamedFlatListing.ts` — client Retry; root config in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/allow-root.ts` — `rawRoots` (lines 50–72). No dedicated "add browse root" endpoint exists — routes to Settings.

**Notes / gaps.** Deep per-directory failures are **intentionally not errored** (`fsindex.service.ts` ~96–102 skips unreadable dirs) so a partial result returns silently — **a folder the user can't fully read shows FEWER rows with no warning at all**. *Gap: partial-permission subtrees are invisible;* consider a "some subfolders were skipped (permission)" warn count emitted from the walk. When the root rejection is specifically a confinement, this is the Full Paths surfacing of §10.4.3 (fs-path-not-allowed) — same underlying `resolveDir` throw.

#### 10.4.3 That folder is off-limits — `bad` (id: fs-path-not-allowed)

*Where shown:* File System page (generic red **column** text) and Full Paths page (red **walk-error banner**) — wherever the user typed or deep-linked the path. No explanation of *why*, no distinction between the two sub-causes.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `resolveDir → assertAllowedPath` throws `Error("path not allowed")` in **two** cases: (1) the canonicalized (realpath-resolved) path is **not under any allow-root** — home dir, `scanner.roots`, registered repo paths, detected cloud mounts, or `LFB_BROWSE_ROOTS`; or (2) any path **segment** is a denied secret name — `.ssh`, `.gnupg`, `.aws`, `.credentials`, `.password-store` — **or** the path falls under a denied prefix (`~/.ssh`, `~/.credentials`, `~/.aws`, `~/.gnupg`, `~/.config/gcloud`, `~/.kube`, `~/.docker`, `~/.password-store`, `~/Library/Keychains`). The message passes through the router to the generic column red text or the Full Paths red banner. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/allow-root.ts` — `assertAllowedPath` out-of-root throw (line 120), `DENY_SEGMENTS` set (line 105) and `deniedPrefixes` (lines 89–102) throws (lines 122–125); invoked from `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/paths.ts` — `resolveDir` (line 33).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* This is a **security confinement, not a bug**. The app only serves folders under your home directory, your configured scanner roots, your registered repos, and detected cloud mounts — and it **always** blocks secret stashes (SSH keys, cloud credentials, keychains, this app's own credentials) even when they live inside home. *Why it matters:* This protects your secrets from ever being enumerated, hashed, or bridged; a blocked secret folder is the policy working correctly, not a failure. *Options:* none for a secret-denylist hit; for an out-of-root folder, an offer to add it as a root. *Action button:* "Add this folder as a browse root" (out-of-root case only) → opens Settings to append to `scanner.roots`; for a **secret-denylist** hit the popup states plainly there is **no override** and offers no action button. Not dismissible.

**(C) The fix.** For a legitimate out-of-root folder: append it to `scanner.roots` (or set `LFB_BROWSE_ROOTS`), then re-resolve — **but no dedicated "add browse root" mutation endpoint exists in this partition (gap)**; it routes to a Settings config write. For a secret-denylist hit there is **no fix by design** — it must stay blocked. *Fix in:* config `scanner.roots` consumed by `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/allow-root.ts` — `rawRoots` (lines 60–65); secret denylist has no fix (`allow-root.ts` lines 89–105). No auto-fix — routes to Settings.

**Notes / gaps.** Both sub-causes share the single string `"path not allowed"`, so at the UI layer it is **indistinguishable** from each other and from the read-failure of §10.4.1 (all become generic red text via the router). *Gap: the popup cannot reliably branch "outside-root" vs "secret-denylist" without a server-side discriminator.* Charter tie: the secret denylist enforces the security posture that LFBridge never serves or bridges anyone's private key material.

#### 10.4.4 That path isn't a folder we can open — `warn` (id: fs-path-not-found-or-not-dir)

*Where shown:* File System page (column error) and Full Paths page (walk error) — after the user submits the path/jump box or restores a stale deep-link. Generic red text, no input-level validation, no suggestion.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `resolveDir` throws one of three: `"invalid path"` (path contains a NUL byte), `"directory not found"` (`statSync` fails — path doesn't exist), or `"not a directory"` (path exists but is a file / socket / device). Triggered by the Home/jump-to input (`FileSystemPage.jumpTo`, `FullPathsPage` root submit) or a **stale `?path` deep-link / restored column chain** pointing at something that no longer exists or was replaced by a file. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/paths.ts` — `resolveDir` (lines 28–42: invalid path line 32, directory not found line 38, not a directory line 40); frontend entry points `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FileSystemPage.tsx` — `jumpTo` (lines 143–149) and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — root form (lines 331–346).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The path you typed or linked to can't be opened — either it **doesn't exist** or it points at a **file, not a folder**. If it came from a saved column that went stale, the folder may have been moved or renamed. *Why it matters:* Nothing is broken with your files — this is a navigation dead-end; the saved view is just pointing somewhere that's gone. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Go Home" (reset root/stack to the home directory and clear the stale saved view); for a deep-link that resolves to a file, an alternate "Open this file" that navigates to the `/file` viewer. Dismissible as an offer since it's `warn`, but it re-fires if the same stale path is re-entered.

**(C) The fix.** No backend mutation. "Go Home" resets root/stack to `home.data.home` and clears the stale saved view; also invalidate `['fs','viewState']` since the saved-view loader already prunes stale paths server-side. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FileSystemPage.tsx` — `goHome` (lines 137–142); stale-view pruning in `fs-view.service` `loadFsView` (referenced `fs.router.ts` lines 20–30). No new endpoint.

**Notes / gaps.** `"invalid path"` (NUL byte) is effectively an attack/garbage guard and won't occur via normal typing. The realistic trigger is the **stale saved column** — directly relevant to this repo's Tower auto-commit context where folders move/rename under the app. This shares `resolveDir` with §10.4.3 but is `warn` (recoverable, not a confinement) vs `bad`.

#### 10.4.5 Folder narrowed — showing only the first 5,000 items — `warn` (id: fs-column-truncated)

*Where shown:* File System page — an **amber strip pinned at the top of the truncated column**. No Fix button, no popup today.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `listDirectory` stops after `FS_ENTRY_CAP` (**5000**) entries and sets `listing.truncated = true`. Fires only for a **single directory** with more than 5000 non-hidden children (or more than 5000 total with **Show hidden** on). Rows are sorted dirs-first then by name, so the first 5000 in that order are what's shown. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/fs.service.ts` — `FS_ENTRY_CAP` const (line 27) and truncation set (lines 79–82, cap check ~55); frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FileSystemPage.tsx` — `q.data.truncated` banner (lines 253–257).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* A **performance guard, not data loss** — this folder has more than 5,000 items and only the first 5,000 (sorted dirs-first, then name) are shown so the browser stays responsive. *Why it matters:* Nothing is hidden permanently; the remaining items are still on disk and reachable — you just need a narrower view to see them. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Open in Full Paths" — jumps to the Full Paths recursive table rooted at this dir (`/fs/full-paths?path=<dir>`), which surfaces the large files regardless of the per-directory cap; optionally surfaces the **Show hidden** toggle context. Dismissible offer.

**(C) The fix.** No destructive fix, no backend action — pure navigation. Re-roots the Full Paths page at this directory so large files deeper in are reachable. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — `setRoot` to this dir. No mutation endpoint.

**Notes / gaps.** Amber by design — an **offer to view differently, never an alarm**. The 5000 cap is **not user-tunable** in this partition.

#### 10.4.6 Large-file list capped — narrow the folder to see everything — `warn` (id: fullpaths-walk-truncated)

*Where shown:* Full Paths page — an **amber banner above the table**. No Fix button today.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `walkFilesFlatStreaming` sets `truncated = true` when **either** cap trips: (1) it has emitted `FLAT_FILE_CAP` (**5000**) rows, **or** (2) its directory-pop budget `FLAT_ITER_BUDGET` (**300000**) is exhausted before the tree finishes. The terminal `{t:'done',truncated:true}` sets `flat.truncated`. Case (2) means some large files deeper in the tree **may be missing** from the list. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fsindex/fsindex.service.ts` — `FLAT_FILE_CAP` (line 25), `FLAT_ITER_BUDGET` (line 26), budget truncation (lines 90–93), file-cap truncation (lines 121–124); frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — `flat.truncated` banner (lines 487–491).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Two different caps can trigger this — **either** more than 5,000 large files matched, **or** the folder tree was so large that the 300,000-directory walk budget ran out before finishing. *Why it matters:* It's a responsiveness guard (no data loss), but under the budget cap some large files deeper down may not appear, so an at-risk file could be missed. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Choose a narrower folder" (re-root at a deeper subfolder the user picks) plus a link to **Settings → big-file threshold** (raising the threshold reduces the match count). Dismissible offer.

**(C) The fix.** No destructive fix, no backend mutation — the caps are not exposed as user settings in this partition.
