Client re-roots at a deeper subfolder; the threshold link routes to Settings. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — `setRoot`; threshold in config `big_file.threshold_bytes` (referenced `fsindex.service.ts` line 61 via `buildBadgeContext`).

**Notes / gaps.** The banner **cannot currently tell which cap fired** (file-cap vs budget) — the summary only carries a boolean `truncated`. *Gap: distinguishing the two would let the popup give the right advice — "narrow the folder" for the file-cap vs "raise the threshold / some files may be missing" for the budget cap.*

#### 10.4.7 Uncompressed videos here can be shrunk — `warn` (id: fs-videos-uncompressed)

*Where shown:* File System page and Full Paths page — **only as per-row 'C' badges** today; the page-level offer sits in the action-links row ("Compress all videos…"), **not** a verdict banner. No amber banner and **no visible count** on either fs page.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `compressBadge` returns `'compress'` (the yellow **C** chip) for any file whose extension is in `VIDEO_EXT` **and** whose name does **not** match `VIDEO_COMPRESSED_MARK` (`compress|h264|x264|hevc|x265|av1|reenc|shrunk|small`). Suppressed to no badge when the entity — or an **ancestor directory** — carries the sticky `no_compress` flag (`effectiveFlag`). Full Paths can also filter to these via the **Compressed = Uncompressed** segmented control (`compressStateOf → 'uncompressed'`). A page-level rollup **count** exists as `DirRollup.videosToCompress` but is **not shown** on these two fs pages. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` — `VIDEO_EXT` (lines 23–25), `VIDEO_COMPRESSED_MARK` (line 39), `compressBadge` (lines 187–197), `no_compress` suppression in `computeBadges` (line 120); count in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `videosToCompress++` (line 275); frontend filter `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — `compressStateOf` (lines 66–67).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* These videos **look uncompressed** (by extension plus a filename heuristic) and could be re-encoded to **H.264** to save space — always an **OFFER**; nothing is altered unless you ask. *Why it matters:* Uncompressed video is the single biggest waste of disk and sync bandwidth; shrinking it saves space on every computer it syncs to. *Options:* none beyond opening the scoped dialog (the dialog itself carries the checkboxes). *Action button:* "Compress videos here" → opens the Compress-inside dialog scoped to the current directory with **videos pre-checked**. Dismissible offer. Note the heuristic is **name-based** — a truly-compressed file lacking a marker word can still show **C**.

**(C) The fix.** Opens the Compress-inside dialog scoped to the column browser's `currentDir` or the Full Paths root, with videos pre-checked; it re-encodes to **H.264/MP4** and **never deletes the original without explicit confirm**. A true batch "compress all videos under this root" endpoint **does not exist yet** — the dialog is the real path. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/menu/domainActions.tsx` — `compressAllVideos` (lines 26–41) → `openCompressInside(root,{videos:true})`; backend re-encode in `compression.service` (see §10.6 compression category). Falls back to a `notWiredToast` only when no root can be resolved (rare here, since both pages have a root).

**Notes / gaps.** *Gap: no page verdict banner and no visible count on the fs pages* — the amber "improvable" signal is only per-row. Charter tie: compression is a core value and the "how many look uncompressed" metric (`videosToCompress`) exists but isn't shown here.

#### 10.4.8 Images here can be compressed or converted — `warn` (id: fs-images-uncompressed)

*Where shown:* File System page and Full Paths page — per-row 'C' badges; the "Compress all images…" page offer is on the **column browser only**. Full Paths does **not** include a compress-images action. No banner, no count, no split between "shrink PNG/TIFF" and "convert HEIC for compatibility".

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `compressBadge` returns `'compress'` (**C**) for (1) `IMAGE_UNCOMPRESSED_EXT` — `.png .bmp .tif .tiff .gif` (lossless, genuinely shrinkable) — **and** (2) `IMAGE_CONVERT_EXT` — `.heic .heif .avif` (already byte-efficient but poorly supported, offered as a **compatibility** conversion to JPEG that **intentionally grows** the file). Suppressed by the `no_compress` flag (self or ancestor). Rollup count in `DirRollup.imagesToCompress` (not shown here). The image-driven folder-tint interest floor is **3 MB**, but the **C badge itself has no size floor**. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` — `IMAGE_UNCOMPRESSED_EXT` (line 27), `IMAGE_CONVERT_EXT` (line 37), `compressBadge` (lines 189–191), `compressInfo` mirror (lines 200–216); count `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `imagesToCompress++` (line 276).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Two very different offers share the one **C** badge — (1) lossless images (PNG/TIFF/BMP/GIF) can be recompressed/converted to JPEG/WebP to **save** space; (2) HEIC/HEIF/AVIF are already small but get an optional conversion to JPEG **for site compatibility that will INCREASE file size** — a compatibility trade, not a space win. *Why it matters:* The first saves disk and sync bandwidth; the second is only worth it when you need broad compatibility, and it costs space, so the two must not be conflated. *Options:* the dialog's per-type checkboxes; converting a **PNG with a real alpha channel loses transparency** — a safety check runs first and warns. *Action button:* "Compress images here" → Compress-inside with images pre-checked. Mark the HEIC-convert option as a compatibility trade (grows file); mark the PNG-alpha case as lossy → warn/confirm. Dismissible offer.

**(C) The fix.** Opens Compress-inside with images pre-checked. For HEIC it runs the **compatibility conversion** (grows the file, exempt from the size-gain guard via `formatConvert` — see MEMORY heic-jpeg-conversion). Before converting a PNG it **checks for a used alpha channel** and warns about transparency loss. No silent action, no batch endpoint — the dialog is the wired path. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/menu/domainActions.tsx` — `compressAllImages` (lines 44–59); alpha/size-gain checks in `compression.service` `pickImageTarget` (see §10.6, referenced `badges.ts` line 36).

**Notes / gaps.** *Gap: Full Paths' action-links row omits Compress-all-images* (only `compressAllVideos` is added there, ~line 291), so on Full Paths images can be compressed **per-row only**. *Gap: the C badge merges shrink-vs-compat-convert into one signal* — the popup is where the two must be separated. HEIC-grows and PNG-alpha behaviors are implemented outside this partition (compression category).

#### 10.4.9 Big files here aren't git-ignored — `warn` (id: fs-big-not-ignored)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not shown on the File System or Full Paths pages today.** The count exists only in the entity/directory rollup (and surfaces on the rollup table — see §10.4.12). The only related affordance on the fs pages is the "Git-ignore big files…" action-link, which is confirm-gated but fires `notWiredToast` (no batch endpoint).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** During the directory rollup walk, a file with `size >= big_file.threshold_bytes` that is **not** among the enclosing repo's git-ignore candidates (`candidateRel`) increments `bigNotIgnored` — i.e. a big file that would be **committed to git** instead of bridged over IPFS. This is `DirRollup` **category 3**. The two fs pages compute per-file repo/sync/compress badges but have **no badge or banner** for "big & committable," so the condition is invisible on exactly the pages that list the big files. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `bigNotIgnored++` (line 289, threshold gate ~283, `candidateRel` build lines 197–208); threshold from config `big_file.threshold_bytes` via `buildBadgeContext` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` (lines 54–75). **No detection wired into `FileSystemPage`/`FullPathsPage`.**

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Big files committed to git **bloat the repo forever** — every clone, on every computer, carries the full history of that blob. LFBridge's model is to **git-ignore** large files and sync them via IPFS instead. *Why it matters:* An un-ignored big file inflates the repo and slows every clone/pull; ignoring it removes it from **future** commits (existing history is untouched) and lets LFBridge bridge it instead. *Options:* show the **count and total size** of big-not-ignored files under this folder; scope = all N / selected rows. *Action button:* "Git-ignore these files" → appends the matching files to the enclosing repo's `.gitignore`. Per charter this is **confirm-gated and never automatic**. Dismissible offer.

**(C) The fix.** Should append the matching big files to the enclosing repo's `.gitignore` (one-click), after which they become sync candidates. **No batch endpoint exists yet** — `gitIgnoreBig()` currently only shows `notWiredToast`; today's real path is **per-file** git-ignore from a file's ⋯ menu (`setEntityDecision('ignore')`). Building the batch endpoint is the concrete backend work this Fix needs. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/menu/domainActions.tsx` — `gitIgnoreBig` (lines 62–80, confirm modal + `notWiredToast` — **not wired**); per-file ignore via `setEntityDecision('ignore')` (entity module); detection to reuse at `entity.service.ts` lines 283–290. No auto-fix — the batch path routes through the (unbuilt) endpoint.

**Notes / gaps.** *Gap: not wired on these pages at all* — the clearest "should exist but isn't surfaced" amber offer in this partition. **Charter is explicit: never auto-add a `.gitignore` entry — only surface and offer a one-click ignore.** Same underlying counter as the rollup-table row 3 (§10.4.12).

#### 10.4.10 Big git-ignored files aren't being synced — `warn` (id: fs-big-ignored-not-tracked)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not shown on the File System or Full Paths pages today.** The count exists only in the directory rollup (and rollup table row 4, §10.4.12). On the fs pages, a synced file shows the pink **S** badge; a big git-ignored file with **no S badge** is exactly this at-risk case, but nothing flags it as such.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** In the rollup walk, a big file (`size >= threshold`) that **is** a git-ignore candidate (`candidateRel.has(abs)`) but is **not** decided `'sync'` (`!candidateDecided.has(abs)`) and does **not** carry the `neverIpfs` flag increments `bigIgnoredNotTracked` — `DirRollup` **category 4**. Meaning: the file is correctly kept out of git, but LFBridge is **neither tracking nor bridging it**, so it exists on only **one** computer and would be **lost if that machine dies**. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `bigIgnoredNotTracked++` (line 287: `candidateRel.has && !candidateDecided && !flags.neverIpfs`); the inverse "S" signal in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` — `fileIsSynced` (lines 172–183) + `computeBadges` (line 112). **Not surfaced in `FileSystemPage`/`FullPathsPage`.**

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* These large files are git-ignored (good) but **not bridged over IPFS**, so they exist on only **this** computer. *Why it matters:* Lose this machine and you lose the files — this is the charter's core promise ("if you lose a laptop, your files are safely on your other computers") going unmet. *Options:* show the count/size; files marked **Never IPFS** are intentionally excluded and called out. *Action button:* "Track & sync these files" → marks the affected files `decision='sync'` (pin), which replicates them to your other computers. Dismissible offer.

**(C) The fix.** Marks the affected files `decision='sync'` (pin) — the Full Paths page already does this **per selection** via `api.setEntityDecision(path,'sync')`. Whole-directory track/sync is **not batch-wired** (`trackSyncDir → notWiredToast`); the real path today is: select the rows in Full Paths (or filter **IPFS = Not**) and click IPFS pin. The Fix should pre-select these rows and run that same mutation. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — pin `useMutation` (lines 243–270, `api.setEntityDecision(p,'sync')`); batch dir-track gap in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/menu/domainActions.tsx` — `trackSyncDir` (lines 83–95, `notWiredToast`).

**Notes / gaps.** *Gap: the highest-value at-risk signal is invisible on the fs pages.* A page verdict could roll `DirRollup.bigIgnoredNotTracked` into an amber "N files on only this computer" banner. Same counter feeds rollup-table row 4 (§10.4.12).

#### 10.4.11 Some files couldn't be pinned/unpinned — `warn` (id: fs-ipfs-pin-partial-skip)

*Where shown:* Full Paths page — currently a **sonner toast** after the pin/Unpin action (green success with a trailing ", skipped M"), **not** a banner. A hard-error toast covers total failure.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The pin mutation runs `api.setEntityDecision(path,decision)` for every selected path via `Promise.allSettled`; any **rejected** promise is counted as "skipped." Rejections happen when a file is **outside a registered repo** (no repo owns the decision, so there's nowhere to record it), has **Never-IPFS** set, or the endpoint errors. `onSuccess` toasts "Pinned N files, skipped M." The page contract (comment lines 4–6) is that such files are **reported skipped, never silently dropped**. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — pin `mutationFn` (lines 243–253, `Promise.allSettled`, skipped = rejected count at line 247), `onSuccess` toast (lines 254–268), `pinScope` guard (lines 277–286).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Some selected files were **skipped** when pinning — because they aren't inside a repo LFBridge manages (so there's no place to record the sync decision), or they're marked **Never IPFS**, or the per-file call failed. *Why it matters:* Skipped files were **left untouched** — they simply didn't get pinned, so they're still at risk of living on only one machine until you resolve why. *Options:* per-reason follow-ups (register the folder as a repo; clear Never-IPFS; retry transient failures). *Action button:* varies by reason — "Register this folder as a repo" (outside-repo), "Clear Never IPFS" (per file), or "Retry skipped" (transient). Dismissible offer.

**(C) The fix.** For "outside a repo": guide registering the enclosing folder as a repo (Repos page) so decisions can be stored, then retry the pin. For "Never IPFS": explain it's intentional and offer to clear the flag per file. For transient errors: a Retry that re-runs the mutation over **just the skipped paths**. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` — pin `mutate` (lines 243–270); per-file flag clear / repo registration live outside this partition (entity flags / repos module). No single auto-fix — routes per reason.

**Notes / gaps.** *Gap: the skipped reasons are lost* — `Promise.allSettled` only counts fulfilled vs rejected (line 247) and discards each rejection's `reason`, so the toast/popup **cannot say WHY** a file was skipped. Only a `warn`-level partial-success signal; total failure is the `onError` red toast.

#### 10.4.12 Big files not git-ignored / git-ignored-but-not-tracked (category rollup rows 3 & 4) — `warn` (id: big-files-rollup-ignore-track)

*Where shown:* **View-one-directory category rollup table** rows **3 & 4**, alongside the compressible-media rows. This is the **table form** of the charter's Category Rollup Table (§9) and the directory-level surfacing of §10.4.9 and §10.4.10. Each row shows a **count + a RowAction**. No top-of-page banner.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Same rollup counters as §10.4.9/§10.4.10, rendered as rows: **row 3** `bigNotIgnored` = big files (over `big_file.threshold_bytes`) that are **not** git-ignored → offer **"Git-ignore…"**; **row 4** `bigIgnoredNotTracked` = big files that **are** git-ignored but not yet tracked/synced by LFBridge and `!flags.neverIpfs` → offer **"Track / Sync"**. Row 4 is **hidden when the `neverIpfs` flag is set**. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `computeRollup` counters (lines 215–216 declared, 285–289 incremented); frontend rows `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/entity/ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` — rows (lines 47–48), `rollupMenu` RowActions (lines 101–113).

**(B) The popup.** *Row 3 — what this is:* Big files are best **git-ignored** — they sync via IPFS instead of bloating git history — offering a **one-click ignore** (charter: "never add a `.gitignore` entry automatically… we surface and offer"). *Row 4 — what this is:* These big files are git-ignored, so LFBridge is **not tracking, syncing, or backing them up** — they live on only this computer. *Why it matters:* Row 3 keeps the repo lean for every clone; row 4 gets the file replicated so a dead machine doesn't lose it. *Options:* count + scope per row. *Action buttons:* row 3 → "Git-ignore these"; row 4 → "Track & sync". Row 3's write is confirm-gated. Both dismissible offers.

**(C) The fix.** **Row 3** *should* add the `.gitignore` entry for the selected big files (one-click, per charter) — but on the rollup page it **currently punts** to a placeholder toast: "Git-ignore is offered per file — open in File System to review" (**gap: no real one-click ignore here**). **Row 4** navigates to `/fs` / sets `decision:'sync'` → adds to IPFS. Neither acts without a click. *Fix in:* track/sync via `api.setEntityDecision('sync')` — `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/entity/ViewOneFilePage.tsx` `decide` (lines 31–35); git-ignore endpoint referenced by `domainActions.gitIgnoreBig` (FullPathsPage) — **not wired on the directory rollup page** (routes to File System).

**Notes / gaps.** *Gap: "Git-ignore…" on the directory rollup is a placeholder toast, not the real one-click ignore.* This is the same missing batch git-ignore endpoint as §10.4.9. These rows share the same rollup table as the compressible-media counts (`videosToCompress`/`imagesToCompress`, §10.4.7/§10.4.8), making this the single Category Rollup Table the charter §9 describes.

#### 10.4.13 File System pages have no top-of-page health verdict — `warn` (id: fs-pages-no-verdict-banner)

*Where shown:* **GAP — spans the whole File System page and Full Paths page.** Neither renders `StatusBanner`, `FixButton`, or the health model; the only status surfaces are the localized inline amber/red strips catalogued above.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** This is a **structural absence**, not a runtime condition: neither `FileSystemPage` nor `FullPathsPage` imports or renders `StatusBanner` / `FixButton` / the health model, so the "am I OK?" verdict row every other page shows (use_cases.mdx §2) is **absent here**, and the `worst()` rollup of this partition's conditions (a read error/path rejection outranking any big-not-ignored/uncompressed offer) is never computed or shown. *Computed in (absence):* no `StatusBanner` import in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FileSystemPage.tsx` (imports lines 6–26) or `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/fs/FullPathsPage.tsx` (imports lines 7–52). Health model is available at `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/health.ts` — `worst()` (lines 10–12) and `StatusBanner` at `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/ui/StatusBanner.tsx`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Structurally N/A — **this finding IS the request to add the banner**. The banner it introduces is what would host the popups for every other finding in this partition (read-error/path-rejection as `bad`; big-not-ignored, ignored-not-tracked, uncompressed videos/images as amber offers) and compute the page verdict via `worst()`. *Why it matters:* Without it, the Fixed/Improvable/Broken verdict model this whole spec centers on is simply not mounted on the pages that list the user's big files, so nothing tells the user "am I OK?" at the top of these pages. *Options:* N/A. *Action button:* N/A (drives whatever the highest-severity live condition's action is).

**(C) The fix.** Mount a `StatusBanner` at the top of both fs pages that rolls up this partition's states with `health.worst()`: **bad** if the current directory/root errored or a path was rejected (§10.4.1–§10.4.3); **warn** if there are uncompressed videos/images (§10.4.7/§10.4.8), big-not-ignored (§10.4.9), or big-ignored-not-tracked (§10.4.10) counts — pulled from `DirRollup` for the current root; **ok/neutral** otherwise. The banner's single blue-arrow popup + Fix button drives the highest-severity condition's action (Retry / add browse root / open Compress-inside / one-click git-ignore / pin). *Fix in:* wire `StatusBanner` (`~/.../components/ui/StatusBanner.tsx`) + `worst()` (`~/.../components/ui/health.ts`) into `FileSystemPage.tsx` and `FullPathsPage.tsx`; source the amber counts from `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `computeRollup`/`computeDirRollup` (lines 213–316) for the current root. No auto-fix — this is the wiring work itself.

**Notes / gaps.** *Overarching gap for the partition:* the per-row badges and the not-wired action-links exist, but the verdict banner model the whole warnings spec centers on is not mounted on either fs page — so every warning above (10.4.1–10.4.11) currently has nowhere to live at the top of the page. This is the umbrella fix that lands all the others behind one blue arrow.

## 10.5 Compression & media conversion

This category owns every warning about **shrinking, converting, or refusing to touch media files** — the charter's core compression value (detect-and-offer, *never* alter without an explicit ask, and always run the PNG/alpha safety check before a lossy convert). All of it is computed by two backend modules — the badge/verdict layer `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` (is this file "should" or "done"?) and the engine `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` (the actual encode, the guards, the refusals) — plus the video-playback path in `.../modules/media/transcode.service.ts`. The offers surface on `MediaViewer`, the `ViewOneDirectoryPage` rollup table, and the `CompressInsideDialog`. Ranked Broken → Improvable → neutral. A recurring cross-cutting **gap** runs through this whole category: the real, alpha-aware, size-aware truth is computed in the backend (`checkFile` / `GET /compress/check`) but almost none of the educational **blue-arrow WarningPopup** surfaces are wired yet — today the user gets amber badges and terse toasts, not the §4 educate-and-fix popup.

#### 10.5.1 A required compression / conversion tool isn't installed — `bad` (id: compress-tool-missing)

*Where shown:* pre-compress dry-run (`checkFile.action = "needs <tool>"`) and the failed-compress toast in `MediaViewer` (`bad` when it blocks a run the user asked for); also passively on **Settings → Tools** per-row (`warn` for optional compression tools, `bad` only for the required `node`). Merges the backend and Tools-page duplicates and the HEIC-specific `libheif-missing-for-heic`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `detectTools()` probes `PATH` via `which`/`onPath()` for `magick`, `ffmpeg`, `ffprobe`, `oxipng`, `cjpeg`, `jpegoptim`, `cwebp`. When the tool the chosen plan needs is absent, `pickImageTarget`/`pickVideoTarget` return `{ toolMissing: "<tool> (brew install …)" }` (each string embeds its own brew command): `ffmpeg` for any video, `ImageMagick` for most images + HEIC, `oxipng` for lossless PNG, `cwebp` for WebP. `checkFile` surfaces `action = "needs <tool>"` and `compressFile` returns `status:"failed"` reason `needs <tool>`. **HEIC special case (`libheif`):** `magickSupportsHeif()` is false when neither `heif-dec`/`heif-convert` is on `PATH` nor ImageMagick's `-list format` advertises heic/heif → `detectTools().heif=false` → the HEIC branch returns `toolMissing:"libheif for ImageMagick (brew install imagemagick libheif)"`. This probe is **memoized for the process lifetime** (`_heifSupport`), so a fresh install needs an app restart to be seen. Video-with-no-ffmpeg is the hardest case: no video compression at all. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `detectTools()` (L116–133), `onPath()` (L84–90), `magickSupportsHeif()` (L96–114), the `toolMissing` gates throughout `pickImageTarget`/`pickVideoTarget` (L294–380), `compressFile` fail path (L483, L503); frontend rows in `.../frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` — `buildRows()` (L220–270), `ToolRowView` (L279).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* names the exact missing CLI and its role — ffmpeg = video, ImageMagick = most images + HEIC, oxipng = lossless PNG, cwebp = WebP, libheif = reading Apple HEIC photos — and states plainly that **the app never installs software itself as a side effect**. *Why it matters:* without the tool the compress/convert offer can't run; compression is simply disabled for that type, though scan and sync still work (optional vs. required tooling). *Options:* none — one-click. *Action button:* "Install <tool>" (runs the package-manager job on macOS/Windows) or, where no package manager exists (Linux/other), the button copies the exact brew command rather than executing it.

**(C) The fix.** On the Tools page the Fix triggers `startInstall` (`brew install ffmpeg`/`imagemagick`/`oxipng`/`webp`, or `winget`), streams the install log, and on success **re-probes** `detectTools()` so the compress offer goes live. There is **no** in-context installer from the compress toast today — a blocked run only toasts "Compression failed: needs …" with no deep link. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` — `startInstall` mutation (~L55–65) + `brew()` command (L220–221); re-probe endpoint `compression.router.ts` `GET /tools` (L21–23) → `detectTools()`.

**Notes / gaps.** The app must **never run an installer silently** — the button executes an explicit, user-clicked package-manager job (Tools page) or just shows the copyable command; it does not phone home. **Gap:** an in-context compress attempt that hits `toolMissing` produces only a toast — it should deep-link to Tools and compress banners should reflect the out-of-tools state ("Install ffmpeg to enable video compression"). `_heifSupport` caching means a post-install restart is required for HEIC.

#### 10.5.2 Browser can't play this codec and ffmpeg isn't installed — `bad` (id: media-stream-needs-ffmpeg)

*Where shown:* the `MediaViewer` video canvas `UnplayableCard`, when native `<video>` decode **and** the on-the-fly server transcode both fail. Distinct from 10.5.1 (this is the *playback* path, not the compress engine) and from 10.5.13 (the convert *offer*, which requires ffmpeg to exist).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The viewer falls back from native decode to `GET /api/media/stream`; `streamPlayable` returns **HTTP 503** `{"ffmpeg not installed — install it (brew install ffmpeg) to stream this codec"}` when `hasFfmpeg()` is false. When ffmpeg *is* present, `planStream` inspects ffprobe output and picks `copy` / remux-audio / transcode based on whether the streams are browser-safe (`SAFE_VCODEC`/`SAFE_PIXFMT`/`SAFE_ACODEC`: HEVC, ProRes, 10-bit, 4:2:2, or AC-3/DTS/PCM audio are **not** browser-safe). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/media/transcode.service.ts` — `hasFfmpeg()` (L28–30), `streamPlayable` 503 (L142–144), `planStream` (L92–110), safe-set constants (L37–40); frontend `UnplayableCard` in `.../frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` (L816–846).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the file uses a codec/pixel-format the browser can't decode (HEVC/ProRes/10-bit); LFBridge can live-stream a browser-safe copy but that needs ffmpeg; and this same-origin streaming is **your own file to your own browser — not an IPFS gateway** (charter no-relay policy). *Why it matters:* without ffmpeg you can neither preview the video in-app nor produce a shareable copy. *Options:* none — one-click. *Action button:* "Install ffmpeg" (routes to Tools, 10.5.1) — and the card separately offers "Convert to H.264 (MP4)…" (10.5.13) as the permanent, seekable path.

**(C) The fix.** No auto-install. `brew install ffmpeg` enables live streaming (a forward-only pipe, `Accept-Ranges: none`, no seeking). The seekable/shareable path is instead the on-disk H.264 convert: "Convert to H.264 (MP4)…" → `POST /api/compress/file {path, videoCodec:"h264"}`. *Fix in:* `transcode.service.ts` `streamPlayable` (L141–184); convert offer → `compression.router.ts` `POST /file` (L52–66). No auto-fix for the ffmpeg install itself — routes to `ToolsPage`.

**Notes / gaps.** Live transcode has no seeking by design; the H.264 on-disk convert is the way to seek and to upload. Ties to charter no-relay/gateway-off: streaming is same-origin to the user's own browser only.

#### 10.5.3 Compression blocked — video has a used alpha channel the codec can't keep — `bad` (id: compress-blocked-alpha-video)

*Where shown:* red toast after a compress attempt (`MediaViewer` `reportCompress` "blocked" branch). No banner, no popup, no guided resolution today. Merges the video branch of `alpha-would-be-lost`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** For **video**, `checkFile` derives `alphaUsed` from the ffprobe `pix_fmt` via `pixFmtHasAlpha()` (matches `yuva*`, `rgba`, `argb`, `ya8`, …). If `alphaUsed === true` and the chosen target codec (H.264 / HEVC / AV1 — every `VIDEO_TARGETS` entry is `alpha:false`) can't keep it, then `alphaSafe=false`, `eligible=false`, a warning is set, and `compressFile` returns `status:"blocked"`. The transactional rule guarantees the **original is never touched** on a block. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `pixFmtHasAlpha()` (L237–241), video branch of `checkFile()` (L415–427, `alphaSafe` L422, warning L426), `compressFile` block guard (L484), `VIDEO_TARGETS` all `alpha:false` (L249–253); frontend `reportCompress` blocked branch in `.../frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` (L861–862).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the video has a genuinely-**used** transparency (alpha) channel, and the compression codecs are opaque-only, so compressing would destroy the transparency — LFBridge refused rather than damage the file, and nothing was changed. Note it's rare (mostly ProRes 4444 / animation renders). *Why it matters:* an accepted compress would have silently flattened transparency onto a background — permanent data loss. *Options:* none that preserve alpha — the popup educates only. *Action button:* no destructive one-click; offer "Do not compress" to stop re-offering. **Never** present a one-click that would flatten alpha.

**(C) The fix.** No safe auto-fix — refusing is the correct behavior (charter: warn before losing alpha data). Manual next steps: keep the file as-is; or (advanced) deliberately choose a codec/container that preserves alpha; or set the per-file "Do not compress" flag. *Fix in:* intentional refusal in `compression.service.ts` `compressFile()` (L484); suppress future offers via `setEntityFlags {noCompress:true}` — `.../frontend/src/api/client.ts` (L221). No auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** This is the **hard-block** counterpart to the image alpha case (10.5.8) which merely *steers* to WebP — video has no alpha-safe target in `VIDEO_TARGETS`, so it blocks outright. Gap: surfaced only as a transient red toast, no persistent banner/popup.

#### 10.5.4 Compression refused — it would have changed the resolution — `bad` (id: resolution-changed-refusal)

*Where shown:* red "Compression blocked: refused: resolution changed …" toast after a compress attempt (`reportCompress` blocked branch). Not a banner. Merges `compress-resolution-changed-blocked` (the backend labels the same event a `warn`-tone "blocked"; the frontend shows it red) — it is a **protective refusal**, not data loss.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** With `preserveResolution` on (the default), after the encode completes to a temp file, if the input dimensions differ from the output dimensions (`inDims.w !== outDims.w || inDims.h !== outDims.h`) the temp is discarded and `compressFile` returns `status:"blocked"`, reason `refused: resolution changed WxH → WxH`. This enforces the charter §5 invariant that LFBridge **never silently downscales**. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — resolution guard in `compressFile()` (L528–533, condition at L530), `preserveResolution` setting (L45 read / L64 write); frontend `reportCompress` blocked branch `MediaViewer.tsx` (L861–862).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the encoder produced different pixel dimensions than the source, so LFBridge threw the result away and kept the original untouched — a safety guarantee, not a failure of your file (usually an odd-dimension / pixel-format edge the encoder rounded). *Why it matters:* it protects you from an unasked-for downscale/aspect change to your media. *Options:* none. *Action button:* none destructive — educate + "keep original" (already the outcome); optionally "Do not compress" to stop retrying.

**(C) The fix.** No safe auto-fix that preserves the invariant. Manual: keep the original; try a different target codec/quality; or, if the user genuinely wants a downscale, that's a separate deliberate action (e.g. the AI-description compress-to-fit ladder), not this engine. *Fix in:* intentional refusal at `compression.service.ts` `compressFile()` (L528–533). No auto-fix — routes to leaving the file as-is.

**Notes / gaps.** Should almost never fire for a correctly-built encode command — it is defense-in-depth alongside the alpha-block (10.5.3) and no-gain-skip (10.5.15) transactional refusals. The two source partitions disagreed on severity (backend `warn` / frontend `bad`); presented as `bad` to match the red toast, but framed as a healthy refusal.

#### 10.5.5 This video looks uncompressed — offer to compress — `warn` (id: uncompressed-video-can-compress)

*Where shown:* `MediaViewer` action bar + property grid (amber "Compress…" button), the directory-browser "C" badge, `ViewOneFilePage` Compression card, and the `ViewOneDirectoryPage` category-rollup row "Videos that can be compressed". Merges the frontend rollup `uncompressed-media-can-be-shrunk` (video half).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** A file whose extension is in `VIDEO_EXT` **and** whose **name does NOT** match `VIDEO_COMPRESSED_MARK` = `/(compress|h264|x264|hevc|x265|av1|reenc|shrunk|small)/i` → `compressState:"should"`. In the viewer, `canOfferCompress(v) = v.compressState==="should" && !v.flags.noCompress`. **Pure filename + extension heuristic — size is ignored** for the per-file "C" badge. The **directory rollup** count `videosToCompress` increments only when `compressState==="should"` **AND** `!flags.noCompress` **AND** `size >= COMPRESS_FLOOR_BYTES` (1 MiB) — so a sub-1 MiB video can show a "C" badge that the rollup count ignores (a real badge-vs-count mismatch). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` — `compressBadge()` (L187–197, `VIDEO_COMPRESSED_MARK` L39, `VIDEO_EXT` L23–25) + `compressInfo()` (L200–216); rollup in `.../backend/src/modules/entity/entity.service.ts` — `computeRollup` (L213–312, floor const L189, increment L274–276); frontend `canOfferCompress()` `MediaViewer.tsx` (L852–854), rollup rows `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` (L43–50).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFBridge found a video not yet known to be compressed and **offers** — never automatically — to re-encode it at medium quality **keeping the same resolution and aspect ratio**; the original moves to a recoverable LFBridge trash (or hard-delete per the per-run radio). It may report "no gain" if already efficient. *Why it matters:* uncompressed video is the biggest sync/storage cost across your computers; shrinking it saves space and IPFS transfer. *Options:* radio **"Move original to LFBridge trash (recoverable)"** vs **"Hard delete original"**; checkbox **"Do not compress this file"** to silence future offers. *Action button:* "Compress".

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/compress/file {path}` for one file, or `POST /api/compress/inside {root, images, videos, recursive, deleteOriginal}` for a whole directory (backgrounds a per-file-safe batch, toasts the queued count). The engine runs an ffmpeg libx264/libx265 CRF encode to a temp file, verifies resolution unchanged **and** a real size gain, then disposes the original and stamps the in-file `LFBcompressed` marker. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.router.ts` — `POST /file` (L52–66), `POST /inside` (L83–103) → `compression.service.ts` `compressFile()` (L470–587); directory dialog wiring `.../frontend/src/lib/compressInside.ts` `openCompressInside()`.

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap (shared with 10.5.6):** `ViewOneDirectoryPage` has **no top-of-page StatusBanner** — the rollup counts should roll up into an amber Improvable banner ("12 videos + 4 images can be compressed", per use_cases.mdx §1 worst-of rollup) but that isn't wired; the only surface is the rollup table. The "should" verdict is a **filename heuristic only** (see 10.5.14): an already-compressed video lacking a marker word (e.g. `clip.mp4`) falsely reads "should" — but the in-file `isAlreadyCompressed` marker makes the actual run a cheap skip, so the false positive costs one probe, not a re-encode. **Charter tie:** never alter without an explicit ask — this is strictly detect-and-offer.

#### 10.5.6 This image looks uncompressed — offer to compress/convert — `warn` (id: uncompressed-image-can-compress)

*Where shown:* `MediaViewer` amber "Compress…" offer + property grid, directory "C" badge, `ViewOneFilePage` Compression card, `ViewOneDirectoryPage` rollup row "Images that can be compressed". Merges the image half of `uncompressed-media-can-be-shrunk`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Extension in `IMAGE_UNCOMPRESSED_EXT` (`.png/.bmp/.tif/.tiff/.gif`) → `compressState:"should"`. HEIC/HEIF/AVIF also read "should" but are the *compatibility-conversion* case (see 10.5.7). Two floors matter: for the **per-file "C" offer there is no size floor**; for **folder "interesting" coloring** an image must be ≥ `IMAGE_INTEREST_FLOOR_BYTES` (3 MB) to light a folder; and the **directory rollup count** uses the 1 MiB `COMPRESS_FLOOR_BYTES`. So a folder of tiny PNG icons stays quiet while each icon can still carry a badge. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` — `IMAGE_UNCOMPRESSED_EXT` (L27), `IMAGE_INTEREST_FLOOR_BYTES` (L30), `compressBadge()` (L190), `compressInfo()` (L206), `computeDirInterest()` image floor (L366); rollup increment `entity.service.ts` `computeRollup` (L274–276).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* explains lossless recompress (oxipng for PNG, keeps the format) vs. re-encode/convert to WebP/JPEG per the codec prefs, that **resolution is preserved**, and that a PNG with **real transparency is steered to an alpha-safe target** (see 10.5.8) — it is never silently flattened. Mentions the 3 MB folder-interest floor so a folder of tiny PNG icons not lighting up is understood. *Why it matters:* uncompressed images (especially large PNG/TIFF) bloat storage and sync; lossless recompress is free savings. *Options:* trash-vs-hard-delete radio; "Do not compress" checkbox. *Action button:* "Compress".

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/compress/file {path}` → `pickImageTarget()` chooses oxipng lossless (PNG kept) / cwebp / ImageMagick per `convert_types` + `prefer` + `deny`; the size-gain guard keeps the original if there's no gain. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `pickImageTarget()` (L294–364), `imageCommand()` (L589–634); router `POST /file` (L52–66).

**Notes / gaps.** Interest floor (3 MB) is higher than the 1 MiB compress floor so small icons stay quiet. **Gap:** the badge (no floor) vs. rollup count (1 MiB) mismatch can confuse — a badge shows while the count says 0. Shares the missing-top-banner gap with 10.5.5.

#### 10.5.7 HEIC/HEIF/AVIF — offer a JPEG compatibility conversion — `warn` (id: heic-compatibility-conversion)

*Where shown:* the same "C"/"looks uncompressed"/rollup surfaces as any compressible image (`compressState:"should"`). Merges the backend `heic-compatibility-convert-offer` and frontend `heic-compatibility-conversion`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Extension in `IMAGE_CONVERT_EXT` (`.heic/.heif/.avif`) → `compressState:"should"` (badges.ts L208), so it counts as compressible. These are already byte-efficient, so we **offer** conversion only for *compatibility* (many sites/browsers can't display HEIC). Governed by the `convert_types` setting: with `convertTypes` OFF there is no in-place compressor for the type, so `checkFile` returns skip "conversion is turned off in settings". `pickImageTarget`'s HEIC branch requires libheif (`tools.heif` via the memoized `magickSupportsHeif()` probe) and routes to **JPEG** — unless `alphaUsed===true` (→ lossless **WebP**, keeps alpha) or JPEG is denied. The plan is marked `formatConvert:true`, which **exempts it from the size-gain guard** (see 10.5.11) so the output may be **larger** than the source. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `HEIC_FAMILY_EXT` (L74), `magickSupportsHeif()`/`_heifSupport` (L96–114), `pickImageTarget` HEIC branch (L316–334), `formatConvert` flag (L287), primary-still-only decode `imageCommand` (L604–611), size-gain exemption (L535–541); badge classification `badges.ts` `IMAGE_CONVERT_EXT` (L37), `compressBadge`/`compressInfo` (L191/L208).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* HEIC/HEIF/AVIF are already-efficient modern formats; LFBridge offers a JPEG copy for **universal compatibility, not to shrink** — the file **MAY get larger**, and that's expected and allowed (exempt from the "must get smaller" guard). A HEIC container can hold a primary image + thumbnails + depth/aux images + a Live-Photo motion clip; LFBridge decodes **only the primary still** (`file.heic[0]`, `-auto-orient`) — thumbnails, depth/aux, and the motion clip are **dropped**. If transparency is used it converts to lossless WebP instead (keeps alpha). *Why it matters:* you get a file every site can display, at the cost of possibly more bytes and the loss of the Live-Photo/depth extras. *Options:* checkbox acknowledging "May grow / drops motion+depth"; trash-vs-hard-delete radio. *Action button:* "Convert to JPEG" (confirm the intent is compatibility, not savings).

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/compress/file {path}` (or compress-inside). Requires `convertTypes=true` **AND** libheif; reads only the primary still via `magick "file.heic[0]" -auto-orient`; targets JPEG, or lossless WebP when alpha is used. If libheif/ImageMagick is absent the plan returns `toolMissing` → deep-link to Settings → Tools (10.5.1) rather than fail silently. *Fix in:* `compression.service.ts` `imageCommand()` HEIC branch (L604–611), `pickImageTarget` (L316–334); tool install path `.../frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx`.

**Notes / gaps.** Passes no `--with-aux`/coalesce, so no aux/depth/motion frame is ever selected. **Compliance/labeling gap:** counting HEIC as "can be compressed" is arguably misleading since it typically won't shrink — the count/label conflate "shrink" and "convert for compatibility"; consider a distinct category/label. See MEMORY `heic-jpeg-conversion` (intentional growth via the `formatConvert` exemption).

#### 10.5.8 This PNG uses transparency — converting to JPEG would lose it — `warn` (id: png-alpha-would-lose-transparency)

*Where shown:* **GAP — currently surfaced nowhere in the UI.** Should appear on the single-file/`MediaViewer` compress offer and inside `CompressInsideDialog`. Merges the image branch of `alpha-would-be-lost`. This is the charter's **mandated PNG-alpha safety check**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** For images, `imageAlphaUsed()` runs `magick identify -format %[opaque]`; `alphaUsed===true` means **real, used** transparency (an opaque image → false). If `alphaUsed!==false` and the chosen target has no alpha (jpeg/jpeg2000), `checkFile` sets `warning="would lose transparency — steering to an alpha-safe target"`; the planner then **auto-steers away** — `pickImageTarget` skips no-alpha targets when `alphaUsed!==false` (L340) and routes HEIC-with-alpha to lossless WebP or skips (L320–324). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `imageAlphaUsed()` (L217–235), `pixFmtHasAlpha()` (L237–241), image branch of `checkFile()` (L402–414, warning L412), alpha steering in `pickImageTarget` (L340–344). The result is exposed as `GET /compress/check` → `CompressCheck{alphaUsed, alphaSafe, warning}`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* this image has a **real (used)** alpha channel; converting to JPEG would flatten transparency onto a background and lose it permanently. LFBridge instead keeps it lossless (WebP with alpha) or skips it rather than destroy data — per charter "check whether the alpha channel is actually used … warn that conversion will lose that transparency data." *Why it matters:* silent transparency loss is irreversible data loss on the user's asset. *Options:* proceed with the alpha-**safe** plan (lossless WebP, keeps alpha) — default; or, if the user insists on JPEG, an **explicit confirm** acknowledging transparency loss (destructive → red button). *Action button:* "Convert (keep transparency)" — or the red "Flatten to JPEG (lose transparency)" only behind confirm.

**(C) The fix.** The Fix should call `GET /compress/check` for the file and either (a) proceed with the alpha-safe plan via `api.compressFile`, or (b) require the explicit lossy confirm. **No safe silent auto-fix — surface the choice.** If ImageMagick is missing (alpha can't be verified) offer to install it (Tools, 10.5.1). *Fix in:* backend truth already computed at `compression.service.ts` `checkFile()` (L383–428) + `pickImageTarget()` (L294–364); frontend client `.../frontend/src/api/client.ts` `compressCheck` (L233) — **currently uncalled**; must be wired into `CompressInsideDialog` / `MediaViewer`.

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap: not yet wired** — `api.compressCheck` has **zero callers** in the frontend (grep of pages/components/lib returns nothing), so the user never sees the alpha verdict before compressing. The backend fully implements the charter's required pre-convert alpha check; no UI consumes it. High-value safety warning. Distinct from 10.5.3 (video hard-block) — images *steer*, video *blocks*.

#### 10.5.9 "PNG files will be turned into JPEG" — the blunt static dialog warning — `warn` (id: png-to-jpeg-lossy-static-warning)

*Where shown:* inline red text under the Images checkbox in the compress-inside pop-over (`CompressInsideDialog`).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Purely UI-conditional: the red `AlertTriangle` line renders whenever the **Images checkbox is checked** (`images===true`). It is **NOT gated on any file inspection** — it fires even if the directory contains zero PNGs, or only PNGs with real alpha (where the backend would actually steer to WebP, never JPEG). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/compress/CompressInsideDialog.tsx` — the `{images && (…)}` block (L92–98), using `var(--lfb-bad)`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* educate that with `convert_types` ON, PNG/BMP/TIFF/GIF get re-encoded and a PNG **may** become JPEG (lossy) or WebP; JPEG is lossy and discards an **unused** alpha channel; and the backend actually **protects** transparency — a PNG whose alpha is genuinely used is steered to lossless WebP or skipped, **never silently flattened**. Clarify the warning is precautionary, not per-file. *Why it matters:* lossy re-encode is irreversible; the user should know which files are actually affected. *Options:* trash-vs-hard-delete radio for originals. *Action button:* "Continue".

**(C) The fix.** No destructive auto-fix here — it's a pre-flight warning inside the offer dialog; the real safety happens server-side (the alpha check, 10.5.8). To make it honest, the dialog **should** call `GET /compress/check` per candidate (or a batch check) and show the **actual per-file plan** (→JPEG vs →WebP vs lossless PNG recompress) and the count of PNGs-with-alpha that will be steered/skipped. *Fix in:* backend already computes the truth — `compression.service.ts` `checkFile()` (L383–428) + `pickImageTarget()` (L294–364), exposed as `api.compressCheck` → `GET /compress/check`.

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap:** the warning is a blunt static string, not driven by real content — the precise, alpha-aware `CompressCheck` exists in the backend but the dialog ignores it. Pair the fix with 10.5.8's wiring.

#### 10.5.10 Can't tell if this image uses transparency (ImageMagick missing) — `warn` (id: alpha-unknown-no-imagemagick)

*Where shown:* the pre-compress dry-run in the viewer (a warning string in the `checkFile` payload).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `imageAlphaUsed()` returns **null** when ImageMagick (`magick`/`convert`) is absent (`tools.magick` false). `checkFile` then sets `warning="alpha usage unknown (ImageMagick not installed) — treating conservatively"`, and because the planner treats `alphaUsed!==false` as "may have alpha," it **refuses no-alpha targets** (avoids JPEG). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `imageAlphaUsed()` returns null if `!tools.magick` (L217–218), warning in `checkFile()` (L412), `detectTools()` (L116–127).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* ImageMagick isn't installed, so LFBridge can't inspect the alpha channel and plays it safe by avoiding formats that would drop transparency. Installing ImageMagick unlocks JPEG conversion **and** accurate alpha detection. *Why it matters:* these files may only ever lossless-recompress (never convert to the smaller JPEG) until the tool is present. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Install ImageMagick" (→ Tools, 10.5.1).

**(C) The fix.** No auto-fix (the app installs no software on its own). Manual: `brew install imagemagick`; re-running `detectTools()` (`GET /api/compress/tools`) then reflects it. *Fix in:* `compression.router.ts` `GET /tools` (L21–23) → `detectTools()` (L116–127). No auto-fix — routes to `ToolsPage`.

**Notes / gaps.** Conservative treatment is intentional (charter alpha-safety) — better to under-shrink than to lose transparency we couldn't verify.

#### 10.5.11 A compatibility conversion may make the file BIGGER — `warn` (id: size-gain-exemption-may-grow)

*Where shown:* the HEIC→JPEG / forced-H.264 conversion result (informational verdict / property grid after convert).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** When `plan.formatConvert===true` (HEIC/HEIF/AVIF→JPEG/WebP, or a forced video codec), `compressFile` **skips** the "output must be smaller" guard (`afterBytes>=beforeBytes`) that every ordinary compress enforces — so the output can legitimately be larger than the source. Only these two conversion classes are exempt. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `formatConvert` set in `pickImageTarget` (L322/L328/L331) and the Plan doc (L282–288), the exemption `if (!plan.formatConvert && … afterBytes>=beforeBytes) skip` (L535–541), `pickVideoTarget` force path (L370–373).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the conversion's purpose is **compatibility / universal playback, not shrinkage**, so unlike a normal compress it's allowed to increase byte size — and it shows the before→after delta so the user isn't surprised the JPEG is bigger than the HEIC. *Why it matters:* the user should understand they traded bytes for compatibility, deliberately. *Options:* if the user only wanted shrinkage, checkbox "Keep the smaller original and discard the conversion." *Action button:* none required (intended behavior) — or "Keep original instead."

**(C) The fix.** No fix needed — intended behavior. Optional: keep the smaller original and discard the conversion (the original is already in LFBridge trash and recoverable via `trashOriginal()`). *Fix in:* `compression.service.ts` `trashOriginal()` (L438–450) as the recovery source. No auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** Every non-conversion compress still requires a real size gain or the original is left untouched (10.5.15) — this exemption is narrowly scoped to the two compatibility-convert classes (HEIC family, forced video codec).

#### 10.5.12 cwebp can't read GIF/BMP — WebP conversion needs ImageMagick — `warn` (id: cwebp-gif-bmp-routing)

*Where shown:* internal to the compress engine; surfaces to the user **only** as a tool-missing failure if ImageMagick is *also* absent. Included for completeness — mostly a correctness guard, not usually user-facing.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `cwebp`'s decodable set is `CWEBP_READABLE = {.png,.jpg,.jpeg,.tif,.tiff,.webp}`. A GIF/BMP targeting WebP would fail cwebp ("Cannot read input picture file"), so `imageCommand()` **gates the cwebp branch on `CWEBP_READABLE.has(srcExt)`** and otherwise falls through to the ImageMagick branch (which decodes GIF/BMP and coalesces multi-frame GIF → animated WebP). If ImageMagick is **also** missing, the WebP plan returns `toolMissing`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `CWEBP_READABLE` (L256–257), `imageCommand` cwebp gate (L617–628), `pickImageTarget` webp tool gate (L342).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* if it surfaces at all — a GIF/BMP→WebP needs ImageMagick (cwebp alone can't read those); offer the brew command. Otherwise **no popup** — the routing is automatic and correct. *Why it matters:* only matters when neither cwebp's path nor ImageMagick is present. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Install ImageMagick" (→ Tools).

**(C) The fix.** No auto-fix. Manual: `brew install imagemagick` (and/or `brew install webp`); `GET /api/compress/tools` reflects presence. *Fix in:* `compression.service.ts` `imageCommand()` (L617–633). No auto-fix — routes to `ToolsPage`.

**Notes / gaps.** This is a correctness guard, not usually a warning. Multi-frame GIF is coalesced into animated WebP by the ImageMagick branch.

#### 10.5.13 This video won't play/upload everywhere — convert to a universal H.264 MP4 — `warn` (id: video-not-browser-playable-convert-offer)

*Where shown:* the `MediaViewer` `UnplayableCard` / `DecodeFailure` card — an amber "Convert to H.264 (MP4)…" button — reached after **both** native decode **and** the backend transcode-stream fail. Merges the duplicate `video-decode-failed-convert-h264`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `ViewerSurface` tries native `<video>`; on decode error it retries via `/api/media/stream` (backend H.264/AAC fragmented MP4). If that also fails, `DecodeFailure` renders, and the offer shows only when `kind==="video" && !view.flags.noCompress` (`offerConvert`). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` — `ViewerSurface` fallback (L693–706), `DecodeFailure` (L799–848), `offerConvert` (L814), `runConvertOffer` (L873–877); backend `planStream` transcode decision `transcode.service.ts` (L92–110).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the file uses a codec browsers can't decode (and even a server-side transcode preview failed); converting the file **on disk** to **H.264 · yuv420p · AAC · MP4** makes it play everywhere **and** upload cleanly to TikTok/X/YouTube/Instagram (unlike HEVC/ProRes/AV1/MKV). Nothing changes until confirmed, and the original moves to recoverable trash. This is a compatibility convert (`forceVideoCodec:"h264"`, `formatConvert`) — exempt from the size-gain guard (10.5.11), so it may not shrink. *Why it matters:* an unplayable/un-uploadable video is effectively stranded until converted. *Options:* trash-vs-hard-delete radio. *Action button:* "Convert to H.264 (MP4)" — **confirm-gated** (charter §6.1; nothing changes until the user confirms).

**(C) The fix.** `runConvertOffer` → `api.compressFile(path, {forceVideoCodec:"h264", deleteOriginal per settings})` → `POST /api/compress/file {path, videoCodec:"h264"}`, which **forces** the H.264 plan regardless of the user's default codec pref, verifies, and does a recoverable replace to the `.mp4` path. If ffmpeg is missing it returns `toolMissing` → route to Tools (10.5.1 / 10.5.2). *Fix in:* `.../frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` `runConvertOffer` (L873); backend forced-codec `pickVideoTarget` force branch (L366–380) + `compressFile` (L470).

**Notes / gaps.** Suppressed when the `noCompress` flag is set. CLAUDE.md/MEMORY: **X/Twitter does not support AV1** — H.264 is the safe target this offer enforces. It's a viewer-embedded card, not the top StatusBanner, and there's no blue-arrow educational popup yet.

#### 10.5.14 Compressed-vs-uncompressed verdict is extension-only (learned bell-curve baseline not wired) — `warn` (id: learned-baseline-not-wired)

*Where shown:* everywhere the "should/done compress" verdict and the computer/repo/directory uncompressed-count metric appear. This is the **charter's learned-baseline requirement**, currently an unimplemented seam.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `compressBadge`/`compressInfo` decide "should" vs. "done" purely from **extension + a filename regex**. The charter's learned size-baseline model (per-duration × per-resolution mean / 1σ / 2σ bell curves in a repo YAML/CSV, used to judge whether a file's **size** looks compressed) is only a code seam — the comment `Seam to the learned size-baseline model (code_plan §13)` marks the unimplemented hook, and `_sizeBytes` / `_threshold` are **unused params**. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` — `compressBadge()` with the unused `_sizeBytes`/`_threshold` args and the seam comment (L186–197, verified: seam comment L186, signature L187).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* today the app **guesses** compression state from file type/name; a smarter size-baseline (learned from your own files by duration + resolution) would catch (a) large videos that are technically `.mp4` but clearly un-optimized and (b) already-small files mislabeled "should." *Why it matters:* the current heuristic both over-offers (a `clip.mp4` that's already compressed) and under-detects (a bloated but correctly-extensioned file), so the uncompressed-count metric is only approximate. *Options:* checkbox "Start learning baselines from my current files." *Action button:* "Learn baselines" — **build gap, not shippable yet.**

**(C) The fix.** No safe auto-fix — this is a build gap. Manual next step: implement the learned baseline store (YAML/CSV of mean/1σ/2σ by duration+resolution, per charter) and feed the real byte size into `compressBadge` to produce a size-aware "looks uncompressed" confidence plus the uncompressed-count rollup metric. *Fix in:* to build — a compression baseline store + wire size into `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/fs/badges.ts` `compressBadge()`. No auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** **Gap: not yet wired.** The charter's "Detecting whether a file is compressed (learned baselines)" section **and** the per-file compressed/uncompressed hash tracking both depend on this. Every "should" false-positive in 10.5.5/10.5.6 traces back here.

#### 10.5.15 Not compressed — already well compressed (no size gain) — `neutral` (id: compress-no-gain)

*Where shown:* a neutral compress-result toast in the viewer ("Not compressed: no gain"). Not a banner. Merges the frontend `compress-no-gain-skip`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** After a real encode, for a **non-`formatConvert`** plan, if `afterBytes >= beforeBytes` the temp is discarded and `status:"skipped"`, reason `no gain (already well compressed)` — the original is left untouched (transactional). Also emitted **before** any transcode when the file already carries the in-file `LFBcompressed` marker (`isAlreadyCompressed`, e.g. a peer already compressed it and it synced over IPFS) → reason `already compressed (marker)`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — no-gain skip (L534–541), already-compressed marker skip (L494–496), `isAlreadyCompressed()` (L205–207), `readMarker()` (L183–201), `markerPayload()` (L177–180); frontend skipped-branch toast `MediaViewer.tsx` `reportCompress` (L863–864).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* reassure that the file is already about as small as it will get, so LFBridge left the original untouched, and it writes an in-file marker so it (and your other computers via IPFS) won't waste time re-encoding it again. Explain **why** it still showed a "C" offer (the heuristic is extension/name-based, not size-baseline-based yet — 10.5.14). *Why it matters:* nothing was changed — a healthy, quiet outcome. *Options:* "Do not compress this file" to stop re-offering. *Action button:* none required — optional "Do not compress."

**(C) The fix.** No fix needed — the correct, safe outcome. Best manual next step: set the "Do not compress" flag (`api.setEntityFlags {noCompress:true}`) so the file drops out of the compressible count and offers. *Fix in:* `.../frontend/src/api/client.ts` `setEntityFlags` (L221); the flag suppresses rollup/badge via `entity.service` (L274, `!flags.noCompress`). No auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** The marker rides in the file's container comment tag (ffmpeg `-metadata` / magick `-set comment`) so it syncs over IPFS and is read back with fast probes. **Gap:** there is **no** persistent per-file "no-gain" marker for a *skipped-no-gain* file (only for a successful compress), so the "C" offer does **not** clear after a no-gain skip — the app keeps offering to compress a file that can't shrink until the user manually sets `noCompress`. Persisting a no-gain marker would auto-clear the offer.

#### 10.5.16 Compression is turned off — globally, by extension, or per-file — `neutral` (id: compression-disabled-or-excluded)

*Where shown:* mixed. Per-file/folder "Do not compress" is a quiet slate pill on `ViewOneFilePage` / `MediaViewer` property grid and a "—" in the rollup Action column; global/settings disablement is only a `checkFile.action` skip reason with **no page banner**. Merges `compression-disabled-in-settings` and `do-not-compress-flag-suppressing-offers`.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Three mechanisms suppress the offer: **(a) global settings** — `getCompressionSettings().images.enabled` / `.video.enabled` false → `checkFile` returns `<media> compression is disabled in settings`, `eligible:false`; **(b) per-extension opt-out** — `srcExt ∈ prefs.skipExts` → `extension excluded by settings`; **(c) convert_types off** — for HEIC/AVIF with no in-place compressor → skip `conversion is turned off in settings`; **(d) per-file/folder flag** — `flags.noCompress` true → `canOfferCompress` returns false, rollup video/image rows are marked hidden with a "—" action, and the "C" badge offer is suppressed in `EntityMenu` (`compressible && compressState!=="done" && !noCompress`); a folder-level flag hides both compress rollup rows. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/compress/compression.service.ts` — `checkFile` enabled guard (L396), `skipExts` (L399), `convertTypes`-off skip (L302–314); frontend `canOfferCompress` `MediaViewer.tsx` (L852–854), hidden-flag + "—" action `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` (L45–46, L142), pill `ViewOneFilePage.tsx` (L122), `EntityMenu` (L335).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* this kind of file is opted out of compression — either the user turned off image/video compression globally, added the extension to the skip list, turned off `convert_types`, or set "Do not compress" on this file/folder — so LFBridge won't offer to shrink it and it's excluded from the compressible counts. All are deliberate user choices, so this is **neutral, never amber**. *Why it matters:* explains *why* a compressible-looking file shows no offer. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Open compression settings" (global cases) or toggle "Do not compress" off (per-file). No destructive action.

**(C) The fix.** For global/extension cases: `PATCH /api/compress/settings` — e.g. `{video:{enabled:true}}`, `{images:{convertTypes:true}}`, or remove the ext from `skipExts` (`setCompressionSettings()`). For the per-file flag: toggle `noCompress:false` via `api.setEntityFlags` to re-enable offers and re-include the file in counts. *Fix in:* `compression.router.ts` `PATCH /settings` (L31–38) → `setCompressionSettings()` `compression.service.ts` (L50–69); per-file toggle `.../frontend/src/api/client.ts` `setEntityFlags` (L221), `ViewOneDirectoryPage.tsx` `toggleFlag` (L83–91).

**Notes / gaps.** Not an alarm — surface as a quiet explanation. **Gap:** the badges/counts **don't** account for the global `enabled`/`skipExts` state, so a user can be offered a compress that immediately returns "disabled." Reconcile the offer surfaces (badges/counts) with settings.

#### 10.5.17 Describe auto-writes a .gitignore entry for its sidecar (charter-tension note) — `neutral` (id: describe-autogitignores-sidecar)

*Where shown:* **not user-visible today** — a silent `.gitignore` edit on a successful describe in a plain git repo. Owned here as a compliance flag against the charter's big-file gitignore rule (see also §10.4 for the general big-file gitignore nudge).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** On a successful describe in a plain repo (the `gitIgnore` flag true), `ensureLfbridgeIgnored()` **automatically** appends `*.ai_description` to the repo's `.gitignore` if absent — no user click. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.service.ts` — `ensureLfbridgeIgnored()` (L58–75), called at L221.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* if surfaced — explain that LFBridge keeps its generated description sidecars out of Git in a plain repo (mirroring transcription's `*.transcription`), and let the user **opt out** — because the charter's big-file policy says "**never add a `.gitignore` entry automatically for anyone**." *Why it matters:* it's an unrequested write to the user's `.gitignore`, however benign. *Options:* checkbox "Don't auto-ignore my description sidecars." *Action button:* none for correctness — an offer/confirm at most.

**(C) The fix.** No fix needed for correctness, but for charter compliance consider gating this behind a user confirm/offer rather than an automatic write, consistent with the big-file gitignore nudge policy. *Fix in:* `describe.service.ts` `ensureLfbridgeIgnored()` (L58–75). No auto-fix — a policy/design change.

**Notes / gaps.** **Compliance tension:** this auto-write is for the app's **own** artifact (arguably fine, like transcribe's sidecar), but it's the one place the describe module edits `.gitignore` without an explicit user click — flagged for review against the "never auto-gitignore" charter rule.

## 10.6 AI description (vision) warnings

These warnings govern the **"Generate AI description"** feature — the one place LFBridge deliberately sends a file's bytes off-box, to a hosted vision model (Gemini / Grok / OpenAI), to produce a `.ai_description` sidecar. Every failure mode of that flow surfaces through the standard banner + popup: the file can't be described because no key is configured, the pinned model was retired, the provider rejected/timed-out the call, no Personal storage owns the file, or the file is over the inline-upload cap. The one hard rule threaded through all of them: **generation never modifies the original** — large files are transcoded to a throwaway temp copy purely for upload. All backend logic lives in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/` (`describe.service.ts`, `adapters.ts`, `models.ts`, `fit-media.ts`, `describe.router.ts`); the surfaces are the `MediaViewer` entity page and the Settings/Tools/AI-credentials pages. Ranked Broken (`bad`) before Improvable (`warn`).

#### 10.6.1 The AI model you pinned was retired — update it — `bad` (id: describe-model-retired)

*Where shown:* Media viewer (`/video`, `/image`) after a Generate attempt returns a failure — currently a `toast.error` surface; **gap: not yet wired to the WarningBanner/WarningPopup** (it's a transient toast today, not a persistent banner).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** After a Generate call, the provider returns a 404 / `NOT_FOUND` / "no longer available" style error. `looksLikeModelRetired(msg)` matches that shape; `explainModelError()` then rewrites the raw provider error into an actionable message naming the **specific bad model id** and the **recommended current default**. Two distinct pathways: (1) ids in the `RETIRED_GEMINI_MODELS` allow-list are **auto-healed** to `DEFAULT_GEMINI_MODEL` (`"gemini-flash-latest"`) on config load, so they never reach the wire; (2) a **user-pinned** id that is unknown/retired-but-not-in-the-list still 404s at call time → `describeOne` returns `status='failed'` carrying the rewritten message. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/models.ts` — `looksLikeModelRetired()` (line 37), `RETIRED_GEMINI_MODELS` (lines 22–33), `DEFAULT_GEMINI_MODEL` (line 16); `adapters.ts` — `explainModelError()` (lines 62–72), invoked at the Gemini adapter (line 135) and the chat-vision adapter (line 182); `describe.service.ts` — `describeOne` failed-result branch (~lines 238–243).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Vision providers retire old model ids on a published schedule, so a model id that was hard-pinned in Settings can begin returning 404 forever even though your key is perfectly valid. LFBridge names the exact retired model and the replacement it recommends. *Why it matters:* Until the pinned id is changed, **every** description on this machine will keep failing — it's a permanent, not transient, break; nothing gets described and no sidecar is written. *Options:* none — one-click fix (set the recommended default). Optionally a checkbox "Use the rolling `gemini-flash-latest` alias (auto-tracks the newest model so this can't recur)". *Action button:* "Update model" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** The button issues `PATCH /api/describe/config {gemini:{model:'gemini-flash-latest'}}` (or the recommended default for whichever provider failed), which persists the model in `config.yaml`; setting an **empty** model string reverts to the provider default. After the write the user re-runs Generate. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.router.ts` — `PATCH /config` (lines 31–42) → `describe.service.ts` `setAiConfig()` (lines ~155–167, which clears the key on `""` and only overwrites the model on a non-empty trimmed value).

**Notes / gaps.** Auto-heal covers **only** ids explicitly listed in `RETIRED_GEMINI_MODELS` (append-only — add ids as Google retires more); any other unknown/retired pin needs this manual fix. The default deliberately uses the `gemini-flash-latest` **alias** (Google hot-swaps it to the newest GA Flash) precisely so a default install never hits this. **Gap:** today this is only a toast; per §2 it should become a persistent `bad` banner with the arrow-to-popup so the guidance survives a page refresh.

#### 10.6.2 AI description failed (provider error / blocked / no text) — `bad` (id: describe-failed-provider-error)

*Where shown:* Media viewer generate result — currently `toast.error` + a durable entry in `error.err`; **gap: not yet wired to a persistent WarningBanner/WarningPopup.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `describeOne`'s try/catch converts any thrown provider/transport error into `status='failed'` carrying the provider's own message. Distinct sub-cases the code raises: (a) **safety block** — Gemini `promptFeedback.blockReason` → "Gemini blocked the request: <reason>"; (b) **empty result** — no candidates / empty text → "Gemini/OpenAI/Grok returned no description"; (c) **HTTP / non-JSON error** from `postJson` (auth 401/403, rate-limit 429, 5xx); (d) **timeout** — the 120s `AbortController` fires. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/adapters.ts` — `postJson` timeout + HTTP-error handling (lines 74–97), Gemini `blockReason` (line 137) and no-text (line 139), chat-vision no-text (line 185); `describe.service.ts` — failed-result branch (~lines 238–243). Summary rollup lumps `failed`/`no_provider`/`unsupported` together as "failed" in `summarizeDescribe` (line 369).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The call reached the provider but the provider refused or couldn't answer — and the popup shows the **honest reason** verbatim (rate limit, safety block, bad key, timeout). *Why it matters:* This particular file has no description yet; depending on cause it may succeed on retry (transient/timeout/rate-limit), may need a key fix (auth), or may be permanently refused (a safety block on the content itself — no fix). *Options:* the popup **branches on the message class** — for auth show "Fix the key" routing to §10.6.3; for transient/timeout show a "Try again" primary; for a safety block show an explanatory note and **no** action button (nothing to fix). *Action button:* "Try again" (blue) for the retryable classes; suppressed for a safety block.

**(C) The fix.** There is **no blanket auto-fix** — the action depends on cause. Retry re-issues `POST /api/describe/file`. An auth cause routes to the key setup (`PATCH /api/describe/config`). A safety block is terminal (the provider will keep refusing that content). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.router.ts` — `POST /file` (lines ~62–73); auth branch → `PATCH /config` (lines 31–42).

**Notes / gaps.** The full fault is written durably to `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err` (§5.5). Because `summarizeDescribe` folds `no_provider`/`unsupported` into the same "failed" count, a batch summary can't by itself distinguish "provider errored" from "no key" — the per-file `status`/`reason` is the authoritative signal the popup must read. **Gap:** persistent-banner wiring pending.

#### 10.6.3 No AI vision provider is configured — can't describe this file — `warn` (id: describe-no-provider; supersedes no-ai-provider-key-configured, ai-credentials-missing, ai-credentials-missing-for-description)

*Where shown:* This one real-world condition (no usable vision key resolves on this machine) surfaces on **four** surfaces, all backed by the same backend probe: (1) **Media viewer** band-6 AI-description column → `CredentialsMissingDialog` (Close / Instructions); (2) **Tools page** AI-description section — amber "No provider is configured — AI description is disabled until you add at least one API key. Only Gemini describes video."; (3) **AiCredentialsPage** top status banner — amber `AlertCircle` "No provider key is configured on this computer yet…"; (4) **Settings page** per-provider row — "✗ no key". *Merged from ids `no-ai-provider-key-configured`, `ai-credentials-missing`, `ai-credentials-missing-for-description`.*

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Backend resolves a key for each provider in order **config.yaml → env var → shared `~/.config/GoogleCloud/apikey.yaml`**; env vars honored are `GEMINI_API_KEY`/`GOOGLE_GENAI_API_KEY`/`GOOGLE_API_KEY` (Gemini), `XAI_API_KEY`/`GROK_API_KEY` (Grok), `OPENAI_API_KEY` (OpenAI). `describeProviders().anyAvailable` is `false` when **no** adapter's `available()` returns true — that single boolean drives every surface's preflight. Runtime path: `selectAdapter(kind)` returns `null` → `describeOne` returns `status='no_provider'` with reason "no AI provider configured for <kind> — add an API key for <need>". Two-tier detection is deliberate: the preflight `anyAvailable` probe **plus** the runtime `no_provider` result, so a gap is caught both before and after the click. *Computed in:* backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.service.ts` — `describeProviders()`/`anyAvailable` (~lines 113–116), `describeOne` `no_provider` (line 200), `aiCredentialsInfo()` (~lines 140–151, drives the Instructions page); `adapters.ts` — `selectAdapter()` (lines 228–240), per-adapter `available()` (lines 114/158). Frontend: `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/lib/describe.ts` — `runDescribeFile` `no_provider` branch (lines 56–57) + `msgOne` (lines 11–19) firing `onNoProvider`; `~/.../frontend/src/components/describe/CredentialsMissingDialog.tsx`; `~/.../frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` — providers query (lines 434–436), `noProviderKnown` (line 443), Generate creds branch (lines 448–461), dialog render (lines 527–529), amber hint under the button (lines 482/597); `~/.../frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` `AiDescriptionSection` (lines 156–173, `ENV_HINT` lines 126–130); `~/.../frontend/src/pages/settings/AiCredentialsPage.tsx` (banner lines 63–77; the distinct "file present but no usable key" sub-state at lines 99–103); `~/.../frontend/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` `AiProviderRow` (lines 235, 240–242).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* AI description sends the image/video to a **cloud** vision model, which requires an API key — and no usable key was found on this computer. Keys are read from `config.yaml`, an environment variable, or the shared `~/.config/GoogleCloud/apikey.yaml`, and **stay on this machine** — the app never displays the raw key value. Images can use Gemini, Grok, **or** OpenAI; **only Gemini can describe video**, so a Gemini key is the priority. *Why it matters:* Until a key resolves, the whole AI-description feature is disabled — no file on this machine can be described; the media's bytes would (once a key exists) be uploaded to the chosen provider (a compressed temp copy for large files — the original is never touched). *Options:* none that the app can safely apply — it **cannot mint a secret**. The popup is educational + routing. *Action button:* "Instructions" / "Add a key" (blue) → opens the AI-credentials setup.
