**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix** (can't fabricate a key). The button routes to `AiCredentialsPage` (`/ai-credentials`, new tab), which shows the exact file `~/.config/GoogleCloud/apikey.yaml`, its YAML schema/placeholder, and the app `config.yaml` path — **or** the user uses Settings → AI providers, whose save writes the key via `PATCH /api/describe/config` (`api.setAiConfig`). Keys added by **file or env** are read at backend start, so if the app is already running the user must **restart** it; a key added via Settings takes effect immediately. After a key resolves, re-run Generate. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.router.ts` — `PATCH /config` (lines 31–42), `GET /credentials` (lines 46–48) → `describe.service.ts` `setAiConfig()` (~lines 155–167) & `aiCredentialsInfo()` (~lines 140–151); frontend routing in `CredentialsMissingDialog.tsx` `openInstructions` (~lines 20–22) and `SettingsPage.tsx` `AiProvidersSection` save → `api.setAiConfig`.

**Notes / gaps.** This is an **Improvable offer** (a gated feature), never a data-at-risk alarm — so it is dismissible per §5.6. Per-provider sub-states are independent: one row can read "✗ no key" while another is configured (`AiProviderRow`), and a distinct "file exists but holds no usable key" sub-state is flagged separately (`AiCredentialsPage` lines 99–103). Charter/security tie: this network call is the app's **one deliberate egress** — it is the exception to the local-only default, made only on explicit user action, and the key value is never rendered.

#### 10.6.4 Video description needs Gemini specifically — `warn` (id: describe-video-needs-gemini)

*Where shown:* Media viewer for a **video** when the machine *is* configured — but only with **image-capable** keys (OpenAI and/or Grok) and **no** Gemini key. Same `CredentialsMissingDialog`, with a reason naming Gemini as the only video-capable provider.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** For `kind='video'`, `selectAdapter` can only match the Gemini adapter — it is the **sole** adapter whose `supports` array contains `'video'` (`["image","video"]`); the chat-vision adapter is image-only (`["image"]`). So if Gemini has no key but OpenAI/Grok do, `selectAdapter('video')` returns `null` and `describeOne` yields `status='no_provider'` with the **video-specific** `need` string: "Gemini (only Gemini describes video)". A runtime `no_provider` can also arise post-click. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/adapters.ts` — Gemini `supports` (line 103) vs chat-vision `supports` (line 156), `selectAdapter()` (lines 228–240); `describe.service.ts` — `need` string composed in the `no_provider` branch (~line ~197, before the return at line 200).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The image providers you have configured (OpenAI / Grok) **cannot process video** — only Gemini can — so a Gemini key is required to describe this video. *Why it matters:* This is a subtle gap: the machine looks "set up" (a green image-provider key exists) yet every video will still fail to describe until Gemini is added. *Options:* none the app can apply. *Action button:* "Add Gemini key" (blue) → credentials setup.

**(C) The fix.** No auto-fix — the user must add a Gemini key: `PATCH /api/describe/config {gemini:{apiKey}}`, or set `GEMINI_API_KEY` (env; restart required), or drop the shared `~/.config/GoogleCloud/apikey.yaml`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.router.ts` — `PATCH /config` (lines 31–42).

**Notes / gaps.** Kept **distinct** from §10.6.3 on purpose: the generic no-provider warning fires when `anyAvailable===false`, but this one fires when `anyAvailable===true` yet no adapter supports **video** — a machine can be fully "configured" and still unable to describe video. The popup copy and the routing differ (it names Gemini specifically). Preference order across providers is Gemini → OpenAI → Grok.

#### 10.6.5 No Personal storage owns this file — set up storage first — `warn` (id: describe-needs-setup; merges needs-personal-storage-setup-for-describe)

*Where shown:* Media viewer Generate-description action, and the page-action "Create AI descriptions" when **every** eligible file lacks storage. Instead of a banner-popup it opens the **`FirstTimeStorageWizard`** modal (a first-time gate). *Merged from ids `describe-needs-setup` (backend) and `needs-personal-storage-setup-for-describe` (frontend).*

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `resolveDescriptionPath()` walks ancestors looking for a home storage (a `storage.yaml` / `.lfbridge` / `.git` marker) — if none owns the file, `needsSetup=true` and `describeOne` returns `status='needs_setup'` ("no storage is set up for this file — configure Personal storage first"). In the batch path, `enqueueDescribe` counts `needSetup`; when `needSetup === eligible.length` (i.e. **all** eligible files lack storage) it queues **nothing** and returns `{needsSetup:true, setupPath}` (the representative path) to open the wizard rather than write a sidecar in a surprising directory. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.service.ts` — `resolveDescriptionPath()` (from line 44), `describeOne` `needs_setup` (line 189), `enqueueDescribe` all-need-setup gate (lines 309–311). Frontend: `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/lib/describe.ts` — `runDescribeFile` `needs_setup` branch (lines 48–55) + `msgOne` (lines 21–23) → `requestStorageSetup({mediaPath, actionLabel, retry})`; `~/.../frontend/src/lib/setupWizard.ts` `requestStorageSetup`; component `FirstTimeStorageWizard.tsx`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* AI descriptions (and other per-file metadata) are written into the **syncable-data-location of a Personal storage** so they get placed and synced predictably — but no storage currently owns this file, so a one-time storage must be created first. The popup explains, in plain terms, what a storage/SDL is and that setup is quick and one-time. *Why it matters:* Without a home storage the sidecar would either not be written or land somewhere unexpected and un-synced. *Options:* the wizard flow (choose/create the Personal storage location). *Action button:* the wizard's own primary (creates/registers the Personal storage covering this path).

**(C) The fix.** Run the `FirstTimeStorageWizard` for `setupPath` to create/register a Personal storage (SDL) covering the file; on success the queued describe **auto-retries** (the retry closure is passed through from `describe.ts`). Manual alternative: Settings → Storages → add a Personal storage. **No silent auto-fix** — the user must pick the storage location. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/describe.service.ts` — `enqueueDescribe` setup return (lines 309–311); frontend `~/.../frontend/src/lib/setupWizard.ts` `requestStorageSetup` + `components/FirstTimeStorageWizard.tsx`, with the auto-retry closure from `describe.ts` (lines 48–55).

**Notes / gaps.** `needs_setup` is counted as **skipped** (not an error) in batch summaries — `summarizeDescribe` folds it with `skipped` (line 368) so the counts still sum. A toast fallback ("Set up Personal storage first — Settings → Storages") exists for surfaces that can't pop the wizard. This is a **setup gate / offer** (`warn`), not data-at-risk.

#### 10.6.6 File is over the AI upload limit — needs ffmpeg/ImageMagick to auto-compress a copy — `warn` (id: describe-file-over-inline-limit)

*Where shown:* Media viewer generate flow. **Normally invisible** — the compress-to-fit runs transparently and only the fitted temp copy is uploaded. It only surfaces (as a `status='failed'` with a helpful message) when the required tool is missing or the squeeze genuinely can't fit the file.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Hosted vision models cap the inline upload: `INLINE_MAX_BYTES = 18MB` (`readBase64Capped` throws above it). Before upload, `fitMediaUnderLimit` targets `FIT_TARGET_BYTES = 17.5MB`; if the file exceeds the target it transcodes a **TEMP** copy. `fitVideoUnderLimit` throws "…needs ffmpeg… `brew install ffmpeg`" when ffmpeg is absent; `fitImageUnderLimit` throws "…needs ImageMagick… `brew install imagemagick`" when `magick` is absent; either throws "could not compress under NMB" if the quality/resolution ladder can't get it under target. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/adapters.ts` — `INLINE_MAX_BYTES` (line 39), `readBase64Capped` (lines 49–57); `fit-media.ts` — `FIT_TARGET_BYTES` (line 29), `fitMediaUnderLimit` (from line 255), `fitVideoUnderLimit` ffmpeg gate (line 176) + can't-fit throw (~line 215), `fitImageUnderLimit` magick gate (line 227) + can't-fit throw (~line 246).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Hosted vision models cap the inline upload at ~18MB, so a large file is transcoded to a **temporary** H.264 (video) or JPEG (image) copy **just for the upload** — the original on disk is never modified. If the needed tool isn't installed, the popup gives the exact `brew` command; if the file genuinely can't be squeezed under the cap, it suggests compressing/trimming the source first. *Why it matters:* Without ffmpeg/ImageMagick this specific large file can't be described at all; but there is **zero risk to the original** — all writes are temp-only under the state dir. *Options:* none the app runs. *Action button:* none / "Copy `brew` command" (there is no app-run installer).

**(C) The fix.** **No app-run installer.** Manual, tool-dependent: `brew install ffmpeg` (video) or `brew install imagemagick` (image). When the tools are present there is **no user action** — compress-to-fit is automatic and silent (a note is logged, the original untouched). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/describe/fit-media.ts` — `fitVideoUnderLimit` (lines 174–216), `fitImageUnderLimit` (lines 224–247); no auto-fix endpoint — routes to a manual `brew` install.

**Notes / gaps.** The video ladder follows the charter compression strategy: keep resolution first (CRF 28→34), then step down ~25% at a time to a 240p floor, with a final two-pass exact-bitrate guarantee. The **original is guaranteed untouched** (temp-only writes), satisfying the charter's "never alter a file unless the user explicitly asks." **Gap:** when the failure is a missing tool, this is a persistent, actionable `warn` that today only shows as a toast — per §2 it should be a banner + popup carrying the `brew` command.

## 10.7 Storages & communities

These are the warnings for the **Storages** tab / detail / settings pages (`frontend/src/pages/storages/*`) and the **Communities** page (`frontend/src/pages/communities/*`), backed by the storage, store-mode, and communities backend modules. A "storage" is a tracked home for large files — the **Personal** storage (loose files under `~`), a **company** storage (a shared `*_large_files_bridge` repo), or a discovered **repo** — and a "community" is a publisher whose public files this computer optionally pins for redundancy. The dominant theme here is that almost every failure is currently **silent** (server log only): the descriptor, device-registry, git-backbone, and disk-budget faults below all "succeed" in the UI today, so most of these subsections carry a **gap: not wired to a StatusBanner** flag. Ordered Broken before Improvable; none are neutral.

#### 10.7.1 This storage has no Git backbone — your other computers will never receive its file list — `bad` (id: storage-no-git-backbone)

*Where shown:* Storage detail / Storage settings for a **company** or **personal** storage. **Gap: not wired to any banner today — the failure is fully silent** (the exact reported "Act3 company storage" defect).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires for a `company`/`personal` storage when `getGitBackboneRemote(id) === null`. That resolver returns null only when **both** backbone sources are absent: (1) the explicit dedicated-repo backing is off — `backing.dedicated_repo.enabled` is false or has no path, so `getDedicatedRepoRemote(id)` is null; **and** (2) the storage root is not itself a git working tree — `<root>/.git` does not exist (the auto-adopt path). With no remote, this computer writes its device file to `.lfbridge/devices/<self>.yaml` but has nowhere to `git add`/`commit`/`push` it, so the registry + manifest never travel. `type === "repo"` storages are excluded (those git-ignore `.lfbridge/` by design). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` — `getGitBackboneRemote()` (lines 270–279), delegating to `getDedicatedRepoRemote()` (lines 243–251); the code comment at lines 254–269 documents this as the Act3 defect.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* A company/personal storage travels between your machines over a **Git repo** — the hidden `.lfbridge/` text (the device registry + the file manifest) is the payload that git carries. With no dedicated-repo backing **and** the root not being a git repo, this computer records itself locally but can never push that record. *Why it matters:* Your **other** computers never learn this storage exists or which files it holds — so nothing about this storage syncs off this one machine, and if this disk dies its file list is lost with it. *Options:* two mutually-exclusive radios (no blind auto-pick of a remote): **"Turn on the dedicated-repo backing"** (point the backbone at a versioned repo LFB commits into — takes an optional path, defaulting to this root) vs **"Make this storage's root a Git repo"** (auto-adopt — `git init` the root). *Action button:* "Set up Git backbone" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** Preferred: `PATCH /api/storages/:id/settings` with `{backing:{dedicatedRepo:{enabled:true, path:<root or chosen repo>}}}` — then `ensureBackingLocations()` `git init`s the location and the next sync pass commits+pushes the device registry. Alternative: `git init` the storage root (auto-adopt). **No single silent action is unambiguous** — offer the two choices; never pick a remote URL for the user. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` — `PATCH /:id/settings` (lines 118–127) → `storage-settings.service.ts` `writeStorageSettings()` (lines 174–209); materialized by `storage.service.ts` `ensureBackingLocations()` (lines 453–498, git init at 491–495).

**Notes / gaps.** BAD because file lists silently never reach other machines — the highest-severity storage fault. Grounded directly in the in-code defect comment. Gap: not surfaced in any banner — needs a top-of-detail StatusBanner rollup.

#### 10.7.2 Can't measure this computer's free disk — community budget is unavailable — `bad` (id: disk-measure-failed)

*Where shown:* Communities page — the storage-budget header (`StorageHeader`, four stat tiles + meter). **Gap: the zeroed header is currently indistinguishable from a genuinely 0-budget disk; needs a `totalDiskBytes===0` sentinel to fire BAD.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** In `computeStorageMath()`, `fs.promises.statfs(resolveStateDir())` throws → the catch logs `statfs failed` and leaves `totalDiskBytes = 0` and `freeOutsideIpfsBytes = 0`. That collapses `reservedHeadroomBytes` to the 10 GiB floor (`HEADROOM_MIN_BYTES`), `growable` to 0, and `communityBudgetBytes` to 0. The distinguishing sentinel from a real full/empty disk is **`totalDiskBytes === 0`** (a real volume always reports a nonzero total). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.service.ts` — `computeStorageMath()` (lines 49–78; catch at 57–59); consumed by `StorageHeader` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/communities/CommunitiesPage.tsx` (lines 151–201). State root resolved in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/config/state-dir.ts` `resolveStateDir()`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFB couldn't read the disk that holds the state root (`~/T/_large_files_bridge`), so it can't compute a safe storage budget for backing up communities. *Why it matters:* Community backup planning is **paused** — until free space can be measured, no community can be assigned a backup target, so pinning of communities you chose to Support/Full won't proceed. Likely causes: the state-root volume is unavailable or its permissions changed. *Options:* none — informational + retry. *Action button:* "Retry" (blue) — re-calls `GET /api/communities`.

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix** — LFB can't remount a volume. Manual: verify the state-root volume (`LFB_STATE_DIR` / `~/T/_large_files_bridge`) is mounted and readable, then reload. *Fix in:* no auto-fix — routes to retry via `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.router.ts` `GET /` (lines 12–19); state root in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/config/state-dir.ts`.

**Notes / gaps.** BAD, but today it renders as four "0 B" tiles with no error — indistinguishable from a real 0-budget disk. Guard: only fire BAD when `totalDiskBytes === 0` (measurement failed); a genuinely-full disk with `totalDiskBytes > 0` is the *Improvable* case §10.7.11.

#### 10.7.3 This storage isn't set up yet — `warn` (id: storage-not-initialized)

*Where shown:* Storages tab row (amber "not set up" badge + an **Initialize** button replacing "Open") and the Storage detail header. Gap: the inline affordance exists but is **not wired into a top-of-page StatusBanner rollup**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `StorageRow.initialized === false`, computed as `initialized: !!desc` where `desc = readDescriptor(root)`. It means a directory was **discovered** — via `storage.yaml`, the `*_large_files_bridge` naming convention, or the canonical personal path — but has no readable descriptor written yet. Rolls up to WARN if **any** discovered row has `initialized === false`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.service.ts` — `buildRow()` (line 269) + `discoverRoots()` (lines 227–252); badge in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/storages/StoragesPage.tsx` (line 42).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFB found a folder that looks like an LFBridge storage but it has no `storage.yaml` / `.lfbridge/` yet, so it isn't tracking or syncing anything. *Why it matters:* Nothing in this folder is indexed, fingerprinted, or synced to your other computers until it's set up. *Options:* none — one-click fix (setting up writes the descriptor + the hidden tracking dir and registers this computer in the device registry; **no file bytes are touched**). *Action button:* "Initialize" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/storages/:id/init` → `initStorageById()` → `ensureStorage(root, type)` writes `storage.yaml`, creates `.lfbridge/`, reconciles `.gitignore`, and calls `writeSelfDevice(root)`. Safe, **idempotent** auto-fix (the inline Initialize button already calls `api.initStorage`). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` — `POST /:id/init` (lines 88–95) → `storage.service.ts` `initStorageById()` (lines 337–345) / `ensureStorage()` (lines 132–161).

**Notes / gaps.** Distinct from §10.7.16 (descriptor present but corrupt, which *also* reads `initialized=false`) — this one is a truly-missing descriptor. Gap: no banner rollup on the Storages tab.

#### 10.7.4 This storage has never been indexed — `warn` (id: storage-never-indexed)

*Where shown:* Storages tab (Files column "—") and Storage detail (Files-tracked fact "—" + empty file table with a primary **Index files** button). Gap: no banner verdict.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `StorageRow.fileCount === null`. `countStorageIndex(root)` returns **null** (not 0) precisely when `<root>/.lfbridge/files.yaml` does not exist or can't be parsed — i.e. the fingerprint index was never built. **Critical distinction: `0` = indexed but no large files (ok/neutral); `null` = never indexed (warn).** *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/tracking.service.ts` — `countStorageIndex()` (lines 175–183); consumed in `storage.service.ts` `buildRow()` (line 271); UI in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/storages/StoragesPage.tsx` (lines 50–51) and `StorageDetailPage.tsx` (lines 123, 138).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFB hasn't yet scanned this storage for large files, so it can't tell you what's big, uncompressed, or unsynced here. Indexing builds a fingerprint (hash + size + created/modified dates) per large file so changes can be detected. *Why it matters:* Without an index there's no change-detection, no uncompressed-file count, and no sync plan for this storage. *Options:* none — one-click fix (it **only reads files, never modifies them**). *Action button:* "Index files" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/storages/:id/index` → `indexStorageById()` → `indexStorageFiles(root)`: a parallel head/tail+sha256 fingerprint of every file over the big-file threshold, written to `.lfbridge/files.yaml`. Safe, read-only auto-fix. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` — `POST /:id/index` (lines 99–106) → `storage.service.ts` `indexStorageById()` (lines 375–379) → `tracking.service.ts` `indexStorageFiles()` (lines 91–151).

**Notes / gaps.** False-alarm guard: never fire on `fileCount === 0` — that's a fully-indexed empty storage. Gap: no banner rollup. Related: an index that hits the 5,000-file cap is §10.7.15.

#### 10.7.5 This storage's files are not being synced to your other computers — `warn` (id: storage-sync-off)

*Where shown:* Storage settings ("Sync over IPFS" section) and should also verdict on Storage detail. Gap: no StatusBanner on the detail/settings page.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `StorageSettings.synced === false` — a **machine-local, per-storage** config flag (`synced`, schema default **false**). `getStorageSynced(id)` returns false, and the sync pass gates all byte work for this storage on this flag. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` — `readStorageSettings()` (line 159, `synced`) + `getStorageSynced()` (lines 230–236); UI in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/storages/StorageSettingsPage.tsx` (lines 45–52).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFB never pins/replicates a storage's bytes without opt-in (the charter default), so with this **off** the large files here live on **only this computer**. *Why it matters:* A lost or failed disk loses these files — there is no second copy. Turning it on makes this computer add+pin these files over IPFS so your other machines can fetch them; it does **not** make you a public gateway. *Options:* none — one-click toggle. *Action button:* "Sync this storage" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** `PATCH /api/storages/:id/settings {synced:true}` → `writeStorageSettings` sets the machine-local `synced=true`; the next sync pass begins pinning this storage's mapped-dir bytes. Safe, reversible. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` — `PATCH /:id/settings` (lines 118–127) → `storage-settings.service.ts` `writeStorageSettings()` (lines 174–209, at line 180).

**Notes / gaps.** This is an **offer (amber), never an alarm** — off is the compliant, charter-correct default (no unsolicited pinning). Dismissible as an Improvable offer. Gap: no banner.

#### 10.7.6 A backup copy is turned on but its drive isn't connected here — `warn` (id: backing-enabled-but-drive-unreachable)

*Where shown:* Storage settings — Backing-locations rows (Google Drive / Dropbox / dedicated repo). Gap: today only a server info log + a disabled checkbox; no user-facing verdict.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `StorageBackingLocation.enabled === true && available === false`. `available` = `detectGoogleDriveBase() !== null` / `detectDropboxBase() !== null` (Drive under `~/Library/CloudStorage/GoogleDrive-*`; Dropbox via `~/.dropbox/info.json` or default roots). `ensureBackingLocations` then **skips** this location every pass, so the mirror stops updating. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` — `buildBacking()` (lines 122–130) + `detectGoogleDriveBase()` (lines 30–42) / `detectDropboxBase()` (lines 50–84); the skip at `ensureBackingLocations()` (lines 478–481); UI `BackingRow` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/storages/StorageSettingsPage.tsx` (lines 201–209).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* This backup mirror is switched on but the drive it lives on isn't mounted on this computer, so that extra copy is **not** being kept up to date here. *Why it matters:* You believe you have a redundant Drive/Dropbox copy, but it's silently stale on this machine. *Options:* radios — reconnect the drive vs repoint the path to a reachable directory vs turn this location off here. *Action button:* "Repoint / turn off" (blue) when repointing/disabling; reconnecting is manual.

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix** (LFB can't mount a cloud drive). Manual: launch/relink the Google Drive or Dropbox desktop app and let it mount, **or** `PATCH /api/storages/:id/settings` to repoint `backing.<x>.path` to a reachable directory, **or** turn the location off here. *Fix in:* no auto-fix — routes to manual reconnect; repoint via `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` `PATCH /:id/settings` (lines 118–127).

**Notes / gaps.** Guard: the checkbox is already disabled when the drive is absent at edit-time; this warning is for the case where a location was persisted `enabled=true` and the drive was **later** disconnected. Gap: currently only a server info log ("enabled but not reachable — skipping").

#### 10.7.7 This storage doesn't cover any directories yet — `warn` (id: mapped-dirs-empty)

*Where shown:* Storage settings — "Mapped source directories" section (company/personal storages). Gap: not surfaced above the section as a verdict.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** For a company/personal storage: `MappedDirsView.rows.length === 0`. `getMappedDirsView` reads the shared `mapped_dirs.yaml` joined with this device's graft; an empty list means nothing is in scope, so nothing will ever be indexed or synced for this storage. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` — `getMappedDirsView()` (lines 343–365) / `readMappedDirsForRoot()` (lines 298–304); UI `MappedDirsSection` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/storages/StorageSettingsPage.tsx` (line 133).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* A company/personal storage tracks whatever **source directories** you map into it (everything recursive under each). With none mapped, this storage syncs nothing. *Why it matters:* The storage exists but is empty of scope — no files travel across your computers until you map at least one directory holding the large files you care about. *Options:* none in the popup — routes to the section's "Add directory" flow. *Action button:* "Add a directory" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** **No blind auto-fix** (LFB must not guess a directory). Manual: the user clicks "Add directory" → `PATCH /api/storages/:id/mapped-dirs {mapped:[...]}` adds a row, then sets this computer's local path (graft — see §10.7.8). *Fix in:* no auto-fix — routes to `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` `PATCH /:id/mapped-dirs` (lines 154–163) → `storage-settings.service.ts` `patchMappedDirs()` / `setMappedDirs()` (lines 317–390).

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: not surfaced above the section as a verdict.

#### 10.7.8 A mapped directory has no location on this computer — `warn` (id: mapped-dir-not-grafted-here)

*Where shown:* Storage settings — individual "Mapped source directories" rows. Gap: no per-row or page-level warning today.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** For a mapped row: `localPath == null` (and/or `wanted === false`) in `MappedDirRow` — this device hasn't set its per-key **graft** path for a directory the shared list says belongs to the storage. `localPath` comes from `readSelfGraft`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` — `getMappedDirsView()` (lines 349–358, `localPath` from `readSelfGraft`); UI in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/storages/StorageSettingsPage.tsx` (lines 151–160).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The mapped-directory list is **shared** across your computers, but each machine must say **where** that directory lives locally — paths differ per computer. *Why it matters:* Until you set this computer's path, the storage won't sync that directory **here**, even though your other machines might already be syncing it. *Options:* none in the popup — routes to the row's path input. *Action button:* "Set this computer's path" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix** (the path is machine-specific and unknown). Manual: enter the local path in the row → `PATCH /api/storages/:id/mapped-dirs {graft:{<key>:<localPath>}}`. *Fix in:* no auto-fix — routes to `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` `patchMappedDirs()` (lines 372–390, graft branch → `setSelfGraftPath`).

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: no per-row or page-level warning today.

#### 10.7.9 Set up the storage before choosing a Drive/Dropbox mirror path — `warn` (id: clones-edit-before-init)

*Where shown:* Storage settings — Backing locations (Google Drive / Dropbox path fields) on a **not-yet-initialized** storage. Gap: only a server log today; the UI shows a misleading success toast.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** In `writeStorageSettings`, `patch.backing.googleDrive.path` or `.dropbox.path` is defined **AND** `readDescriptor(root) === null` (no `storage.yaml` yet). The clone path is **not** persisted to the shared descriptor — it falls into the else-branch that logs `…no storage.yaml yet — clones not written`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` — `writeStorageSettings()` (lines 195–206, the `else`-branch `log.warn`).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The Drive/Dropbox mirror location has a **machine-local** part (your path here) and a **shared canonical** part (where the mirror sits relative to the drive, agreed by all your computers). The shared part can only be recorded once the storage is initialized (`storage.yaml` exists). *Why it matters:* If you set the mirror path before initializing, the canonical shared path is silently dropped, so your other computers never learn where the mirror lives — only this machine's local config saved. *Options:* none — one-click chained fix (init, then re-apply the pending path). *Action button:* "Initialize, then set path" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/storages/:id/init` to write `storage.yaml`, then re-apply the backing-path PATCH. Can be **chained as one auto-fix**: init, then `PATCH /:id/settings` with the pending path. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` — `POST /:id/init` (lines 88–95) then `PATCH /:id/settings` (lines 118–127).

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: only a server log today; the UI shows a **success** toast, which is misleading because the shared clone path was actually dropped.

#### 10.7.10 You Support this community but it's set to Block — nothing is being kept — `warn` (id: community-support-without-backup-mode)

*Where shown:* Communities page — per-community row (the "Support" intent chip vs the Backup-mode segmented control). Gap: not currently flagged; both controls render silently and independently.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `CommunityRow.subscription.support === true && subscription.backupMode === 'block'`. Block forces `targetBytes = 0` (the `backupMode === 'block' ? 0` computation, and `planTargets` leftover → 0), so "Support" (pin to add redundancy) pins **zero bytes** — it has no effect. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.service.ts` — `targetBytes` calc (line 168) + `planTargets()` (line 128); UI intent toggles in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/communities/CommunitiesPage.tsx` (lines 74–101).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "Support" means *pin this publisher's **public** files so there's another copy keeping them alive* — but a backup mode of **Block** reserves 0 bytes, so you're supporting in name only. *Why it matters:* You think you're helping keep this community's content secure, but no bytes are actually pinned. *Options:* radios — **Recommended** (a bounded share of your budget) vs **Full** (all their files, up to budget). *Action button:* "Keep this community" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** `PATCH /api/communities/:id {backupMode:'recommended'}` — the safe minimal action that makes Support effective within the budget. Reversible one-click. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.router.ts` — `PATCH /:id` (lines 34–50) → `setCommunitySubscription()` (lines 187–199).

**Notes / gaps.** Charter tie: Support is a narrow **per-community opt-in**, never a public gateway. Gap: not flagged today.

#### 10.7.11 No room left in your community backup budget — `warn` (id: community-budget-exhausted)

*Where shown:* Communities page — storage-budget header + per-row "Keeping secure / target". Gap: not surfaced as a verdict.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** In `computeStorageMath`, `growable = max(0, freeOutsideIpfs − reservedHeadroom)` is 0 (or near 0), so `communityBudgetBytes` clamps to ~0 even for Full communities; `planTargets` then assigns 0 to every community. Fires when **`totalDiskBytes > 0`** (a real, measurable disk — distinguishing it from §10.7.2) **AND** `communityBudgetBytes === 0` **AND** ≥1 community is Recommended/Full. The headroom floor is `max(10% of volume, 10 GiB)` (`HEADROOM_FRACTION 0.1` / `HEADROOM_MIN_BYTES` 10 GiB). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.service.ts` — `computeStorageMath()` (lines 61–68) + `planTargets()` (lines 105–130).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFB always keeps a **headroom floor** (10% of the volume, at least 10 GiB) free and never spends past it, so with the disk this full there's no budget to back up communities you chose to Support/Full. *Why it matters:* Full/Recommended communities get a `targetBytes` of 0 — their "Keeping secure" reads "0 / 0 B" — so none of their content is being kept on this computer. *Options:* radios — lower a community's backup mode to Block/Recommended (the budget input itself can't be raised past `growable` by design). *Action button:* "Lower backup mode" (blue); freeing disk is manual. Dismissible offer.

**(C) The fix.** **No charter-safe auto-fix** (LFB won't cross the headroom floor or delete files). Manual: free disk space, or lower a community's backup mode via `PATCH /api/communities/:id {backupMode:'block'|'recommended'}`. *Fix in:* no auto-fix beyond mode change — `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.router.ts` `PATCH /:id` (lines 34–50) / `PUT /budget` (lines 22–31, clamped in `setCommunityBudget` → `computeStorageMath`).

**Notes / gaps.** Interacts with IPFS-datastore accounting: `freeOutsideIpfs` already excludes committed pin bytes. Guard: this is the `totalDiskBytes > 0` sibling of the BAD measurement-failure §10.7.2. Gap: not surfaced as a verdict.

#### 10.7.12 This community isn't fully backed up yet — `warn` (id: community-backup-below-target)

*Where shown:* Communities page — the "Keeping secure" column (secured / target bytes). Gap: no banner rollup, and see the false-alarm caveat below.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `subscription.backupMode !== 'block' && keepingSecureBytes < targetBytes`. Today `keepingSecureBytes` is honestly reported as **0** until a sync pass wires the pin plan, so every non-Block community currently reads under-target. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.service.ts` — `getCommunitiesPage()` (lines 157–174; `keepingSecureBytes: 0`, `targetBytes` at 168); UI keeping-cell in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/communities/CommunitiesPage.tsx` (lines 102–109).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The planner reserved budget (target) for this community, but the actual pinned bytes are still below it — the backup hasn't caught up (or the sync pass that pins community files isn't running). *Why it matters:* You've opted to keep this community's content, but coverage is incomplete; if the sync never moves, your intended redundancy doesn't exist. *Options:* none — informational, plus a pointer to check that background sync is on and the storage is synced. *Action button:* none / "Open Sync settings" (blue) as a route-out.

**(C) The fix.** **No direct button** — coverage is achieved by the background sync pass pinning toward target. Manual next step: ensure the background sync process is installed+on (Sync page) and this computer has room. *Fix in:* no auto-fix — the pin path lives in the sync pass (out of this partition); the planner is `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.service.ts` `planTargets()` (lines 105–130).

**Notes / gaps.** **Important false-alarm guard: `keepingSecureBytes` is hardcoded 0 (pin accounting not yet wired), so this would fire for ALL non-Block communities today.** Only surface it once real coverage is reported — otherwise it is pure noise. Gap: pin accounting not implemented.

#### 10.7.13 Can't confirm how many copies of this community exist — `warn` (id: community-redundancy-unknown)

*Where shown:* Communities page — the "Redundancy" column (renders "—"). Gap: arguably **neutral/informational** rather than warn until peer discovery lands.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `CommunityRow.redundancy === null` — set **unconditionally** because there is no peer/pinner data source yet. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/communities/communities.service.ts` — `getCommunitiesPage()` (line 170, `redundancy: null`); UI in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/communities/CommunitiesPage.tsx` (lines 110–113).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Redundancy = how many **independent machines** are pinning this community's files (higher = safer). LFB doesn't have peer data for this community yet. *Why it matters:* It can't tell you whether your Support meaningfully adds a needed copy or is redundant with others — **this is informational, not a fault**. *Options:* none. *Action button:* none (informational only — arguably no arrow button per §2).

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix** — requires peer/pinner discovery not yet implemented. Manual: none. *Fix in:* no auto-fix — peer data source not implemented; the future accessor is `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/peers.service.ts`.

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: should likely be **neutral** (informational, no arrow) rather than an amber warning until peer discovery exists — currently would show on every community row.

#### 10.7.14 The hidden tracking directory is turned off for this storage — `warn` (id: lfbridge-tracking-disabled)

*Where shown:* Storage settings — "Hidden tracking directory" section. Gap: no verdict; only the toggle state communicates it.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `StorageSettings.lfbridge.enabled === false`. When off, `ensureBackingLocations` **skips** creating/maintaining `.lfbridge/` on this computer, so the device registry + manifest + fingerprint index for this storage aren't kept here — the storage can't travel/sync from this machine. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage-settings.service.ts` — `readStorageSettings()` (lines 160–164); skip in `storage.service.ts` `ensureBackingLocations()` (line 460); UI in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/storages/StorageSettingsPage.tsx` (lines 54–68).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The hidden `.lfbridge/` directory is where LFB keeps this storage's tracking data (device registry, manifest, fingerprint index) **on this computer**. *Why it matters:* Turning it off means this machine stops participating in the storage's sync — it won't record itself or carry the file list. Only turn it off if you deliberately want this computer excluded. *Options:* none — one-click toggle. *Action button:* "Turn tracking on" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** `PATCH /api/storages/:id/settings {lfbridge:{enabled:true}}` → the next pass recreates `<root>/.lfbridge/`. Safe one-click. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` — `PATCH /:id/settings` (lines 118–127) → `writeStorageSettings()` (lines 181–184).

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: no verdict — only the toggle state communicates it.

#### 10.7.15 This storage is too large to fully index (5,000-file cap) — `warn` (id: index-file-cap-hit)

*Where shown:* Storage detail, after "Index files" — should surface near the file table. **Gap: `capped` is computed but not returned to the client, so the UI cannot show it yet.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** During `indexStorageFiles`, the metadata walk hits `MAX_FILES` (5000): `capped = collected.length >= MAX_FILES` is true, so large files beyond the cap are never fingerprinted or listed. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/tracking.service.ts` — `indexStorageFiles()` (`MAX_FILES` const at line 27; cap checks at lines 98/106/126; warn at line 148).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The index stops at 5,000 large files to stay responsive, so an oversized storage may have **untracked** files beyond the cap. *Why it matters:* Those extra files won't be fingerprinted, change-detected, or synced — they're invisible to LFB. *Options:* none in the popup — guidance to narrow scope. *Action button:* "Open mapped directories" (blue) as a route-out; no direct fix.

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix.** Manual: reduce the storage's scope (mapped dirs), raise the big-file threshold to shrink the candidate set, or split into multiple storages. Surfacing this requires returning `capped` from the index endpoint (currently only logged). *Fix in:* no auto-fix — return-shape change needed in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.service.ts` `indexStorageById()` (lines 375–379, add a `capped` flag) + router `POST /:id/index` (lines 99–106).

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: `capped` is computed but not returned to the client — the toast currently says "Indexed N files" with no hint that files were skipped.

#### 10.7.16 This storage's descriptor couldn't be read — `warn` (id: descriptor-corrupt)

*Where shown:* Storages tab — a folder that **has** a `storage.yaml` but shows as "not set up". **Gap: currently indistinguishable from truly-uninitialized (§10.7.3) — needs a distinct "descriptor present but unreadable" signal, not the same badge.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `readDescriptor(root)` **throws** while parsing YAML → the catch logs `readDescriptor failed` and returns null. `buildRow` then treats `initialized = !!null = false`, so a **present-but-corrupt** `storage.yaml` masquerades as an uninitialized candidate and falls back to convention-derived name/type. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.service.ts` — `readDescriptor()` (lines 77–87; catch at 83–86) → `buildRow()` (line 269); path resolution in `descriptorPath()` (lines 69–75).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFB found a `storage.yaml` here but it's **malformed** and couldn't be parsed, so the storage's identity / clones / mapped config is being ignored. *Why it matters:* The storage looks unconfigured even though real config exists on disk — and re-initializing blindly could **overwrite the real descriptor**. *Options:* none — read-only guidance. *Action button:* none — do **not** offer re-Initialize here (it would clobber the real file); route to the log/file instead.

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix** (re-init would overwrite the user's real descriptor). Manual: open `<root>/storage.yaml` (or `<root>/.lfbridge/storage.yaml`) and repair the YAML; check the server log for the parse error. *Fix in:* no auto-fix — descriptor path resolution in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.service.ts` `descriptorPath()` (lines 69–75).

**Notes / gaps.** Critically distinct from §10.7.3 (no file at all) but currently renders with the **same** "not set up" badge — the key gap. Guard: never present the one-click Initialize for this case.

#### 10.7.17 This computer couldn't register itself in the storage — `warn` (id: self-device-write-failed)

*Where shown:* Storage detail / settings, after Initialize. Gap: failure is only a server log; no success/failure signal reaches the UI — initialization still reports success.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** In `ensureStorage`, `writeSelfDevice(root)` **throws** (e.g. permissions on `.lfbridge/devices/`) and is swallowed by a try/catch that logs `writeSelfDevice … failed`. The device registry then lacks this machine's entry, so peers/other computers won't see this computer for the storage. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.service.ts` — `ensureStorage()` (lines 138–144, the `writeSelfDevice` try/catch); the write itself in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` `writeSelfDevice()`, invoked from `ensureStorage()` (line 141).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Each computer must write a **device file** into the storage's travelling registry so your other machines know this computer carries the storage. That write failed here. *Why it matters:* This machine is **invisible** to the storage's sync mesh — peers won't fetch from or sync to it for this storage. Likely a permissions issue on the `.lfbridge/` directory. *Options:* none — one-click retry. *Action button:* "Retry registration" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** Auto-fix: retry `writeSelfDevice(root)` (idempotent) — expose via a small endpoint or fold into a re-Initialize. Manual fallback: fix permissions on `<root>/.lfbridge/`, then re-Initialize. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` `writeSelfDevice()`; invoked from `storage.service.ts` `ensureStorage()` (line 141).

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: the failure is caught and only logged; initialization reports success, so the user has no signal their machine is unregistered.

#### 10.7.18 You haven't set up your Personal storage yet — `warn` (id: no-personal-storage)

*Where shown:* Storages tab (no Personal row); also **gates** the Transcribe / Get-AI-details actions on loose files (they silently route to a setup wizard). Gap: the wizard is reachable from media actions but the Storages tab has **no proactive banner** offering it.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `listStoragesPage().personal === null` (no discovered personal storage). Equivalently, artifact-placement's `ownerIndex` reports `personalExists === false`, and `resolveArtifactPlacement` returns `needsSetup === true` for any file the mapped dirs don't own — so derived artifacts (transcripts, descriptions) for loose files have no home. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.service.ts` — `listStoragesPage()` (line 306, the personal find); `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/artifact-placement.service.ts` — `buildOwnerIndex()` (line 117) + `resolveArtifactPlacement()` (lines 182–185, `needsSetup`).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The Personal storage is the default home for large files under `~` that aren't inside a repo or company storage. *Why it matters:* Without it, transcripts/descriptions and syncing of your loose personal files have nowhere consistent to go — media actions dead-end at a setup wizard. *Options:* one checkbox/radio — **"Make it a dedicated Git repo"** (versioned + synced) vs **"Plain folder"**. *Action button:* "Create Personal storage" (blue).

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/storages/personal/create {dedicatedRepo:true|false}` → `createPersonalStorage()`: `mkdir` the canonical root (`~/BGit/Bryan_git/personal_large_files_bridge/`), optional `git init`, `ensureStorage(root,'personal')`, and (if `dedicatedRepo`) turn on the dedicated-repo backing so artifacts route into the repo. Safe, **idempotent** (an existing Personal is returned as-is). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/storage.router.ts` — `POST /personal/create` (lines 74–85) → `storage.service.ts` `createPersonalStorage()` (lines 358–373).

**Notes / gaps.** Ties to the charter's Personal-storage-as-default-home model and to §10.7.1 (choosing the dedicated-repo option here gives Personal its git backbone up front). Gap: no proactive banner on the Storages tab — the offer only appears reactively when a media action needs a home.

## 10.8 Devices, peers & the Scans/Sync verdict

This category owns the **Devices / Peers** page (the roster of every computer that carries your files), the **View one device** page, and the **Scans** page's sync verdict. The through-line is the charter promise *"if you lose a laptop, your files are safely on your other computers"* — so most warnings here are really about **backup freshness and roster truthfulness**, not raw counts. Several conditions below are **gaps**: the backend already computes or logs them, but no banner is wired yet. The generic *"the last background sync failed"* worker banner is owned by **§10.9** (sync-worker health); this category owns the **per-unit reasons** behind it and the device-roster verdicts.

The registry `scope` for these is `device` (or `computer` for the roster rollup, `global` for the Scans poll). All read the same three data sources: `config.yaml→computer` (self), machine-local `peers.yaml`, and each storage's travelling `devices/` registry — unioned by `deviceRows()`.

#### 10.8.1 "N computers keep copies" shows green even when every peer is stale/offline — `bad` (id: devices-green-hides-stale-peers)

*Where shown:* Devices / Peers page, top-of-page `StatusBanner`. **Gap: the freshness check is not yet wired** — today the banner is green whenever any peer exists.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The page verdict is computed **purely from a count**: `otherCount = rows.filter(d => !d.isSelf).length`. When `otherCount > 0` it renders a **green** `state="ok"` banner ("N other computers keep copies of your files / Your synced files are backed up across these machines") with **no inspection of any peer's `lastSeen`**. So three peers all last seen 60 days ago still render fully green. The correct verdict must fold each non-self row's freshness: `worst(...rows.filter(d=>!d.isSelf).map(d => seenHealth(d.lastSeen)))`, where `seenHealth(iso)` returns `ok` (<24h), `warn` (24h–7d), or `neutral` (≥7d / null / NaN). Green only if ≥1 other peer is `ok`; amber if the best other peer is 1–7d; red/neutral if all others are >7d or never seen. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/DevicesPage.tsx` — `DevicesPage()`, `otherCount` (line 144), the count-only ok-banner render (lines 160–168), and the existing but **page-unused** `seenHealth()` (lines 26–33); rollup helper `worst()` already exists in `components/ui/health.ts`. Backing data (per-row `lastSeen`) from `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` — `deviceRows()` (self `lastSeen=now` line 247; peer `lastSeen` line 269; registry `lastSeen=rec.updatedAt` line 304).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The page told you your files were backed up on other machines, but that verdict counted computers, not *live* backups. A computer that hasn't checked in recently isn't mirroring your recent changes. *Why it matters:* If every "backup" peer is offline and you lose this Mac, files you changed since they last synced are gone; a false-green directly undercuts the whole point of the app. *Options:* none — informational + navigation. *Action button:* "Go to stalest computer" (deep-links to that device's View-one-device page) or "Open Scans" to confirm this machine is publishing its manifest. Not destructive.

**(C) The fix.** No backend action — this is a **frontend rollup fix** in `DevicesPage.tsx`: fold `seenHealth` over non-self rows into the banner `state` so the color reflects freshness, then route the button to the stalest peer or to Scans. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/DevicesPage.tsx` — replace the `otherCount > 0` green branch (lines 160–168) with a `worst(seenHealth…)` verdict; **no auto-fix for the underlying staleness** (that needs the peer to come online — see §10.8.4).

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not yet wired — this is the highest-severity item in the category because it silently reassures the user their mirror is fresh when it is stale. Guard against over-firing: a brand-new peer with a null `lastSeen` should read as `neutral`/amber, not immediately red.

#### 10.8.2 A synced file list has an unresolved Git merge conflict (quarantined) — `bad` (id: committed-manifest-merge-conflict)

*Where shown:* Should surface on the Scans page and/or the owning repo page. **Gap: only logs an ERROR and writes a quarantine file today — no banner.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** When two computers edit the **same file's manifest region** on a Git-backed storage, Git leaves conflict markers in `<repoRoot>/.lfbridge/manifest.yaml`. `readCommittedManifest()` scans for `/^(<{7}|={7}|>{7})/m`; on a hit it **copies the file to `manifest.conflicted.yaml`**, logs an ERROR, and **throws** `Merge conflict in committed manifest` — so that unit's sync **aborts and retains its prior state** (the app never trusts half-merged data). It also throws on `Corrupt` / `Invalid` manifest content. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/manifest.service.ts` — `hasConflictMarkers()` (lines 25–27) and `readCommittedManifest()` conflict branch (lines 47–60, throws at 59); consumed by `syncStorageUnitInner()` at `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.service.ts` line 437. Deterministic per-path serialization (`serializeDeterministic()`, lines 116–133) minimizes but cannot eliminate same-file conflicts.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The small text file that lists what to sync travels between your computers over Git. Two machines edited overlapping entries and Git couldn't auto-merge, so LFBridge safely refused to load the half-merged file and kept the last good copy. *Why it matters:* That repo's file list is **frozen** until the conflict is resolved — its files stop syncing (bytes stop reconciling), even though nothing is corrupted. This is rare. *Options (guided resolve, since entries are per-path):* ◉ "Use my version" · ○ "Use their version" · ○ "Let me resolve it manually". *Action button:* "Resolve & sync" (red/destructive treatment + confirm, because it overwrites the committed manifest). If manual is chosen the button becomes "Show me the file" (opens `<repo>/.lfbridge/manifest.yaml`).

**(C) The fix.** No fully-safe auto-merge exists (conflicting intent needs a human decision). Guided path: pick a side (or accept the app's reconciliation), write the resolved **deterministic** form back, commit, then re-run Sync now. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/manifest.service.ts` — `writeCommittedManifest()` (lines 82–107) already writes the resolved deterministic form; **no UI/endpoint currently exposes resolution** — routes today only to the log + the `manifest.conflicted.yaml` quarantine file. Re-sync via `POST /api/sync/:worker` (`sync.router.ts`).

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not wired to any banner. This is one concrete cause behind §10.8.3's per-unit `last_error`.

#### 10.8.3 Per-unit sync errors (repo missing / IPFS down / merge conflict) not shown on Scans — `bad` (id: unit-sync-error-not-surfaced-on-scans)

*Where shown:* Scans page (should show the *specific* failing repo + reason; currently only logged + written to `status.yaml`). **Gap: the Scans verdict never reads any unit's `last_error`.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `runUnitSync` records a `UnitStatus.last_error` via `markUnitError()` for each distinct per-unit failure: **`repo missing`** (the repo's working tree was moved/deleted — `preflightError()`), and **`IPFS node unreachable`** (`ipfs.health() !== 'ok'`). The committed-manifest read can additionally **throw** merge-conflict/corrupt/invalid (§10.8.2), aborting the unit. All of these set `status.last_error` or abort the unit — **but the Scans page verdict is derived only from `WorkerState.lastRunOk`/`overdue`**, so it can say "a sync failed" generically while the specific broken repo and reason stay invisible. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.service.ts` — `markUnitError()` (lines 607–610), preflight `repo missing` (check lines 117–121, set line 294), `IPFS node unreachable` (lines 122–126). Schema: `UnitStatus.last_error` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/shared/src/schemas.ts` line 403. **No frontend reader of `last_error` exists** in the devices/sync surfaces.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* One of your synced folders failed its last pass, and each cause has a different fix — so you need the exact message, not just "a sync failed." *Why it matters:* A specific repo has stopped syncing: its files aren't being mirrored until the named cause is cleared. *Options:* the popup lists each failing unit with its reason and a targeted action per row (not a generic retry). *Action button:* per cause — "Re-point folder" / "Forget repo" (repo missing), "Start IPFS" (node unreachable → cross-ref §10.2 IPFS-down home category), "Resolve conflict" (→ §10.8.2).

**(C) The fix.** No single button — the fix is to **surface `last_error` per unit** on the Scans page (or each owning repo/storage page) with the cause-specific action: `repo missing` → re-point or forget that repo; `IPFS node unreachable` → start the IPFS node; merge conflict → resolve the quarantined `manifest.conflicted.yaml` then re-sync. *Fix in:* wire a GET that returns each `UnitStatus.last_error` (written in `sync.service.ts`) into the Scans frontend; merge-conflict resolution path in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/manifest.service.ts` `readCommittedManifest()` (lines 36–74). **No auto-fix — routes to the per-cause action above.**

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not yet wired. This is the concrete gap behind the generic "see the transfer job below" banner text that currently has nothing specific to show. The generic worker-failed/overdue banner itself is owned by **§10.9**; this warning is the per-unit detail that must hang off it.

#### 10.8.4 A backup computer was last seen 1–7 days ago — `warn` (id: peer-stale-1-to-7-days)

*Where shown:* Devices / Peers table "Last seen" cell (per-row amber text) **and** the View-one-device page top banner (drives the whole banner state). Not yet rolled up into a **page-level** Devices banner — see §10.8.1.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `seenHealth(iso)` returns **`warn`** (amber) when `24h ≤ (now − lastSeen) < 7d`; `ok` when `<24h`; `neutral` when `≥7d` or `lastSeen` is null/NaN. In the table this only tints the cell text; on the device page it sets the `StatusBanner` state. `lastSeen` source: registry `rec.updatedAt` / `peers.yaml` last_seen. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/DevicesPage.tsx` — `seenHealth()` (lines 26–33), cell render (lines 135–140); and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/ViewOneDevicePage.tsx` — `seenHealth()` (lines 28–35), banner (lines 198–214). Backend `lastSeen` from `devices.service.ts` `deviceRows()` (lines 262–308).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* This computer last checked in 1–7 days ago, so file changes you made **here** since then haven't been confirmed pinned there yet — its backup may be a little stale. *Why it matters:* Recent edits may not be mirrored on that machine yet; it usually self-heals when that computer next runs its 15-minute sync. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Sync now" (re-publish this machine's latest manifest so the peer picks it up faster on its next pass) — plus a plain-text next step: *"Open LFBridge on {device} and confirm Automatic syncing is on (Scans page)."* Improvable → **dismissible** offer.

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix targets a remote device** — the stale peer must come online and run its own sync. The only local lever is re-publishing this machine's manifest so the peer converges sooner. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` — `POST /:worker` (re-runs this machine's sync only); **no endpoint can reach a remote device** — routes to the manual "power it on / confirm sync is on" step.

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: staleness is per-row/per-device only; there is no page-level Devices banner that fires when a peer is stale — that rollup is §10.8.1.

#### 10.8.5 A backup computer hasn't been seen in over a week — or never — `warn` (id: peer-long-gone-or-never-seen)

*Where shown:* Devices / Peers table "Last seen" cell **and** the View-one-device banner. **Gap: currently rendered as calm slate `neutral`, arguably too quiet for a backup peer that has dropped off.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `seenHealth` returns **`neutral`** when `(now − lastSeen) ≥ 7 days`, **or** `lastSeen` is null (never seen), **or** the timestamp is unparseable. On the device page this yields a slate banner headlined "Last seen {relativeTime}" or "Not seen yet" — visually identical to a healthy quiet state, giving no alarm that a supposed backup peer effectively dropped off. Distinguish **"never seen"** (a `peers.yaml` entry that never joined — a typo'd Peer ID or a machine that never finished setup) from **"went quiet"** (a real machine now offline/retired). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/DevicesPage.tsx` — `seenHealth()` (lines 26–33); `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/ViewOneDevicePage.tsx` — `seenHealth()` (lines 28–35), banner state (line 199).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* A peer gone more than 7 days is no longer a reliable live backup — files you changed here in the last week are almost certainly not mirrored there. *Why it matters:* If this is your only other copy and it's retired/offline, recent changes have no second home. *Options:* ◉ "Bring it back online" (guidance: open LFBridge on that machine) · ○ "Forget this computer" (remove it from the roster so counts reflect reality). *Action button:* "Forget this computer" (destructive → red + confirm) **only for `source === "peer"`** rows; self/registry rows are not forgettable.

**(C) The fix.** Two manual paths: (1) bring the machine online, or (2) **forget the peer**, which already exists — `ViewOneDevicePage.removePeer()` calls `api.removePeer(device.id)`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/peers/peers.router.ts` — `DELETE /:id` (lines 21–28) → `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/store-model/peers.service.ts` `removePeer()` (~lines 15–24). Forget UI is exposed only for `source === "peer"` (DevicesPage rowMenu lines 184–190; device-page Remove button lines 185–192). Bringing it online has **no endpoint** — manual.

**Notes / gaps.** Gap: `neutral` is arguably too quiet for a >7-day-gone backup peer; product may want amber. "Never seen" + neutral is especially easy to miss. Overlaps §10.8.6 (`peer-known-not-in-any-storage`) — that one is discriminated by `storageCount === 0` (half-joined), this one by age; a peer can be both.

#### 10.8.6 Known from your peers list — not yet seen in a synced storage — `warn` (id: peer-known-not-in-any-storage)

*Where shown:* View-one-device page (`StatusBanner` sub-line + a Hardware-section note).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `device.storageCount === 0 && device.source === "peer"`: the machine exists in `peers.yaml` but appears in **no** storage's travelling `devices/` registry, so it has never actually participated in a synced storage (likely added by Peer ID only and never finished joining a shared location). `storageCount` is incremented only when a registry file for that id is found. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/ViewOneDevicePage.tsx` — banner sub (lines 207–213), hardware note (lines 258–263); `storageCount` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` `deviceRows()` — peer rows created with `storageCount: 0` (line 271), incremented only in the registry union (`existing.storageCount += 1`, line 291).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* This peer is **half-joined** — you told LFBridge about it (Peer ID/label) but it has never written itself into a shared storage's device registry, so it isn't actually pinning your files yet. *Why it matters:* It counts toward your device list but is **not a real backup**; treating it as one over-states your redundancy. *Options:* ○ "Finish setup on that computer" (guidance) · ○ "Forget this computer" (if added in error). *Action button:* "Forget this computer" (destructive → red + confirm) or, when keeping it, an OK/close.

**(C) The fix.** No auto-fix from here — the **other machine must act**: open LFBridge there, sign in with the same Google account, and add/enable at least one shared storage so it joins and starts pinning. If it was a mistake, forget it. *Fix in:* forget path `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/peers/peers.router.ts` — `DELETE /:id` (lines 21–28); **no endpoint** completes the remote join — routes to the manual setup step.

**Notes / gaps.** Distinct from §10.8.5 (long-gone): this peer may be **new, not retired**. `storageCount` is the discriminator between a real synced device and a bare `peers.yaml` entry. Resolves on its own once the peer joins a synced storage (same path that fills in §10.8.10's hardware fingerprint).

#### 10.8.7 Only this computer so far — your files aren't backed up anywhere else — `warn` (id: only-this-computer-not-backed-up)

*Where shown:* Devices / Peers page, top-of-page `StatusBanner`. **Currently rendered `neutral` (slate); flagged here as `warn` per the not-backed-up intent** — product may keep it neutral or promote to amber as an offer to get backed up.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `onlySelf = !isLoading && rows.length === 1 && rows[0]?.isSelf`. The device list **always injects THIS machine** as the first row, so a length-1 list means no `peers.yaml` entry and no other device in any storage registry — i.e. zero redundancy. When true, the page shows the slate "Only this computer so far" banner and a "How to add a computer" disclosure below the table. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/DevicesPage.tsx` — `DevicesPage()` `onlySelf` (line 53), banner (lines 154–159), disclosure (lines 194–207). Backing self-injection: `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` `deviceRows()` self always injected (lines 240–251).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* With a single device there is **no redundancy** — if this Mac is lost, stolen, or its disk dies, every git-ignored large file synced only here is gone. IPFS pinning only protects you when a **second** machine also pins. *Why it matters:* One drive failure = total data loss for the large files LFBridge manages. *Options:* none (adding a device is a manual action on the other machine). *Action button:* "How to add a computer" (deep-links to / expands the existing instructions); optionally "Copy this computer's Peer ID" to speed manual peering. Improvable → **dismissible**.

**(C) The fix.** **No safe one-click auto-fix** — adding a device happens on the *other* machine: install LFBridge there, sign in with the same Google account, and it auto-joins the swarm and starts pinning copies. *Fix in:* **no backend "add device" endpoint exists** — joining happens when the other machine writes itself into the shared storage registry / `peers.yaml`. (Peer *removal* exists — `peers.router.ts DELETE /:id` — but not add.) Routes to the "How to add a computer" disclosure (`DevicesPage.tsx` lines 194–207).

**Notes / gaps.** Directly serves the charter goal "so if you lose a laptop, your files are safely on your other computers." Contrast the green ok banner shown when `otherCount > 0` (§10.8.1) — which itself has the freshness bug.

#### 10.8.8 Scans page couldn't refresh — status you see may be stale — `warn` (id: scans-page-poll-fetch-failure)

*Where shown:* Scans page. **Gap: not surfaced — the failure is only mirrored to `error.err`; the UI stays on a benign state.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `useQuery({queryKey:['syncPage']})` `error` is truthy — the `GET /api/sync/` request failed (network, a **401** when dev-auth is off and the Google session expired, or a backend **500** from `syncPageData` throwing). On the **10-second background refetch** this produces **no toast**; the code only mirrors it to `error.err` via `clientLog.warn`. When `!data`, the page verdict shows a benign neutral **"Loading…" forever**; on a later poll failure nothing visible changes (stale data persists). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — `useQuery` (line 26), `useEffect(error) → clientLog.warn` (lines 29–31), `!data → 'Loading…'` neutral verdict (line 36). Backend 500 path: `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` `GET /` (500 envelope lines 15–19).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The Scans status couldn't be refreshed, so the on/off/overdue readings you see may be stale — the app can't currently confirm the background jobs' state. *Why it matters:* You might believe syncing is healthy when the page simply hasn't heard back; a silently expired login hides real problems. Likely causes: backend not running, auth session expired, transient network. *Options:* none — a retry + conditional re-login. *Action button:* "Retry" (refetch the query); if the failure is a **401** (dev-auth off + expired Google session), the button becomes "Sign in again".

**(C) The fix.** Frontend: react-query refetch on `['syncPage']`. On a 401, prompt re-login; if the backend is down, guide to restart. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` (refetch `['syncPage']`); endpoint health at `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` `GET /` (lines 12–20). **No destructive action.**

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not yet wired as a banner. Per MEMORY, API routes 401 to curl when dev-auth is off and the dev cookie origin drifts — a stale session would make this fire and currently be invisible.

#### 10.8.9 Device roster loaded with a source read failing (silent partial data) — `warn` (id: device-list-registry-union-partial-failure)

*Where shown:* Devices / Peers page. **Gap: not surfaced — the request returns 200 with fewer rows and no signal that a source failed.**

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `deviceRows()` wraps the `peers.yaml` read (step 2) and the per-storage registry union (step 3) in `try/catch` that **only `log.warn` and continue**. If `peers.yaml` or a storage's `devices/` dir is unreadable (e.g. an unmounted external/cloud drive), those computers **silently vanish** from the table while the request still returns 200 — so the user may see **fewer devices than truly exist** and believe they have less/no backup. Individual unreadable device files are likewise skipped with `log.warn`. Only a *total* failure would 500 and error the query; **partial** failures are invisible. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` — `deviceRows()` peers catch (lines 276–278), registry-union catch (lines 312–314); `readDevices()` skips unreadable files with `log.warn`. Frontend: `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/DevicesPage.tsx` `useQuery(['devices'])` (line 51) has **no partial-failure branch**.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* The roster may be incomplete — one source of device info (your peers list or a shared storage's registry) couldn't be read this load, so some computers might be missing from the table. *Why it matters:* Their files/pins are unaffected; only the display is partial — but a missing peer reads as "less backed up" and could wrongly relax the not-backed-up warning (§10.8.7) and the green rollup (§10.8.1). *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Retry" (refetch `['devices']`) plus a plain next step: *"Make sure your external/cloud storage drives are mounted, then reload."*

**(C) The fix.** No destructive action. Backend must **collect and return the read errors** (a partial-failure flag naming the sources that errored) so the frontend can show an amber "some devices may be missing" banner with a Retry. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` `deviceRows()` (surface the swallowed errors at lines 276–278, 312–314); frontend banner + refetch in `DevicesPage.tsx`. **No auto-fix — routes to "mount the drive and reload."**

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not yet wired. Especially relevant on cloud-mounted storages (per MEMORY, dir rollups run slow/fail on cloud mounts). Interacts with §10.8.1/§10.8.7: a dropped source can under-count peers and produce a false "not backed up" or, worse, hide a stale peer.

#### 10.8.10 No hardware fingerprint yet — `neutral` (id: device-no-hardware-fingerprint)

*Where shown:* View-one-device page, Hardware-fingerprint section (plain slate paragraph; no banner, no action). Correctly quiet.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `device.hardware === null` — true for a bare `peers.yaml` entry. `deviceRows()` sets `hardware: null` for peer rows and only fills it in when a storage registry file carries `rec.device.hardware.platform`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/ViewOneDevicePage.tsx` — hardware branch (lines 242–264, else at 258–263); nulling in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` `deviceRows()` — peer `hardware: null` (line 270), registry enrich only when `rec.device.hardware.platform` present (lines 293, 305).

**(B) The popup.** *Informational only* (no arrow button per §2). *What this is:* The fingerprint (model/chip/RAM/disk/screen) travels in the storage registry and only appears once that machine writes itself into a synced storage; a `peers.yaml`-only entry has none yet. *Why it matters:* purely cosmetic — nothing is wrong with your files. *Options / Action button:* none.

**(C) The fix.** **No fix** — resolves on its own once the peer joins a synced storage (same manual path as §10.8.6). *Fix in:* none.

**Notes / gaps.** Correctly neutral/informational; listed for completeness of the device-page verdicts.

#### 10.8.11 This device is no longer in your registry (stale link) — `neutral` (id: device-not-found-stale-link)

*Where shown:* View-one-device page, `StatusBanner` that replaces the whole page body. Correctly neutral — navigation, not an alarm.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The `useQuery` for `api.device(deviceId)` (with `retry: false`) errors or returns no device. The backend returns **404 `{ok:false, error:'device not found'}`** when `deviceRow(id)` finds no row with that id — a stale bookmark/deep-link after the device was forgotten or its id changed. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/devices/ViewOneDevicePage.tsx` — error/`!device` branch (lines 115–126); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/peers/devices.router.ts` `GET /:id` (404 at line 25, lines 22–31); `deviceRow()` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/storage/devices.service.ts` (lines 329–331).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* A dead link — the device id no longer resolves, usually because the peer was forgotten or the registry changed. *Why it matters:* Nothing is broken with your files; this is just an out-of-date link. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Back to Devices / Peers" (`Link to='/devices'`).

**(C) The fix.** No fix action needed — the safe next step is navigation. *Fix in:* frontend navigation only (`ViewOneDevicePage.tsx` back link, lines 100–104). **No backend action.**

**Notes / gaps.** Correctly neutral. **Under-reporting risk:** a genuine backend **500** (non-404) also lands in this same error branch and is displayed identically to a benign stale link — a real server error should be distinguished (an amber/red "couldn't load this device" state) rather than shown as a calm "stale link."

## 10.9 Background workers, schedule, Git backbone & sync resilience

This category owns the *backbone that keeps files moving on their own*: the three launchd background workers (transfer/`sync`, `device` registration, `scan`/Discovery), the in-app live watcher, the schedule watchdog + self-heal, the Git text backbone (pull→merge→commit→push) that coordinates devices and manifests, and the session-level "you've been away / you've never synced" signals. It ties directly to [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) (the F1–F6 failure taxonomy, the watchdog §3, always-push-when-ahead, and the foreign-committer "Bryan 26 Tower" auto-commit reality) and [devices.mdx](./devices.mdx) §12. Almost every worker state is computed by the **same three functions** — `workerState()` (backend truth), `isWorkerOverdue()` (the silent-stall proxy), and `workerHealth()` (the frontend color ladder) — so the sub-warnings below share detection machinery and differ mainly in *which worker* and *which rung of the ladder*.

Two important structural notes the reader should carry through every subsection:
