* **The Scans page top verdict tracks ONLY the transfer (`sync`) worker.** `device`, `scan`, and `watcher` health render as *cards* below the banner, never in the page headline. So a red device/scan card can sit under a green banner — a recurring "promote into the verdict" gap flagged throughout.
* **The Git backbone failures (merge conflict / auth / remote) and the trigger-script-missing crash are detected in code but NOT wired to any banner today** — they only reach `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err`. These are the highest-value gaps in the whole category because they violate [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) §9 AC#7 ("nothing fails silent").

Shared detection code, referenced repeatedly below:
* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/schedule.service.ts` — `workerState()` (lines 94–112, computes `installed`/`enabled`/`overdue`/`lastRunOk`), `isWorkerOverdue()` (lines 86–92), `intervalFor()` (lines 73–78), `control()` (lines 150–184, the install/enable/disable/uninstall verbs), `reconcileWorkerSchedules()` (lines 192–226, the self-heal), `buildInstallOpts()` + `triggerScriptPath()` (lines 129–148 / 44–57), `stampRun()` (lines 249–256), `ensureDeviceWorkerDefaultOn()` (lines 236–247), `syncPageData()` (lines 114–125).
* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — `workerHealth()` (lines 17–23, the neutral→warn→bad→warn→ok ladder), the `verdict` IIFE (lines 35–70), `ipfsDown` (line 32), `watcherHealth()` (lines 118–122).
* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/watchdog.service.ts` — `tick()` / `runWorkerInProcess()` (lines 45–84), the in-process safety net that runs the pass *and* calls `reconcileWorkerSchedules()` every 5 min.

---

#### 10.9.1 Background job launcher file is missing — the schedule will crash on every fire — `bad` (id: worker-trigger-script-missing)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not wired to any UI.** Should be a first-class red banner on the Scans page. Today it exists only as an `error.err` line; the user sees at most the downstream *overdue* amber after missed runs pile up.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `fs.existsSync(triggerScriptPath())` is **false** — i.e. `deploy/launchd/run-worker.mjs` cannot be located. `triggerScriptPath()` walks **up the tree (12 hops)** looking for that file; if none is found it returns the canonical 5-levels-up path, which may not exist on disk. Two moments detect it: (1) at **install** time `buildInstallOpts()` does the `existsSync` check, logs `log.error('schedule', '<kind>: worker trigger script not found at <path> — the launchd job will fail until this file exists')`, and **installs the plist anyway** (so the OS job is registered but crashes `MODULE_NOT_FOUND` on every fire, writing nothing to LFB's own logs); (2) at **reconcile** time `reconcileWorkerSchedules()` re-detects a `scriptMissing`/`scriptDrift` (a baked path in an already-installed plist that no longer resolves) and rewrites it. This is the exact 2026-07-07 F1 silent-stall class (MODULE_NOT_FOUND ×550). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/schedule.service.ts` — `triggerScriptPath()` (lines 44–57), `buildInstallOpts()` `existsSync` guard + `log.error` (lines 129–148, error at ~135–137), `reconcileWorkerSchedules()` scriptDrift/scriptMissing (lines 205–221).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The background job's launcher file is missing (usually right after a code move or app upgrade). macOS still has the job registered, but every time it fires it crashes instantly and writes nothing — so syncing silently stops." *Why it matters:* this is the **deadliest** stall because it produces no error in LFB's logs; it is the precise bug that once stopped device registration invisibly, so your other computers quietly stopped seeing this one. *Reassurance to include:* the in-app **watchdog** runs the work in-process while the app is open, and boot + every watchdog tick call `reconcileWorkerSchedules()` to rewrite the plist path once the file exists — so a permanent (app-closed) install is the only case that stays broken. *Options:* none — one-click fix. *Action button:* "Repair schedule".

**(C) The fix.** The button re-runs `reconcileWorkerSchedules()`, which rewrites and reloads **every** installed plist with the freshly-resolved trigger path (equivalent to `control('sync','uninstall')` then `control('sync','install')` per worker). If `run-worker.mjs` genuinely doesn't exist on disk (a broken build/deploy), there is **no auto-fix** — manual next step: reinstall/rebuild so `code/deploy/launchd/run-worker.mjs` is present. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/schedule.service.ts` — `reconcileWorkerSchedules()` (lines 192–226, also called at boot); watchdog reconcile after an overdue tick in `watchdog.service.ts` (lines 76–79).

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: currently detectable **only** via `error.err`; the root cause is never named in the UI — the user only ever sees the *overdue* proxy. Given [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) §8 this should be a first-class red Scans banner. There is also **no user-triggered "Repair schedule" endpoint** today — reconcile runs only at boot and from the watchdog, so even the fix above needs a new endpoint exposed.

---

#### 10.9.2 The last background sync failed — `bad` (id: sync-worker-last-run-failed)

*Where shown:* Scans page **top verdict banner** (red) + the Transfer WorkerCard (which shows "last run … — failed"). (Canonical merge of `sync-worker-last-run-failed` + `auto-sync-last-run-failed`.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `data.sync.lastRunOk === false` — **strictly `=== false`**, not null. `lastRunOk` rides from config `sync_process.last_run_ok`, stamped by `stampRun('sync', ok)` at the end of every run — whether the run came from the OS launchd worker (via `/api/internal/run`) or the in-process watchdog. A never-run / null does **not** trigger this (it triggers *overdue*, §10.9.8). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — verdict lines ~50–55, `workerHealth()` line 20; backend stamp in `schedule.service.ts` `stampRun()` (lines 249–256); the watchdog failure-stamp path in `watchdog.service.ts` (lines 66–69). The actual work whose failure is being recorded is `sync.service.ts` `syncAll()`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The every-15-minute transfer job ran but hit an error on its most recent pass." Common causes to name: IPFS engine down mid-run, a repo folder moved/deleted, a git push/merge conflict on a Git-backed storage, or a disk/permission error. *Why it matters:* your files may not have moved to your other computers on that pass, and until a run succeeds you could be working against or leaving behind stale files. *Reassurance:* the OS job retries on its next fire and the watchdog retries on its next tick. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Sync now" (re-runs `syncAll()` and re-stamps `lastRunOk`); include a link to `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err`.

**(C) The fix.** There is **no single safe auto-remediation** — the failure cause is unknown from this flag alone. The button triggers an immediate manual run to re-attempt and refresh `lastRunOk`. Ideally the popup reads the last per-unit error and routes accordingly (IPFS down → Start IPFS; repo missing → re-point/forget; merge conflict → resolve). Manual next step: open `error.err`. *Fix in:* retry path `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.service.ts` — `syncAll()` (per scan, lines ~570–595); per-unit cause is written by `markUnitError()` (lines ~607–610) into `UnitStatus.last_error` — **but that string is not yet surfaced** (see 10.9.10 note).

**Notes / gaps.** The banner and card say "failed" / "see the transfer job below" but neither shows the **actual error string** — the real cause lives in `status.yaml` `last_error` and the logs and is not surfaced (improvement gap). The `bad` rung here is what promotes the whole page verdict to red; the underlying reasons are §10.9.11–10.9.13.

---

#### 10.9.3 Automatic syncing is on, but the IPFS engine is down — `bad` (id: sync-on-but-ipfs-down)

*Where shown:* Scans page **top verdict banner** (red). (Canonical merge of `sync-on-but-ipfs-down` + `ipfs-down-while-sync-on`.) Cross-category: the **IPFS-down condition and its Start-IPFS fix are owned by the IPFS category** — see §10.4 (`ipfs-down`) for the daemon lifecycle/enforceCompliance detail; this entry documents only the *sync-resilience framing* of the same signal.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `ipfsDown = data.ipfs !== "ok"`, evaluated **only in the final healthy branch** of the sync verdict — i.e. the transfer worker must be installed **and** enabled **and** not-failed **and** not-overdue; only then does IPFS-down flip that otherwise-green branch to `bad`. `data.ipfs` is `SyncPageData.ipfs = await ipfs.health()`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — `ipfsDown` line 32, healthy branch lines ~62–70; backend `syncPageData()` sets `ipfs` in `schedule.service.ts` (line 123 via `ipfs.health()`). Each unit aborts when `health!=='ok'` in `sync.service.ts` `runUnitSync` (lines ~122–126, marking the unit "IPFS node unreachable" and returning zero bytes moved).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The 15-minute launchd job is firing fine, but the local Kubo/IPFS daemon isn't answering — so every run visits your files but moves zero bytes." Name the Kubo 0.42 Reprovider-crash class (the daemon FATAL-ing on a deprecated config key). Note git text (device registry/manifest) may still flow — only the byte transport is stuck (F6 in [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) §2). *Why it matters:* new/changed large files cannot reach your other computers until IPFS is back. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Start IPFS".

**(C) The fix.** Start/restart the Kubo daemon via the IPFS module's `startDaemon()`; `enforceCompliance()` must write `Provide.Strategy` and **never re-add** the deprecated `Reprovider` key (which FATAL-crashes Kubo 0.42 — see MEMORY: IPFS Reprovider crash). *Fix in:* IPFS module (out of this category): `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/ipfs/ipfs-node.service.ts` `startDaemon()`; guided-start UI in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/ipfs/IpfsOffPage.tsx`. — no auto-fix on the Scans page itself.

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: this is a **red verdict with no in-page Fix button** — the fix is one module away but the Scans banner does not surface a "Start IPFS" action; today the user must navigate to the IPFS page. `ipfs.health()` is the shared signal across categories.

---

#### 10.9.4 A sync couldn't merge — resolve the conflict — `bad` (id: git-merge-conflict)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not wired to any banner today.** Should be a per-storage / Repos banner. Currently the merge is aborted and only `log.warn()`'d to `error.err`; storage units have no persisted status file to read a conflict from.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when a git pass produces `GitCycleResult.conflicts.length > 0` / `GitCycleResult.problem` set. In `pull()`: `git merge --no-edit` throws → `conflictedPaths()` reads `git status().conflicted` → `git merge --abort` (tree left clean, nothing clobbered) → `result.problem = 'Git merge conflict on N file(s) …'`. The committed-manifest quarantine path (`manifest.service` `isConflicted`) is the second entry point. Conflicts are rare by design — device files are self-owned and list files use `merge=union`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/git/git.service.ts` — `pull()` (lines 180–211); consumed (log-only) in `sync.service.ts` `syncStorageUnitInner` (lines ~397–406).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "Git couldn't automatically merge a shared coordination text file. LFBridge aborted the merge so nothing of yours was overwritten, kept your working tree clean, and **keeps syncing your file bytes over IPFS** meanwhile." List the conflicted paths. *Why it matters:* only the small coordination YAML is stuck until you resolve it; your actual large files are unaffected. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Re-check" (re-runs the sync, which re-attempts the merge) — LFBridge will **never** force-push or discard your work (§4 of the charter's sync policy).

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix** — git itself declined the merge, and semantic conflicts need a human. Manual next step: open the repo working copy, resolve the listed conflicted files with your own git tools, commit; LFBridge re-converges on the next pass. The button can at most re-attempt the sync. *Fix in:* manual git resolution; re-attempt via `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.service.ts` `syncStorageUnitInner()`. — no auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not yet wired. Storage units have **no persisted `status.yaml`** (`writeStatus` is a no-op, `sync.service.ts` ~line 438), so there is nowhere for the frontend to read the conflict from. Wiring requires persisting `GitCycleResult.problem`/`conflicts` per storage and rendering it. High-value: this is exactly the "nothing fails silent" AC#7 in [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) §9, F4 in §2.

---

#### 10.9.5 Re-authenticate this Git remote — `bad` (id: git-auth-failure)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not wired today.** Should be a per-storage / Repos banner. Currently only `log.warn()`'d.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** A fetch/push error whose message matches `/auth|denied|credential|403|401|could not read Username|terminal prompts disabled/i` — i.e. a `url` remote with no cached OS credential or an expired token. `GIT_TERMINAL_PROMPT=0` forces a clean failure instead of a hang. `classifyRemoteError()` sets `GitCycleResult.problem = 'Git authentication failed for this remote — re-authenticate it (LFB keeps syncing over IPFS meanwhile).'`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/git/git.service.ts` — `classifyRemoteError()` (lines 287–294), invoked from `pull()` (line 187) and `commitAndPush()` (line 281); consumed (log-only) in `sync.service.ts` (lines ~404–406 / ~454–456).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The git backbone remote (an http(s)/ssh URL) has no valid cached credential, so the small coordination text — device registry and manifests — can't fetch or push. **Your IPFS byte sync keeps running**, so files still move; only the coordination YAML is stuck." *Why it matters:* your other computers may lag on learning about this machine's registry/manifest changes until the remote is re-authenticated. Note LFBridge never prompts inline (non-interactive by design) and never hangs. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Re-test connection" (re-runs the sync after you fix credentials).

**(C) The fix.** **No in-app auto-fix** — credentials live in the OS git credential helper / keychain, outside LFBridge. Manual next step: run a `git fetch`/`git push` against the remote once from a terminal to populate the OS keychain, or switch the remote to an SSH URL with a loaded key; then re-test. *Fix in:* OS git credential helper (external); re-test via `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.service.ts` `syncStorageUnitInner()`. — no auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not wired; needs the same per-storage persistence as 10.9.4 to surface. Applies **only to `url` remotes** (`classifyRemote`) — a `local` path checkout can never hit this, so guard against false alarms on local backbones. F5 in [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) §2.

---

#### 10.9.6 Health check failed — `bad` (id: top-level-health-check-failed)

*Where shown:* Any page that polls `GET /api/health` and gets a **500**. Not rendered as a dedicated banner today — consumers just see a failed request; the SyncPage poll failure is mirrored to `error.err` via `clientLog.warn` but shows no banner (silent background refetch).

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `ipfs.health()` **rejects (throws)** inside the health router `'/'` handler — distinct from IPFS merely returning a non-`ok` status (§10.9.3). The handler try/catches, `log.error`s `'health check failed: …'`, and returns `500 { ok:false, error:'health check failed' }`. Also `GET /api/health/auth-config` 500s on `authConfig()` throw. And a `SyncPage` `useQuery` error → `clientLog.warn('SyncPage.syncPage.poll')`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/health/health.router.ts` (lines 9–28); frontend poll-error mirror in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` `useEffect` (lines ~27–31).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The backend couldn't even complete a health check — the health endpoint itself errored (e.g. `ipfs.health` threw), which usually means the backend process is degraded, not just that the IPFS daemon is down." *Why it matters:* the app can't currently tell you whether anything is OK; a repeated failure of `/api/sync` (`syncPageData`) leaves the whole Scans verdict stuck on "Loading…" (neutral) forever — a silent degradation. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Retry" (may recover a transient throw); point to `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err`.

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix from the client** — a 500 is a server-side failure. Manual next step: check `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err` and the backend process, then restart the app (`just stop && just run`). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/health/health.router.ts` — no fix action; diagnostic only. — no auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: a repeated poll failure of `syncPageData` degrades the Scans verdict to a permanent neutral "Loading…" with no user-visible signal — consider a "can't reach the backend" banner when the query errors repeatedly rather than only `clientLog.warn`.

---

#### 10.9.7 Automatic syncing isn't installed yet — `warn` (id: sync-worker-not-installed)

*Where shown:* Scans page **top verdict banner** (amber) + the Transfer WorkerCard. (Canonical merge of `sync-worker-not-installed` + `auto-sync-not-installed`.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `data.sync.installed === false`. `WorkerState.installed = installer().isInstalled(label) || block.installed` — i.e. the launchd plist `com.largefilebridge.sync` is absent. `workerHealth()` returns **neutral** for an uninstalled card, but the **page verdict promotes the sync worker's not-installed state to `warn`**. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — verdict lines ~38–43, `workerHealth()` lines 17–23; backend `schedule.service.ts` `workerState()` (lines 94–112, `installed` at line 97).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "LFBridge syncs via a macOS launchd background job (the cron equivalent) that fires every 15 minutes even when the app is closed. Without it installed, files only move while you have the app open and manually sync." Explain install is safe, local-only, separate from on/off, and reversible. *Why it matters:* close the app and syncing stops entirely — files stay only on this machine. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Install".

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/sync/sync/install` → `control('sync','install')`, which writes the launchd plist via `launchdInstaller.install(buildInstallOpts('sync'))` and sets `sync_process.installed=true` (typically followed by enable). *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` — `POST /:worker/:action` (lines 39–54); `schedule.service.ts` `control()` (lines 150–184) + `buildInstallOpts()` (lines 129–148). Frontend `api.controlWorker('sync','install')` in the WorkerCard.

**Notes / gaps.** The sync worker (unlike `device`) is **not auto-provisioned** — it requires an explicit user Install, so this is a correct `warn` offer, not an alarm. Improvement gap: the banner has no inline Fix button today — the Install action lives only in the card below; promote an "Install" action into the banner itself.

---

#### 10.9.8 Automatic syncing is installed but turned off — `warn` (id: sync-worker-installed-off)

*Where shown:* Scans page **top verdict banner** (amber) + the Transfer WorkerCard. (Canonical merge of `sync-worker-installed-off` + `auto-sync-installed-but-off`.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `data.sync.installed === true && data.sync.enabled === false`. `enabled` is reconciled against the **real OS state**: `installed ? await installer().isEnabled(label) : block.enabled`, OR'd with `block.enabled` — so the plist exists but is booted-out/disabled. This is a **deliberate user Off state**, distinct from overdue or failed. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — verdict lines ~44–49; `workerHealth()` returns `warn` for installed && !enabled (line 19); backend `schedule.service.ts` `workerState()` (lines 94–112, `enabled` reconcile lines 98–99).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The launchd job exists but is loaded-off, so no automatic 15-minute syncs run; changes accumulate unsynced until you turn it back on (or run a manual Sync now)." *Why it matters:* files only sync while the app is open until you re-enable. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Turn on".

**(C) The fix.** `POST /api/sync/sync/enable` → `control('sync','enable')` → `launchdInstaller.enable(label)` (`launchctl bootstrap`) and sets `sync_process.enabled=true`. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/schedule.service.ts` — `control()` `'enable'` branch (lines 150–184, enable at ~161–181); `sync.router.ts` `POST /:worker/:action` (lines 39–54).

**Notes / gaps.** A correct `warn` — a user opt-out is legitimately respected but gently nudged; never an alarm.

---

#### 10.9.9 Automatic syncing is overdue — `warn` (id: sync-worker-overdue)

*Where shown:* Scans page **top verdict banner** (amber) + the Transfer WorkerCard ("last run … — overdue"). (Canonical merge of `sync-worker-overdue` + `auto-sync-overdue`.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `data.sync.installed && data.sync.enabled && overdue === true`. `overdue` is **derived per read** by `isWorkerOverdue(intervalSeconds, last_run_at)`: **true** when `last_run_at` is null/NaN (never ran) **OR** `(now − last_run_at) > intervalSeconds*2 + 120s` slack. For `sync`, interval = `sync_process.interval_minutes*60` (15 min → overdue after ~30 min + 2 min). Only computed when installed && enabled. This is the **F1 silent-stall proxy** ([sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) §7): the launchd trigger is presumed dead (e.g. a moved/stale `run-worker.mjs`, a booted-out job). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/schedule.service.ts` — `isWorkerOverdue()` (lines 86–92) and `workerState()` `overdue` (line 110); frontend `SyncPage.tsx` verdict lines ~56–61, `workerHealth()` line 21.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The job is installed and on but hasn't run when it should have — a known silent-crash class where the macOS launchd trigger has quietly died (a stale `run-worker.mjs` path after a code move)." *Why it matters:* files aren't moving on their own right now. *Reassurance (important):* the in-process **watchdog** (§3) is **already** running the pass in-app *and* rewriting+reloading the plist every 5 min via `reconcileWorkerSchedules()`, so this is normally transient and self-healing; it persists mainly only if the app itself was down. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Reinstall transfer job".

**(C) The fix.** Auto-repair already runs (`watchdog.tick()` → `runWorkerInProcess()` + `reconcileWorkerSchedules()`). The manual escalation the button offers is `control('sync','uninstall')` then `control('sync','install')` — force-rewrite+reload the launchd plist with the correct interval and freshly-resolved trigger path. *Fix in:* auto-repair `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/watchdog.service.ts` — `tick()` / `runWorkerInProcess()` (lines 45–84); `schedule.service.ts` `reconcileWorkerSchedules()` (lines 192–226); manual reinstall via `control()` (lines 150–184).

**Notes / gaps.** The banner correctly stays **amber** (self-healing), not red — per MEMORY: watchdog + always-push-when-ahead keep the flow alive. The same overdue logic applies to the `device` (10 min) and `scan` (4h) cards. GAP: there is **no dedicated user-triggered "Repair schedule" endpoint** exposed to the banner — reconcile only runs at boot and from the watchdog, so the "Reinstall" button today must go the uninstall+install route.

---

#### 10.9.10 Device registration is off / overdue / failed — `warn` (bad sub-state) (id: device-worker-health)

*Where shown:* Scans page — the **Device-registration WorkerCard** (DiagnosticCard), **not** the top verdict. (Canonical merge of `device-worker-health` + `device-worker-off-overdue-or-failed`.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** The same `workerHealth()` ladder applied to `data.device`: `!installed` → **neutral**; `installed && !enabled` → **warn**; `lastRunOk === false` → **bad**; `overdue` → **warn** (device interval = `device_process.interval_minutes*60` = 10 min → overdue after ~22 min, i.e. 2×10 min + 120s). The device worker is **auto-provisioned ON at first boot** (`ensureDeviceWorkerDefaultOn`), so a "not installed" state should be rare and an "off" state means the user deliberately disabled it. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — `workerHealth()` (lines 17–23) + the WorkerCard (lines ~184–259); backend `schedule.service.ts` `workerState()` (lines 94–112) and `ensureDeviceWorkerDefaultOn()` (lines 236–247). The work it runs: `syncDeviceRegistrations()` in `sync.service.ts` (lines ~526–535).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "This is the flow's **main carrier** ([devices.mdx](./devices.mdx) §12). Every 10 minutes it does `git pull + merge`, writes this computer's `devices/<self>.yaml`, then `commit + push` — even when nothing changed — so your other computers learn about this machine *and* this machine pulls down their registry edits." *Why it matters:* if it's off/overdue/failed, your device roster stops updating across machines and your other computers stop seeing this one — the exact shape of the 2026-07-07 incident. *Options:* none. *Action button:* state-dependent — "Install" (not installed) / "Turn on" (off) / overdue self-heals via watchdog or "Reinstall".

**(C) The fix.** `control('device', <action>)` via `POST /api/sync/device/{action}` (the `worker` enum includes `device`): not installed → install; off → enable; overdue → watchdog auto-repairs (`reconcileWorkerSchedules`) or manual reinstall. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` — `POST /:worker/:action` (lines 39–54); `schedule.service.ts` `control()` (lines 150–184).

**Notes / gaps.** Wired via the **card only**, never the top verdict (which tracks the `sync` worker). Per [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx) §8 a device worker off/overdue is arguably **more serious** than sync overdue (it's why remote devices look stale) — consider promoting device health into the page verdict. Auto-provision *failure* is the separate §10.9.11.

---

#### 10.9.11 Device registration couldn't auto-install at startup — `warn` (id: device-worker-autoprovision-failed)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not distinctly surfaced.** Should be a Scans-page Device-card banner. Manifests only indirectly as the Device card reading "Not installed"; the failure itself is only `log.warn`'d.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `ensureDeviceWorkerDefaultOn()` runs at boot (from `main.ts` bootstrap, before `reconcileWorkerSchedules()`): if `!device_process.auto_provisioned` it `control('device','install')` then `control('device','enable')`. If the `launchctl`/OS step **throws**, the catch leaves `auto_provisioned` **UNSET** (so the next boot retries) and the worker stays not-installed, logging `'device worker: default-on provisioning failed (retries next boot)'`. Detect via `data.device.installed === false` after boot **on macOS**. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/schedule.service.ts` — `ensureDeviceWorkerDefaultOn()` (lines 236–247, catch at ~243–246).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "Device write-back is supposed to be ON by default with no action from you, but the macOS `launchctl` step failed at startup — so this computer isn't yet registering itself to your repos every 10 minutes." *Why it matters:* your other computers won't see this machine until it's installed. *Reassurance:* it auto-retries on the next app restart. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Install".

**(C) The fix.** The button re-runs the same two calls the auto-provisioner makes: `control('device','install')` then `control('device','enable')`. Manual next step if it keeps failing: check `launchctl` permissions. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/schedule/schedule.service.ts` — `control()` (lines 150–184).

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not distinctly surfaced — folds into the generic "Not installed" card. **False-alarm guard:** on non-darwin the `noopInstaller` flips the flags but `isInstalled() === false`, so the Device card reads "Not installed" permanently off-Mac — **only warn on darwin** to avoid a perpetual false alarm.

---

#### 10.9.12 Discovery (scan) is off / overdue / failed — `warn` (bad sub-state) (id: scan-worker-health)

*Where shown:* Scans page — the **Discovery WorkerCard**, not the top verdict. (Canonical merge of `scan-worker-health` + `discovery-scan-worker-off-overdue-or-failed` + the `bad`-severity `scan-worker-last-run-failed`, which is the failed rung of this same ladder.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `workerHealth()` on `data.scan`: `!installed` → **neutral**; `installed && !enabled` → **warn**; `lastRunOk === false` → **bad**; `overdue` → **warn**. Scan interval = `scan_process.interval_hours*3600` (config-healed; note the raw scan data listed both a 4h default and a healed 2h in `config.service` — overdue fires after 2× interval + slack either way). Scan is **NOT auto-provisioned** — it stays neutral until the user Installs it. The `bad` (last-run-failed) rung is stamped by `stampRun('scan', ok)` which `scan-job.ts` calls at the **end of every run** (manual or scheduled) with the real success/failure. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — `workerHealth()` (lines 17–23), the scan WorkerCard + last-run string (lines ~100–105 / ~210–215); backend `schedule.service.ts` `intervalFor('scan')` (lines 73–78) + `workerState()` (lines 94–112); the outcome stamp in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/scanner/scan-job.ts` `stampRun` call (lines 100–106).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "Discovery walks your repos every few hours to find new/changed large files — **metadata only, no bytes move**. If it's off or overdue, newly added big files may not be noticed until you open the app (the live watcher catches adds/deletes then) or run a manual scan. A *failed* last run means your tracking may be stale, but no file data is at risk." Overdue = launchd trigger likely dead; the watchdog re-runs `startScan('scheduled')` and repairs the plist. *Why it matters:* stale tracking → the rest of the UI's counts and offers lag reality until the next successful scan. *Options:* none. *Action button:* state-dependent — "Install" / "Turn on" / (failed) "Run Discovery now" / overdue self-heals.

**(C) The fix.** `control('scan', <action>)` via `POST /api/sync/scan/{action}`; the **failed** case clears with a fresh successful stamp by running `startScan('manual')`; overdue auto-heals via the watchdog's in-process `startScan('scheduled')`. If it keeps failing, reinstall/repair from the same card. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/scanner/scan-job.ts` `startScan()` (lines ~50–68); watchdog `runWorkerInProcess()` in `watchdog.service.ts` (lines ~30–42); `control()` in `schedule.service.ts` (lines 150–184).

**Notes / gaps.** Wired via the card only; lower stakes than sync/device (metadata only). GAP flagged in the scanner partition: consider surfacing a `bad`/overdue scan into the SyncPage **top verdict** so the banner isn't green while the Discovery card is red.

---

#### 10.9.13 Git sync hit a remote/commit error (LFB keeps syncing over IPFS) — `warn` (id: git-remote-or-commit-error)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not wired today.** Should be a per-storage banner. Only `log.warn`'d.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `GitCycleResult.problem` set by one of three non-auth git failures: (a) `classifyRemoteError()`'s **fallback branch** for a non-auth remote error (network, "remote hung up", unknown host) → `'Git remote error — LFB keeps syncing over IPFS.'`; (b) a failed `git commit` → `commitAndPush()` catch → `'Git commit failed: …'`; (c) a **clone failure** in `resolveWorkingCopy()` returns null so `gitBackbone === null` and **no git cycle runs at all** (`ran:false`) — the quietest case. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/git/git.service.ts` — `classifyRemoteError()` fallback (line 293), `commitAndPush()` commit-catch (lines 253–256), `resolveWorkingCopy()` clone-catch (lines 89–92).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The git text backbone hit a transient or config error (network, a bad remote, a clone that couldn't complete), but your **IPFS byte flow is unaffected** — files still sync; only the coordination text is delayed and retries next pass." Distinguish from auth (§10.9.5, which needs your action) — this is usually transient. *Why it matters:* device/manifest coordination lags briefly; a *persistent* clone failure means the backbone is configured but unreachable. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Re-sync now".

**(C) The fix.** Usually **no action** — it retries automatically next pass. The button can force an immediate re-sync (`syncAll` / per-storage). For a persistent clone failure, manual next step: verify the remote URL and network in Repos/Settings. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.service.ts` — `syncStorageUnitInner()`. — largely self-healing; no dedicated auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: not wired; the **clone-failure branch is the quietest** case — the whole git cycle is skipped with only an info/warn log and **no `problem` string reaches the caller** (`ran:false`). Consider surfacing "git backbone configured but not reachable" so a permanently-broken remote doesn't hide behind a working IPFS flow forever.

---

#### 10.9.14 Live watch is off, or on but watching no folders — `warn` (id: live-watcher-off-or-idle)

*Where shown:* Scans page — the **Live-watch WatcherCard**, not the top verdict. (Single canonical warning; appeared in both partitions.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `watcherHealth(data.watcher)`: `enabled === false` → **warn** ("off — changes picked up by the 4-hour Discovery pass instead"); `enabled && watching === false` → **warn** ("on, but no folders are being watched yet — set your scan roots in Settings", i.e. no scan roots bound or all roots unwatchable); `enabled && watching` → **ok** ("watching N folders"). The watcher is **NOT a launchd job** — it runs only while the web app is open and reacts instantly to a big/video/image/audio file being **added or deleted** (never edits, moves no bytes). `watcherState()` supplies `enabled`/`watching`/`roots`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/sync/SyncPage.tsx` — `watcherHealth()` (lines 118–122) + the WatcherCard (lines ~124–182); backend `watcherState()` in `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/watcher/watcher.service.ts` (imported into `schedule.service.ts` line 14, returned by `syncPageData()` line 121); control via `POST /api/sync/watcher/:action` in `sync.router.ts` (lines 26–36).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "The live watcher reacts instantly (while the app is open) to a big file being added or deleted — updating tracking and the File System tree without waiting for the multi-hour Discovery scan. **Off** is fine (Discovery still covers it every few hours); **on-but-idle** means you have no scan roots configured (or they're unwatchable), so it's bound to nothing and can't do its job." *Why it matters:* off → new files wait for the next scheduled scan; idle → the watcher is running but useless until roots exist. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Turn on" (resolves the **off** case only).

**(C) The fix.** **Off** → `POST /api/sync/watcher/enable` → `setWatcherEnabled(true)`. **On-but-idle** → **no watcher endpoint fixes an empty root set**; the real fix is setting scan roots in Settings, so the button should deep-link to Settings › scan roots rather than toggle. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` — `POST /watcher/:action` (lines 26–36) → `setWatcherEnabled()`; the idle case routes to Settings (scan-roots config, out of this category) — no direct watcher auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** Two distinct amber conditions share one card; the **idle** case's fix lives on a different page (scan roots) — enabling the watcher won't help until roots exist, so don't offer "Turn on" as the fix for idle.

---

#### 10.9.15 This computer has never synced — `warn` (id: never-synced-machine)

*Where shown:* **GAP — no global verdict.** Partially surfaced only as per-repo "never" last-sync text in the Repos/One-Repo tables; there is no top-level "you have never synced this computer" banner.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `lastSyncAt() === null` — i.e. there is **no** `sync_process.last_run_at` **and no** repo `status.yaml` has a `last_sync_at`. `isStale(null)` is treated as **infinitely stale** (`=== true`), which also triggers the same invisible auto-sync as §10.9.16. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sessions/sessions.service.ts` — `lastSyncAt()` (lines 30–46, returns null) + `isStale()` (line 96). Per-repo "never" rendering via `relativeTime(null)` in `ReposPage`/`OneRepoPage`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "This is a brand-new / never-synced computer — nothing has been pulled yet, so it doesn't have your other computers' files." *Why it matters:* you're starting from empty; until a first pass runs, this machine is not part of your file mesh. *Options:* none (onboarding guidance). *Action button:* "Run first sync".

**(C) The fix.** Run the first sync now (`syncAll()`) **and** ensure the `sync`/`device` workers are installed+enabled (`control` install/enable). Manual prerequisite the popup must state: a configured git backbone remote and IPFS up. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.service.ts` — `syncAll()`; worker setup via `schedule.service.ts` `control()` (lines 150–184).

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: overlaps §10.9.16 (stale-return) but is **distinct** — "never" is a first-run onboarding state, not drift. Consider a dedicated first-run verdict on Home/Repos rather than letting it hide behind per-repo "never" cells and an invisible auto-sync.

---

#### 10.9.16 More than 48h since last sync — files may be stale (and the catch-up sync is invisible) — `warn` (id: stale-return-autosync-invisible)

*Where shown:* **GAP — the signal is fetched then discarded.** Should be a global/Home banner or toast. The backend computes and returns it; the frontend ping **throws the result away**.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Backend: on a **new web session** (`newSession`), if `isStale(lastSyncAt(), now)` where `isStale = !last (never synced) || now − last > 48h`, `recordActivity()` fires a **non-blocking** `syncAll()` and returns `{ newSession, autoSyncTriggered, lastSyncAt }`. `lastSyncAt()` = the newest of `sync_process.last_run_at` and every repo `status.yaml` `last_sync_at`. Guarded by `autoSyncInFlight` so only one catch-up runs. The frontend `useSessionPing` **only `.catch()`es** the ping — it never reads `autoSyncTriggered`/`lastSyncAt`, so the user is never told. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sessions/sessions.service.ts` — `recordActivity()` (lines 52–87), `isStale()` (lines 95–98), `lastSyncAt()` (lines 30–46), `triggerAutoSync()` (lines 132–147); frontend discard at `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/lib/useSessionPing.ts` (line 22).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* "This computer hasn't synced in over 48 hours ([sessions.mdx](./sessions.mdx) §3), so files from your other computers may be missing or old. LFBridge automatically kicked off a background catch-up sync the moment you came back, so you're not working against stale files." Show the "last synced" age. *Why it matters:* you may otherwise edit or rely on outdated versions. *Options:* none — informational. *Action button:* "View progress" (or re-trigger "Sync now") — no destructive action.

**(C) The fix.** The auto-sync **already fires** (`triggerAutoSync` → `syncAll`); the button is informational — it can re-trigger a manual sync or link to the Progress dock. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sessions/sessions.service.ts` — `triggerAutoSync()` (lines 132–147). — no new fix needed; the missing piece is *surfacing*, not remediation.

**Notes / gaps.** GAP: the signal exists end-to-end but is **dropped at the client**. Low-effort win: surface `autoSyncTriggered`/`lastSyncAt` from `useSessionPing` as a toast or amber Home banner ("Catching up — you'd been away 3 days"). This is a pure transparency gap, tied to [sync_resilience.mdx](./sync_resilience.mdx)'s "nothing fails silent" principle applied to a *success* the user can't see.

## 10.10 Settings, security, credentials & tools

This category owns every warnable condition on the **Settings**, **Tools**, and **Security/Access** surfaces plus the cross-cutting auth plumbing behind them. It is where the charter's auth posture is enforced — **OpenAuth federated, Google email sign-in, allow-list only, no anonymous / no default account** (LFBridge charter "Authentication") — and where the app tells a non-expert that a required tool, credential, or setting is missing. Because sign-in and system tools are prerequisites for everything else, most of the Broken warnings here are **hard gates** (pre-auth full-screen setup, install cards) rather than dismissible banners, and several are **manual-remediation** by design: the app will not mint OAuth secrets, install Homebrew, or install system CLIs on its own (charter consent posture). Ranked Broken → Improvable → neutral.

#### 10.10.1 First-run setup required — decide who may sign in — `bad` (id: security-not-configured-firstrun)

*Where shown:* a **full-screen blocking gate** (`SecuritySetupPage`), rendered by the `<Root>` gate **before any sign-in** whenever the security config is unconfigured. Not a dismissible banner — the app cannot be used until it is completed.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `getPublicSecurityConfig().configured === false`, i.e. `config.access.configured !== true` in the persisted app config. The public probe `GET /api/security/config` returns `{configured:false}` and the frontend gate swaps in the setup page. `securityConfigured()` is the single source of this boolean and is also a precondition for dev-auth (§10.10.7) — a machine with no allow-list can never fabricate a dev admin. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/security/security.service.ts` — `securityConfigured()` (L99–101) and `getPublicSecurityConfig()` (L124–126); router `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/security/security.router.ts` — `GET /config` (L13–15); frontend page `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/security/SecuritySetupPage.tsx`.

**(B) The popup.** This warning *is* a page rather than an arrow-popup, but the educate copy is the same. *What this is:* a one-time, **loopback-only** setup that defines the allow-list before sign-in is possible; you may admit a whole company Google Workspace **domain**, individual **Google accounts**, or both. *Why it matters:* until it is saved, **nobody can sign in** (access is default-deny); and once saved it is locked in — changeable later only from admin Settings → Access. *Options:* the two-section `AllowListFields` (companies + individuals) with the empty-list guard of §10.10.8 live. *Action button:* "Save & enable sign-in" (blue). Not dismissible — it is a gate.

**(C) The fix.** The page **is** the fix: `POST /api/security/setup` with `{allowCompanies, domains, allowIndividuals, emails}`. The endpoint is **loopback-guarded** (403 `not_loopback` off-loopback) and **one-time** (409 `already_configured` once set). On success it calls `completeSetup()`, persists `config.access.configured = true`, and **rebuilds the auth frontend** so the very next Google sign-in is accepted **with no backend restart**. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/security/security.router.ts` — `POST /setup` (L34–54) → `completeSetup()` in `security.service.ts` (L168–184).

**Notes / gaps.** Distinct from any running-app banner — it is the **pre-auth** gate. Refusal states to handle in the UI: 409 `already_configured` and 403 `not_loopback` (security.router.ts L19–24). The empty-list guard (§10.10.8) applies here too, so Save is disabled until at least one valid domain/email exists.

#### 10.10.2 Google sign-in isn't configured on this computer — `bad` (id: google-oauth-not-configured)

*Where shown:* Settings page → **Authentication** `Section` (state `bad`, right label "Not configured"); the same condition renders inline as `CredentialsSetupCard` and pops as `CredentialsMissingDialog` on the sign-in gate.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Frontend computes `authConfigured = !!auth?.oauthConfigured` and branches to the not-configured card when false. Backend truth: `hasGoogleCreds()` returns false when there is **no** `GOOGLE_CLIENT_ID`/`GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET` env pair **AND no valid credentials JSON file** on disk. Two sub-states share this warning: **(a)** file entirely missing, and **(b)** file present but invalid — `credentialsFileInfo().exists === true && configured === false`, which `CredentialsSetupCard` flags with "(A file exists at this path but is missing valid credentials.)". *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` — `SettingsPage` `authConfigured` (L53), Authentication `Section` render (L108–139); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/auth.router.ts` — `authConfig()` (`oauthConfigured = hasGoogleCreds()`, L34–53) and `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/config/credentials-file.ts` — `hasGoogleCreds()` / `credentialsFileInfo()` (L61–79).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* Google sign-in reads an OAuth **client id + secret** from a JSON file (or the `GOOGLE_CLIENT_ID`/`GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET` env vars) **only at backend boot**; until they are present nobody can sign in (localhost dev-auth is the only bypass — §10.10.7). *Why it matters:* the file holds **secrets** and must stay out of any git repo; the redirect URI must be registered **verbatim** on the Google Cloud OAuth client using the API port `8787`; with no creds the whole app is inaccessible to real users. *Options:* none — remediation is manual file/env creation. *Action button:* no blue auto-fix button; instead a "Copy path & schema" affordance plus an optional "Re-check". 

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix** — the app cannot mint Google OAuth secrets. The action deep-links/scrolls to `CredentialsSetupCard`, copies the target path + JSON schema to the clipboard, and offers **Re-check** which re-queries `GET /api/health/auth-config` (→ `authConfig(includeSensitive)`) after the user creates the file. Manual next step: create the credentials JSON (or set env vars) then **restart the backend**. *Fix in:* no backend mutation endpoint exists — guidance component `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/CredentialsSetupCard.tsx`; re-check source `GET /api/health/auth-config` → `auth.router.ts` `authConfig()`.

**Notes / gaps.** The sensitive path/schema/redirect URI and the dev-auth state are returned **only to a loopback caller** — a remote caller gets `oauthConfigured` alone, with path/filename/directory redacted and `devAuth` never disclosed (auth.router.ts L34–45), so an exposed instance can't confirm the bypass is active. On localhost with `LFB_DEV_AUTH` the app remains usable despite this Broken state — see §10.10.7.

#### 10.10.3 Your Google account isn't on the allow-list — `bad` (id: signed-in-not-allowlisted)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not surfaced as a friendly banner today.** A signed-in but non-allow-listed user simply gets 401 on every data route and is bounced back to the sign-in screen with no explanation.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `identify()` verifies the Google token, then sets `user.allowListed = allowListed(email)`. `allowListed()` returns **false** when the email's **domain** is not in an enabled **company** allow-list **AND** the exact email is not in an enabled **individual** allow-list (default-deny). Every data route wrapped by `requireAllowListed` then returns `401 {code:'unauthenticated'}`, and the backend logs `Rejected non-allow-listed sign-in: <email>` at warn. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/identify.ts` — `identify()` sets `allowListed` and warn-logs (L57–69), `requireAllowListed` 401 gate (L78–85); `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/security/security.service.ts` — `allowListed()` (L86–97).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* sign-in with Google **succeeded**, but this account isn't permitted on this install — access is restricted to allow-listed company domains or individual accounts. *Why it matters:* you cannot reach any of your files or settings; this is the charter's allow-list-only posture working as designed. *Options:* none. *Action button:* if the current user **is** an admin, "Add me to Access" deep-links to Settings → Access prefilled with their email; otherwise the button is replaced by manual guidance. Tell the user **which identity was seen** so they know what to ask an admin to add.

**(C) The fix.** **No self-serve auto-fix** — a non-admin cannot widen the allow-list. Admin path: deep-link to `AllowListPage` and add the email via `PATCH /api/settings/security`. Non-admin path: manual next step is "ask an admin to add you." *Fix in:* admin editor `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/AllowListPage.tsx` → `PATCH /api/settings/security` (`settings.router.ts` L115, `requireAdmin`). No auto-fix for a non-admin — routes to "ask an admin."

**Notes / gaps.** **gap: not wired.** The friendly "you're not allow-listed (seen as X)" verdict should replace the silent 401→sign-in loop, which is indistinguishable from a plain expired session (§10.10.14) to the user. Charter tie: enforces allow-list-only access.

#### 10.10.4 Sign-in verification is misconfigured (auth secret unreadable) — `bad` (id: embedded-auth-verification-broken)

*Where shown:* **GAP — no user-facing banner.** Surfaces only as a boot/rebuild failure logged to `error.err`; the app fails to construct auth and sign-in silently breaks.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when `loadOrCreateSecret(authSecretPath())` **throws** (on-disk I/O failure — permissions, disk full, unwritable state dir) inside `ensureEmbeddedVerification()`, or when `createFederatedFrontend()` throws inside `constructAuthFrontend()`. Both `log.error('auth', …)` and rethrow, failing boot or a live `rebuildAuthFrontend()`. This app forces the **embedded HS256 in-process** verification path (`embedded: true`) — if the secret is unreadable the fallback JWKS path throws the misleading `"issuer must be an absolute URL"` error on every token verify. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/auth-frontend.ts` — `ensureEmbeddedVerification()` catch/log/throw (L30–43), `constructAuthFrontend()` catch (L151–156), `rebuildAuthFrontend()` (L163–166).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the app signs sessions with an **on-disk secret** in the state dir; if that secret can't be read or created, token verification falls back to a broken path and **all sign-in fails** with a misleading URL error. *Why it matters:* nobody can sign in; the failure is invisible in the UI and only visible in logs. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Re-run auth setup" (retries `rebuildAuthFrontend()` after the user fixes permissions).

**(C) The fix.** **No safe auto-fix beyond retry.** Manual next step: check that the **state dir is writable** (`~/T/_large_files_bridge` or `LFB_STATE_DIR`), ensure the auth secret file is readable/creatable, then restart the backend. The button can trigger a re-run of `rebuildAuthFrontend()` once permissions are fixed. *Fix in:* state dir resolver `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/config/state-dir.ts` — `resolveStateDir()`; secret path `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/shared/store/scopes.ts` — `authSecretPath()`. No auto-fix — routes to fixing state-dir permissions then restart.

**Notes / gaps.** **gap: not surfaced to the user** — a real failure mode that silently breaks all sign-in. Worth a dedicated health probe + red banner. Charter tie: logs land in the state-root fault trail `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err`, never `/tmp`.

#### 10.10.5 Required tool `ipfs` is not installed — can't scan or sync — `bad` (id: required-tool-ipfs-missing) — cross-ref §10.1

*Where shown:* Tools page → **Tools** section, the `ipfs` row (state `bad`, "✗ missing"), plus an "Install all required" bar when any required tool is missing. (The distinct verdict "IPFS daemon is **down/unreachable**" — installed but not running — is owned by **§10.1**; this warning is specifically the binary being **absent**.)

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `row.installed === false` for the **required** `ipfs` row → `state='bad'`. `buildRows()` sets `installed = node.installed` from `GET /api/ipfs/node`; `missingRequired = rows.filter(r => r.required && !r.installed)`; `canInstall = !!node.installMethod` (only `brew`/`winget`). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` — `buildRows()` (ipfs row L227–236 within L219–268), `missingRequired` (L73–74), install bar (L94–108), `ToolRowView` `bad` state (L279).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* `ipfs` (Kubo) is **mandatory** — without it there is no pinning, `add`/`get`, or pinset, so **nothing syncs and scans can't fingerprint over IPFS**. *Why it matters:* every core LFBridge function is offline until it's installed. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Install all required" (blue) when a package manager is present; otherwise "Copy command" showing the exact install line. Educate that LFB won't install system tools without an explicit click (charter consent posture).

**(C) The fix.** Auto-fix where possible: `POST /api/ipfs/install` (`startInstall`) runs the **single-flight, re-attachable** server job for the platform install command (`brew`/`winget`); the UI polls `GET /api/ipfs/install` for status and live log, then re-probes `GET /api/ipfs/node` + `GET /api/compress/tools`. **Disabled unless `node.packageManagerPresent`** (see §10.10.10). On Linux/other with no `installMethod`, there is no auto-install — show "Copy command" and the manual line. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` — `startInstall` (L64–68) → `api.ipfsInstall()` (`POST /api/ipfs/install`), status poll (L44–62).

**Notes / gaps.** Requires a package manager present (§10.10.10 cascades — button disabled without it). A failed install job is its own transient error state surfaced via toast (ToolsPage.tsx L60). For the "installed but daemon not running / not reachable" case and the compliance/gateway-off posture, **see §10.1**.

#### 10.10.6 Couldn't load settings — `bad` (id: settings-load-failed)

*Where shown:* **GAP on the main Settings page** — it shows a bare "Loading…" forever when `GET /api/settings` fails, so an error is indistinguishable from a slow load. `AiCredentialsPage` does render a proper red error box on query failure.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `SettingsPage`: `useQuery(['settings'])` rejects (backend returns a 500 envelope when `toGlobalSettings()` throws — e.g. the `ipfs.health()` / `isCompliant()` probe throwing or hanging) → `data` stays `undefined` and the code path `if (!data) return <div>Loading…</div>` renders forever with no error branch. `AiCredentialsPage`: `useQuery` error truthy → red box. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` (query L21, loading-only branch L49 — **no error branch**); working pattern in `AiCredentialsPage.tsx` (error branch L40, L56–61); backend 500 envelope `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/settings/settings.router.ts` — `GET /` catch (L46–50), `PATCH /` catch (L94–98).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* the settings data couldn't be fetched from the backend — most often the **IPFS probe failing/hanging** inside `toGlobalSettings()`, or the backend being down/restarting. *Why it matters:* you can't see or change any settings; **your saved config is unaffected** (nothing was lost — it just couldn't be read). *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Retry" (react-query refetch); if it persists, point to backend logs.

**(C) The fix.** **No mutation** — the fix is to retry the query and, if it persists, route the user to the backend fault trail. Manual next step: ensure the backend is running and the IPFS probe isn't hanging. *Fix in:* **GAP** — `SettingsPage.tsx` has no error UI; the pattern to copy is `AiCredentialsPage.tsx` (L56–61). No auto-fix — routes to backend logs `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err`.

**Notes / gaps.** **gap: `SettingsPage` lacks an error state** — a 500 is indistinguishable from loading. Note that **save** failures already toast correctly (`SettingsPage` `save.onError` L43–46); only the initial load lacks an error branch. The `AiCredentialsPage` copy also reassures the user they can still create the file at `~/.config/GoogleCloud/apikey.yaml`.

#### 10.10.7 Sign-in is bypassed (local dev mode) — anyone on this machine is admin — `warn` (id: dev-auth-bypass-active)

*Where shown:* **GAP — not a banner today.** Only a one-line hint inside `CredentialsSetupCard` ("Local dev mode is active, so the app is usable without sign-in for now."). Should be a top-of-page warning on Settings/Home.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `devAuth === true`, defined as `!hasGoogleCreds() && process.env.LFB_DEV_AUTH === 'true'`. The `identify` middleware then **fabricates an allow-listed admin principal** only when **ALL** of: `server.mode === 'local'` **AND** the request `isLoopback()` **AND** `LFB_DEV_AUTH === 'true'` **AND** `securityConfigured()` **AND** `!hasGoogleCreds()`. The fabricated user takes email `access.allowed_emails[0] || 'dev@localhost'`, `roles:['admin']`, `allowListed:true`, `sessionId:'dev'`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/auth.router.ts` — `authConfig()` `devAuth` (L48); `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/identify.ts` — `identify()` fabricated-admin block (L25–44).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* dev-auth fabricates an allow-listed admin so **offline development** works without Google OAuth; it is gated to local mode + loopback + explicit `LFB_DEV_AUTH` opt-in and **never engages in server mode**. *Why it matters:* real access control is **effectively OFF** while this flag is set, so it must **never** be used on a shared or network-exposed machine (charter: allow-listed users only). *Options:* none. *Action button:* "How to disable" → routes to the Authentication section / `CredentialsSetupCard`. Dismissible only as an offer, never silenced permanently.

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix from the web app** — the flag is an environment variable read at boot. Manual next step: **unset `LFB_DEV_AUTH`** and configure real Google creds (§10.10.2), then restart the backend. *Fix in:* manual env var; related enforcement `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/identify.ts` (L26–44). No auto-fix — routes to the Authentication section.

**Notes / gaps.** **gap: not yet wired as a `StatusBanner`.** Security-sensitive per charter. Only ever fires on **localhost**; in server mode `devAuth` is always false, and the bypass additionally requires `securityConfigured()` so a fresh machine still can't skip the first-run gate (§10.10.1).

#### 10.10.8 Allow-list is empty — this would lock everyone out — `warn` (id: allow-list-empty-would-lock-everyone-out)

*Where shown:* `AllowListPage` (Settings → Access) **and** `SecuritySetupPage` — inline amber helper text under the Save button, with the **Save button disabled** while invalid.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `isAllowListValid(value) === false`: **no enabled section has ≥1 valid entry** — i.e. `!(allowCompanies && some domain matches DOMAIN_RE) && !(allowIndividuals && some email matches EMAIL_RE)`. The backend independently mirrors this: `normalizeInput()` throws `SecurityError('empty_allow_list')` (→ 400) when neither `allow_companies` nor `allow_individuals` survives normalization. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/AllowListFields.tsx` — `isAllowListValid()` (L26–32), consumed in `AllowListPage.tsx` (L65, L88–92) and `SecuritySetupPage.tsx` (L52, L71–78); backend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/security/security.service.ts` — `normalizeInput()` (L142–165).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* access is **default-deny** — if no company domain and no individual account is enabled with a valid entry, **nobody (including you) could sign in**. *Why it matters:* saving an empty list would lock you out of your own install. *Options:* the two `AllowListFields` sections — a **company domain** admits any Google account on that domain; an **individual account** admits only exact emails. *Action button:* "Save" (blue, disabled until at least one valid entry). Educate the surprising **CONSUMER_DOMAINS** rule: allow-listing an individual `foo@gmail.com` does **not** widen the OIDC domain pre-filter to `gmail.com` — the domain field stays narrow on purpose.

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix** — the user must type at least one valid domain or email; the disabled Save + amber text guide it. On a valid entry, Save calls `PATCH /api/settings/security` (admin) or `POST /api/security/setup` (first-run). *Fix in:* `PATCH` `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/settings/settings.router.ts` (L115–130, `requireAdmin` → `updateSecurity()`); setup `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/security/security.router.ts` (`POST /setup` L34). No auto-fix — user must enter a valid entry.

**Notes / gaps.** Guard exists on **both** client and server (belt-and-suspenders). The `CONSUMER_DOMAINS` guard (`security.service.ts` L59–78) and `oafAllowedDomains()` (L109–121) are worth surfacing as an educational note so an admin isn't surprised the OIDC domain pre-filter stayed narrow after adding an individual consumer email.

#### 10.10.9 Compression tools aren't installed — compression is unavailable — `warn` (id: optional-compression-tools-missing)

*Where shown:* Tools page → **Tools** section rows for `ffmpeg`/`ffprobe`/`magick` (state `warn`, "✗ missing"); **and** Settings page → **Compression** section amber line.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Tools page: `row.installed === false` for an **optional** row → `state='warn'`. Settings page: `missing = Object.entries(tools).filter(([,v]) => !v)`; render the amber line when `missing.length > 0`. Both read `GET /api/compress/tools`. The `ffprobe` row is satisfied by `ffmpeg` (`installed = ffprobe || ffmpeg`), so one `ffmpeg` install clears both. *Computed in:* Tools page `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` — `buildRows()` (L237–267), `ToolRowView` state (L279); Settings `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` — `CompressionSettingsSection` (L292, L300–304).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* optional CLIs — `ffmpeg`/`ffprobe` for **video** compress plus duration/resolution probing, and **ImageMagick** (`magick`) for **image** compress and PNG→compressible conversion. *Why it matters:* without them the compress/convert offers on media are **disabled**, but the rest of the app works normally. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Copy command" (there is no wired installer for optional tools — `canInstall=false`); the exact line is `brew install ffmpeg imagemagick libheif oxipng webp mozjpeg`. Educate that one `ffmpeg` install satisfies both `ffmpeg` and `ffprobe`.

**(C) The fix.** **No wired auto-install** for optional tools today. The fix copies the exact `brew` command; the rows re-probe on the next `GET /api/compress/tools` fetch. On macOS with Homebrew present this **could** be upgraded to reuse the `POST /api/ipfs/install`-style job. *Fix in:* no backend install endpoint for optional tools — `ToolsPage.tsx` sets `canInstall:false` (L245, L255, L266). No auto-fix — routes to the copied `brew` command + re-probe.

**Notes / gaps.** **gap: optional tools have no one-click installer** (only `ipfs` does — §10.10.5). The Settings amber line and Tools "Copy command" are the current remediation. Charter tie: compression is a core value, so surfacing missing tools directly gates the compress/convert offers described in the charter.

#### 10.10.10 No package manager found — one-click install is unavailable — `warn` (id: package-manager-homebrew-missing)

*Where shown:* Tools page → **Package manager** card (`PackageManagerCard`, state `warn`, right label "not found").

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `node.packageManagerPresent === false` → `state='warn'`. This also **disables** the "Install all required" button (`disabled={installing || !node.packageManagerPresent}`), so it cascades into §10.10.5. `node` comes from `GET /api/ipfs/node`. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` — `PackageManagerCard()` (`found = node.packageManagerPresent`, state at L318, within L315–345); install-button gating (L97).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* a package manager (**Homebrew** on macOS, **winget** on Windows) is what enables one-click installs of `ipfs`/`ffmpeg`/etc.; without one, LFB deliberately will **not** perform the system-level change of installing Homebrew for you. *Why it matters:* every tool must then be installed by hand, and the required-tool one-click install (§10.10.5) is blocked. *Options:* none. *Action button:* macOS → "Copy Homebrew install command" (`/bin/bash -c "$(curl … install.sh)"`); other platforms → explanatory text that no supported manager exists, install tools manually.

**(C) The fix.** **No auto-fix by design** — installing Homebrew is a system-level change LFB refuses to make automatically (charter consent posture). Manual next step: install the package manager, then return to Tools to install the CLIs. *Fix in:* manual — `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/ToolsPage.tsx` — `PackageManagerCard` shows the command (L331–337). No backend endpoint; no auto-fix.

**Notes / gaps.** This warn **cascades**: it also blocks the required-`ipfs` one-click install (button disabled), so on a machine with neither Homebrew nor `ipfs`, fix this one first.

#### 10.10.11 Transcription tools aren't installed (Whisper missing) — `warn` (id: transcription-tools-missing / transcribe-tools-missing)

*Where shown:* the `TranscribeSetupCard` wherever transcription is offered — the **MediaViewer** (`/video`, `/audio`) Transcription analysis column (band 6) when a clip has no transcript, and any other transcription entry point. Not a Settings-page banner but the same "surface + offer + re-check" pattern. *(This merges the two scanned ids `transcription-tools-missing` and `transcribe-tools-missing` — one real condition.)*

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** In MediaViewer: `kind` is `video|audio` **AND** no transcript exists **AND** `api.transcribeTools()` returns `tools && !tools.whisper` → render the setup card. Generally: from `GET /api/transcribe/tools`, `missing = ['whisper','ffmpeg'].filter(k => !tools[k])`. **`whisper` is always required**; `ffmpeg` is needed only to extract audio from **video**; `ffprobe` is a progress-bar nicety satisfied by `ffmpeg` and is **not** its own blocker. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` — `MediaAnalysis` tools query (L431–433), transcription column branch that renders `TranscribeSetupCard` (L501–504); card `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/TranscribeSetupCard.tsx` — `missing`/`commands` (L53–55), `TOOL_INFO` (L36–40), Re-check (L104–113); `CompressTools`/`whisper` contract in `shared/src/types.ts`.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* local transcription runs **entirely on this machine** via OpenAI **Whisper** — **nothing is uploaded** and no API key or Google Cloud credential is needed; it just needs two free CLIs. *Why it matters:* until Whisper is on PATH the "Generate transcript" action is unavailable; but this is an **amber offer, not a red alarm** — no data is at risk. *Options:* per-tool rows (`whisper`, `ffmpeg`, `ffprobe`) showing "● installed" / "✗ missing". *Action button:* "Copy command" (e.g. `pipx install openai-whisper`, `brew install ffmpeg`; `whisper` needs `pipx`, install via `brew install pipx`) plus a **"Re-check"** button.

**(C) The fix.** **No wired installer** (installing system tools is out of scope). The fix shows copy-paste install commands, then **Re-check** re-queries `GET /api/transcribe/tools` and re-enables the run **without a page reload**; once `whisper` resolves the "Generate transcript" button appears. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/entity/MediaViewer.tsx` — `onRecheck` → `refetchTools()` (L504); card `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/components/TranscribeSetupCard.tsx` — `onRecheck` → `GET /api/transcribe/tools`. No auto-install — surface + re-check.

**Notes / gaps.** Same "manual-tools" pattern as the compression probes (§10.10.9), and analogous to `CredentialsSetupCard` (§10.10.2) but needs **no secrets** — a good reassurance point given the charter's local-only, no-phone-home posture (transcription stays on the machine, like the perceptual-hash rule).

#### 10.10.12 Background sync is off / not installed — `warn` (id: background-sync-off-or-autostart-not-installed) — cross-ref §10.9

*Where shown:* **GAP for the Settings surface** — the Settings page does **not** surface background-sync/autostart state at all. The install/enable/disable controls live only on the **Sync page**, which is owned by **§10.9**; this entry documents the Settings-partition gap and cross-references there.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Would read `syncPageData()`: the sync/scan worker's **`installed`** (launchd plist present) and **`enabled`** (on/off) flags, plus `watcher.enabled`. Per charter, the plist must be **installed** for the background process to exist, and **on/off** is a separate, independent choice — both facts must be shown. Not computed anywhere in the settings/security/auth partition today. *Computed in:* cross-partition source `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` — `GET /` (L12–20) → `schedule.service` `syncPageData()`. See **§10.9** for the full detection detail.

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* LFB runs a **launchd background job every 15 minutes** to sync large files over IPFS; there are **two independent facts** — whether the plist is **INSTALLED** (the job exists) and whether it is currently **ON/OFF**. *Why it matters:* with it off or uninstalled, your **other computers won't receive updates automatically** — you'd have to sync by hand. *Options:* none / one-click. *Action button:* "Install background sync" and/or "Turn on".

**(C) The fix.** The endpoints already exist: `POST /api/sync/sync/install` (install the launchd plist), `POST /api/sync/sync/enable` (turn it on), and `POST /api/sync/watcher/enable` (the live filesystem watcher). The only Settings-partition gap is that no banner/verdict surfaces the state here. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/sync/sync.router.ts` — `POST /:worker/:action` (L39–54), `POST /watcher/:action` (L26–36). Full lifecycle in **§10.9**.

**Notes / gaps.** **gap: not wired into Settings** — recommend a Settings "Background sync" `Section` mirroring the Authentication/IPFS pattern so the charter requirement ("expose whether the 15-min launchd sync is installed and on/off") is met on the Settings surface too. The implementation and primary catalog entry are **§10.9**.

#### 10.10.13 Restart the backend to finish enabling the new company domain — `warn` (id: allowlist-save-restart-recommended)

*Where shown:* `AllowListPage` / `SecuritySetupPage` — a **success toast only**, conditional on `r.restartRecommended`. No persistent banner.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** Fires when the save response `r.restartRecommended === true`. **NOTE — effectively dead:** the backend **now always returns `restartRecommended:false`** because it hot-swaps the OIDC pre-filter via `rebuildAuthFrontend()`, so this branch is retained in the contract but never true in practice. *Computed in:* frontend `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/pages/settings/AllowListPage.tsx` — `save.onSuccess` (L50–58) and `SecuritySetupPage.tsx` (L37–42); backend (always false) `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/settings/settings.router.ts` — `PATCH /security` (L122–123), `security.service.ts` — `updateSecurity()` / `completeSetup()` return `restartRecommended:false` (L183 / L187–198).

**(B) The popup.** *What this is:* historically, a newly added company domain needed a **backend restart** before OIDC would accept it. *Why it matters:* now the app **hot-swaps the auth middleware**, so **no restart is needed** — the popup should **reassure** that the change takes effect on the next sign-in immediately. *Options:* none. *Action button:* "Restart backend" only in the (now unreachable) true case; otherwise there is no action.

**(C) The fix.** **No action needed** — the allow-list edit is already live via `rebuildAuthFrontend()`. If `restartRecommended` ever returns true again, the fix would restart the backend. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/auth-frontend.ts` — `rebuildAuthFrontend()` (L163–166), invoked at `settings.router.ts` L122 and `security.router.ts` L43. No action — change is already live.

**Notes / gaps.** **Dead-but-wired:** `restartRecommended` is retained in the contract but **always false**. Flag as **stale UI** to remove or repurpose — the "Access saved" plain toast is the real path.

#### 10.10.14 Signed out — session expired (silent re-login) — `neutral` (id: auth-relogin-401)

*Where shown:* **No banner** — handled invisibly in the axios interceptor; a hard failure redirects to the Google sign-in screen.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** On **HTTP 401** from any `/api` call, when a `reloadSession` is registered and the request hasn't already been retried (`!config.__retried`), the interceptor re-hydrates the OpenAuthFederated token **once** and retries; if it still fails the request rejects and the app falls back to the sign-in redirect. (A 403 instead shows a toast "You don't have permission to do that.") Per MEMORY (`auth-relogin-is-client-side`), backend session persistence is **verified correct** — re-login is caused by **reactive token refresh + drifting dev cookie origin + possibly a stale build**, NOT lost server state. *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/api/axios.ts` — response interceptor (L29–44), `reloadSession` retry (L32–41); `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/api/authCore.ts` — re-hydrate (L22–27); backend gate `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/auth/identify.ts` — `requireAllowListed`.

**(B) The popup.** Deliberately **not surfaced** (neutral). If ever shown: *What this is:* your login token expired and LFB silently refreshed it; if you were fully signed out you'll be sent to Google sign-in. *Why it matters:* **no data or sync state is lost on the server** (persistence is verified correct) — the OS background worker keeps syncing even while you're logged out of the web UI. *Options / Action button:* none.

**(C) The fix.** **Automatic:** `reloadSession()` re-mints the token and retries the request. **Hard failure:** redirect to Google sign-in (`openSignIn` → `/sso-callback`). No server-side fix. Manual: hard-refresh if a stale build is causing a loop. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/frontend/src/api/authCore.ts` — `openSignIn` (L29–40); `axios.ts` `reloadSession` retry (L32–41).

**Notes / gaps.** Deliberately **silent (neutral)** — a banner on every token refresh would be noise. **Escalate to a visible banner only if re-login LOOPS** (repeated 401s in a short window), which indicates the stale-build / origin-drift cause from MEMORY. Note the overlap with §10.10.3: a genuine "not allow-listed" 401 also lands here — the two should be disambiguated so an allow-list rejection doesn't masquerade as an expired session.

#### 10.10.15 Client error reporting is being rate-limited — `neutral` (id: clientlog-rate-limited)

*Where shown:* **No user banner** — an internal anti-abuse safeguard; the browser simply receives a 429.

**(A) Detect it & all conditions.** `POST /api/clientlog` returns `429 { ok:false, code:'rate_limited' }` once a principal exceeds **60 POSTs / 60s**, keyed by `sessionId || email || ip` on a fixed 60-second window. Additionally, a batch of **>50 events** has the extras **dropped** (returned as `{ received, dropped }`). *Computed in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/clientlog/clientlog.router.ts` — `rateLimited()` (L30–39), `MAX_EVENTS` cap (L54), 429 branch (L47–49).

**(B) The popup.** **Not user-facing.** If ever surfaced to a **developer**: a client is flooding `error.err` — likely a frontend error loop (a component erroring on every render, or a 401 re-login loop per §10.10.14). The interesting signal is **why** the browser is emitting so many errors, not the throttle itself. *Options / Action button:* none.

**(C) The fix.** **No user fix.** Developer next step: inspect `error.err` for the repeated `client:*` context to find the looping component/effect and fix the source of the flood. *Fix in:* `~/BGit/Bryan_git/LargeFileBridge/code/packages/backend/src/modules/clientlog/clientlog.router.ts` (guard only — no remediation endpoint). No auto-fix — routes to developer inspection of `~/T/_large_files_bridge/error.err`.

**Notes / gaps.** Flagged for completeness — **not a candidate for the amber/red verdict banner**; it's a flood guard on the shared fault trail (charter: logs live in the state root, never `/tmp`). Its **firing is a proxy** for a frontend error loop worth developer attention, and it pairs with §10.10.14 (a re-login loop is a common cause).
